## Push: DXGI_FORMAT spec-diff audit (4 latent bugs), D3D12 const consolidation (2026-04-18 UTC)

Extended the programmatic-diff audit to DXGI texture formats and more D3D12 enum families. Registered the canonical `dxgiformat.h` from the Chromium directx-headers tree as a new spec-diff header and added four new targets to `config/spec-diff-targets.json`: `dxgi_format` (64 fields covering `runtime/zig/src/backend/d3d12/d3d12_formats.zig`, excluding the Doe-internal alias `DXGI_FORMAT_D24_X8_STENCIL8`), `d3d12_input_classification` (2 fields), `d3d12_command_list_type` (4 fields), and `d3d12_descriptor_heap_type` / `d3d12_descriptor_range_type` / `d3d12_resource_dimension` remain from the earlier push.

Found **4 more latent bugs** in hand-transcribed DXGI_FORMAT values, all two swapped pairs:

- `DXGI_FORMAT_R16_UINT`: 58 тЖТ **57** (was encoding R16_SNORM)
- `DXGI_FORMAT_R16_SNORM`: 57 тЖТ **58** (was encoding R16_UINT)
- `DXGI_FORMAT_R8_UINT`: 63 тЖТ **62** (was encoding R8_SNORM)
- `DXGI_FORMAT_R8_SNORM`: 62 тЖТ **63** (was encoding R8_UINT)

Any render or vertex-input path that binds an R8Snorm or R16Snorm surface would have produced the wrong DXGI format тАФ R8Snorm became R8_UINT, R8Uint became R8_SNORM, etc. Latent for the compute-only cohort but visible as validation errors on any texture/vertex path. The test fixture `runtime/zig/tests/backend/d3d12_descriptors_formats_test.zig` that previously codified the wrong values was corrected to the canonical mapping.

Consolidation pass: duplicated D3D12 consts in `resources/d3d12_depth_stencil.zig` (4 DXGI format consts), `commands/d3d12_copy.zig` (2 RESOURCE_STATE consts), and `commands/d3d12_render.zig` (2 INPUT_CLASSIFICATION consts) now re-export from `d3d12_constants.zig` / `d3d12_formats.zig` so the spec-diff parser has a single source of truth.

**Session running audit total: 34 latent bugs** (17 SPIR-V spec + 7 Vulkan constants + 2 D3D12 resource-state + 4 D3D12 SRV dimension + 4 DXGI format).

Validation: `python3 bench/gates/spec_diff_gate.py` тЖТ PASS (all 30 targets); `python3 bench/gates/schema_gate.py` тЖТ PASS; `zig build test` тЖТ PASS; `zig build test-wgsl` тЖТ PASS.

## Push: ORT EP session-smoke cases land Softmax + LayerNormalization end-to-end (2026-04-18 UTC)

Extends `runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/src/doe_ort_ep_session_smoke.cc` with two new session-smoke cases that exercise the attention-shape ops added in the earlier ORT EP breadth push: `softmax` (rank-2 float32 along axis=-1, opset 13) and `layernorm` (rank-2 float32 with a 1-D scale, opset 17, axis=-1, epsilon=1e-5, no bias). Each case builds an in-memory ONNX model via the Model Editor API (`CreateUnaryModelAtOpset` for Softmax and a dedicated `CreateLayerNormModel` helper for the two-input form), runs the session through the Doe EP, and validates the output against a CPU reference baked into `BuildSmokeCases`. Both cases pass with `outputsMatch=true` and `routedThroughDoe=true`; the regenerated artifact is at `runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/artifacts/20260418T170000Z/doe-ort-ep-session-smoke.json` with 14/14 cases successful and session-level `success: true`.

The `--case` selector now accepts `softmax`, `layernorm`, `concat` (plus the previously undocumented `sigmoid`, `tanh`, `gelu`), and the help string was updated to list them. `SmokeModelKind` gained `kSoftmax`, `kLayerNorm`, and `kConcat` along with the supporting name/input-count/claim-count/input-names switches.

**Concat blocker (deferred).** The Concat case is claimed and executed end-to-end by the Doe EP, but its session-smoke model build needs an integer `axis` attribute passed through `api->CreateOpAttr` to `model_editor_api->CreateNode`. Invoking that combo segfaults inside `libonnx.so.1` on `ReleaseOpAttr` despite the public header docs stating "OrtOpAttr instances are copied" тАФ ownership semantics between `CreateOpAttr` and `CreateNode` still need to be pinned down. The smoke runner therefore keeps all Concat plumbing (enum entry, switch cases, `CreateBinaryConcatModel` helper) but omits the Concat `SmokeCaseSpec` from `BuildSmokeCases` so the full smoke suite runs clean. Follow-up: test the pattern against a pinned ORT 1.24/1.25 or look at how Chromium's WebNN ORT path drives the same combo, then re-enable the Concat case.

Validation: `zig build ort-plugin-ep ort-plugin-ep-session-smoke` тЖТ PASS; `doe-ort-ep-session-smoke --case all` тЖТ 14 cases successful, top-level `success: true`; `zig build test` тЖТ PASS; `zig build test-wgsl` тЖТ PASS.

## Push: loop-only `vectorData[col]` proof contract closes sixth matvec clamp (2026-04-18 UTC)

Closes the last of the six matvec clamps named in the earlier matcher push. New Lean theorem `loop_index_affine_inbounds_when_loop_fits_tight` in `pipeline/lean/Doe/Shader/ComputeBounds.lean` proves `i * loop_stride + offset < array_length` given `i < limit` and the tight precondition `(limit - 1) * loop_stride + offset + 1 тЙд array_length`. Matching matcher contract `loop_affine_matcher_contract_sound_tight` in `pipeline/lean/Doe/Shader/BoundsElisionMatcher.lean` with inductive `MatchesLoopAffine expr loop_stride offset` for the pattern `(.add (.mul .loopIndex (.lit loop_stride)) (.lit offset))`. Both theorems registered in `pipeline/lean/Doe/Extract.lean` (theorems list + bounds-elimination manifest) and picked up by the regenerated `pipeline/lean/artifacts/proven-conditions.json`.

Zig wiring: new `BoundsPattern.loop_1d_storage_buffer_affine` in `runtime/zig/src/lean_proof.zig`, gated on the tight contract string. New `DispatchPreconditionKind.loop_component` in `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/ir.zig`. `runtime/zig/src/dispatch_preconditions.zig` gains a `.loop_component` branch that computes `((loop_limit - 1) * loop_limit_multiplier + element_offset + 1) * element_stride_bytes` тАФ dispatch-geometry independent тАФ with an empty-loop short-circuit returning 0 bytes. `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/dispatch_proof_match.zig` gains `match_loop_only_affine_plus_offset` (reuses the existing `collect_additive_loop_terms` but requires `gid_multiplier == 0`) and a new `try_elide_storage_index` branch that ties it to `loop_match.find_bounded_loop_limit`. Three variant-count tests updated to expect 5 instead of 4 `DispatchPreconditionKind`s and the new `BoundsPattern` entry in the stability table.

End-to-end verification: running the rebuilt `zig-out/bin/doe-emit-spirv --shader-path bench/kernels/matrix_vector_mul_32768x2048_f32_naive_swizzle0.wgsl` under `-Dlean-verified=true` yields a 2548-byte SPIR-V with zero `OpArrayLength` / `OpExtInst UMin` sites (previously 2640 bytes with two clamp ops on `vectorData[col]`). `spirv-val` accepts the output. The checked-in `bench/kernels/*.spv` was intentionally NOT regenerated тАФ the existing AMD Vulkan release receipt at `bench/out/amd-vulkan/20260418T193328Z/` remains the source of truth, and the 6-of-6 elision lands on the next AMD rerun.

Validation: `bash pipeline/lean/check.sh` тЖТ `lean-check: ok`; `bash pipeline/lean/extract.sh` тЖТ artifact written; `python3 pipeline/lean/test_proof_pipeline.py` тЖТ 49/49 PASS; `zig build test` тЖТ PASS; `zig build test-wgsl` тЖТ PASS; `zig build test -Dlean-verified=true` тЖТ PASS; `zig build test-wgsl -Dlean-verified=true` тЖТ PASS; `spirv-val /tmp/matvec_proven.spv` тЖТ PASS.

by the actual emitted bytes, and `shader_artifact_gate.py` verifies three links:
trace-meta manifest hash equals the manifest `hash`, manifest `spirvSha256`
equals the SPIR-V file bytes, and the SPIR-V stage `artifactSha256` equals the
same bytes.

requirements still report `kernel_dispatch`, while shader artifact manifests

identity.

`bench/kernels/` with the lean-verified `doe-emit-spirv` tool. This mattered
because the Vulkan runtime prefers sibling `.spv` files when present; without
regeneration the governed lane could load stale pre-proof SPIR-V even from a
lean-verified runtime build.

`bench/out/amd-vulkan/20260418T200210Z/dawn-vs-doe.amd.vulkan.release.json`,
with release claim sidecar at
`bench/out/amd-vulkan/20260418T200210Z/dawn-vs-doe.amd.vulkan.release.claim.json`.
The report is comparable and the blocking gates pass. The claim sidecar remains
diagnostic; see the sidecar for the non-claimable rows and percentile reasons.
The matvec shader receipt in this run points to a proof-backed SPIR-V artifact
whose disassembly has the matrix/output clamps removed and only the
`vectorData[col]` runtime-sized load clamp remaining.

## Push: browser ORT WebGPU third sentiment shape (2026-04-18 UTC)

Added a medium-length DistilBERT sentiment shape (`sentiment_medium`) to the repo-only browser ORT WebGPU compare surface, between the existing short and longform shapes. Extended the Playwright bench script `browser/chromium/scripts/webgpu-playwright-ort-bench.mjs` `TASKS` object with the new task, added a matching vendor-browser command JSON at `bench/vendor-browser/ort_browser_sentiment_medium_commands.json`, added the workload entry to `bench/workloads/workloads.browser.ort-webgpu-compare.json`, and added the id to the selector in `bench/native-compare/compare.config.browser.ort-webgpu.json`. Schema gate and spec-diff gate still pass.

This is a mechanical breadth add, not the ambitious Gemma 270M or full Transformers.js LLM shape originally proposed. Those remain out-of-scope for a single-session push because they require:

- Vendoring the `onnx-community/gemma-3-270m-it-ONNX` model + tokenizer into the jetstream Transformers.js tree (same pattern as the existing Xenova DistilBERT and Whisper entries).
- Refactoring the Playwright `runTask` closure so it is not hard-coded to a classification-shape output (logits тЖТ argmax тЖТ `["NEGATIVE","POSITIVE"]` labels). An LLM path needs either prefill-only shape (single forward pass, accept hidden-state outputs) or a full prefill+decode generation loop with token sampling.
- Parameterizing output validation per task type so non-classification tasks do not fail the existing expected-labels check.

The Whisper encoder is already vendored at `browser/chromium/src/third_party/jetstream/main/transformersjs/build/models/Xenova/whisper-tiny.en/` and is the lowest-friction next Transformers.js family to add (encoder-only is still a single forward pass), after the runTask refactor.

Browser compare artifact regeneration requires running the Playwright harness on this Linux host with a working Chromium + Dawn/Doe pair; that rerun is follow-up rather than part of this push.

## Push: ORT EP attention-shape op breadth (Softmax, LayerNorm, Concat) (2026-04-18 UTC)

Extended the repo-only ONNX Runtime plugin EP to claim, compile, and execute three new same-shape float32 ops beyond the existing Identity/Add/Relu/Sigmoid/Tanh/Gelu/MatMul/Gemm cohort:

- **Softmax** (opset 13+): unary, last-axis reduction with the standard numerically-stable subtract-max formulation. Claim requires `SameTypeAndShape(input, output)`.
- **LayerNormalization** (opset 17): binary (`input`, `scale`), last-axis normalization with `epsilon=1e-5` and no bias slice in this pass. Claim requires the scale input to be 1-D and match `input.dims.back()`.
- **Concat** (opset 13+): binary, axis attribute read via `ReadOptionalIntAttribute` at claim time; validation rejects any pair whose non-axis dims disagree or whose axis is out of range. Kernel recovers the axis at compute time from the input-shape difference.

Bumped the EP compatibility-info version from `doe-ort-basic-ops-ep-v6` to `v7` to reflect the schema change.

Session-smoke counter serialization extended: `claimed_softmax_nodes`, `claimed_layernorm_nodes`, `claimed_concat_nodes` and the matching `compiled_*_groups` / `compute_*_calls` counters are now written into `runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/artifacts/{timestamp}/doe-ort-ep-session-smoke.json`. Existing session-smoke cases (Add/Relu/MatMul/fusions) remain green тАФ fresh artifact captured at `runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/artifacts/20260418T160000Z/doe-ort-ep-session-smoke.json`.

Reshape was explicitly excluded from this pass: its INT64 shape tensor cannot traverse the EP's existing float32-only `DescribeSupportedTensorValue` path, and routing a second type through that helper is a separate refactor worth staging independently. RMSNormalization deferred for the same reason we defer scale-and-bias LayerNorm bias support: scoping.

Follow-up scope on the next iteration: (1) session-smoke test cases that build in-memory ONNX models with Softmax/LayerNormalization/Concat nodes using the OrtModel / OrtNode editor APIs, (2) matching bench/vendor-native command JSONs and `workloads.native.ort-doe-ep-smoke.json` entries, (3) adding the LayerNormalization bias input (ternary form) and Reshape once `DescribeSupportedTensorValue` accepts a caller-supplied accepted-type list.

Validation: `zig build ort-plugin-ep` тЖТ PASS, `zig build ort-plugin-ep-session-smoke` тЖТ PASS, existing session smoke with `--case all` тЖТ PASS (all operations green, selected EP `DoeExecutionProvider`, 3 discovered devices), `zig build test` тЖТ PASS, `zig build test-wgsl` тЖТ PASS.

## Push: D3D12 SRV_DIMENSION audit (4 latent bugs), spec-diff parser extension (2026-04-18 UTC)

Extended the programmatic-diff audit pattern to D3D12 view-dimension, descriptor-heap, and descriptor-range constants. Found 4 latent bugs in hand-transcribed `D3D12_SRV_DIMENSION` values at `runtime/zig/src/backend/d3d12/resources/d3d12_texture_view.zig` lines 60-65:

- `SRV_DIMENSION_TEXTURE1D`: 3 тЖТ **2** (was encoding TEXTURE1DARRAY)
- `SRV_DIMENSION_TEXTURE3D`: 7 тЖТ **8** (was encoding TEXTURE2DMSARRAY)
- `SRV_DIMENSION_TEXTURECUBE`: 8 тЖТ **9** (was encoding TEXTURE3D)
- `SRV_DIMENSION_TEXTURECUBEARRAY`: 9 тЖТ **10** (was encoding TEXTURECUBE)

Every SRV create call through `map_view_dimension_to_srv` for a 1D, 3D, cube, or cube-array texture wrote the wrong `ViewDimension` into the `D3D12_SHADER_RESOURCE_VIEW_DESC`. Latent for the compute-only cohort that doesn't exercise SRVs today, but would have surfaced on any render/texture workload reaching this path.

Centralized `SRV_DIMENSION_*`, `DESCRIPTOR_HEAP_TYPE_*`, `DESCRIPTOR_RANGE_TYPE_*`, and `RESOURCE_DIMENSION_*` constants in `runtime/zig/src/backend/d3d12/d3d12_constants.zig` so they are governable. Updated `d3d12_texture_view.zig`, `d3d12_descriptors.zig`, and `d3d12_runtime_compute.zig` to import from the central file, removing three duplicated local copies of descriptor heap/range constants.

Extended `bench/gates/spec_diff_gate.py` to resolve `NAME = ( OTHER + N )` enum-arithmetic canonical definitions in a second pass after literal values are collected. DirectX headers use this form for most enum continuations (e.g. `D3D12_DESCRIPTOR_RANGE_TYPE_UAV = ( D3D12_DESCRIPTOR_RANGE_TYPE_SRV + 1 )`), so without this the gate could only audit the first literal of each enum family. Iterates to fixed point so chained references resolve.

Registered four new spec-diff targets in `config/spec-diff-targets.json`: `d3d12_srv_dimension` (11 fields), `d3d12_descriptor_heap_type` (4 fields), `d3d12_descriptor_range_type` (4 fields), and `d3d12_resource_dimension` (5 fields). All pass against the in-tree Chromium directx-headers copy at `browser/chromium/src/third_party/dawn/third_party/directx-headers/src/include/directx/d3d12.h`.

**Session running audit total: 30 latent bugs** (17 SPIR-V spec + 7 Vulkan constants + 2 D3D12 resource-state + 4 D3D12 SRV dimension).

Validation: `python3 bench/gates/spec_diff_gate.py` тЖТ PASS (all 26 targets); `python3 bench/gates/schema_gate.py` тЖТ PASS; `zig build test` тЖТ PASS; `zig build test-wgsl` тЖТ PASS.

## Push: Vulkan matvec proof matcher closes hot-loop clamp gap (2026-04-18 UTC)

The Vulkan lane now structurally closes the remaining proof-integration gap in
`compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32_naive_swizzle0`: the bounds-elision matcher
recognizes matvec-style guarded loops whose trip count is a const global and
whose loop increment is the final body statement, and normalizes scaled affine
terms such as `((4 * rowBy4 + 2) * kPackedCols) + col` into the existing
gid-plus-loop-affine proof contract.

Baseline `-Dlean-verified=false` emission for the governed matvec shader was
2980 bytes with `minCount=6`, `dispatchPreconditions=0`, and six
`OpArrayLength` / `UMin` clamp sites in the disassembly. After the matcher fix,
`-Dlean-verified=true` emission is 2640 bytes with `minCount=1` and
`dispatchPreconditions=5`. The four hot-loop `matrixData[...]` clamps and the
final `outData[rowBy4]` clamp are removed; the only remaining clamp is the
`vectorData[col]` runtime-sized load, which needs a separate loop-only storage
buffer proof contract before it can be safely elided.

No AMD Vulkan timing claim is made from this shell. Strict AMD Vulkan preflight
is blocked here because `/dev/dri/renderD128` is unavailable, the user is not in
the `render` group, Dawn only exposes SwiftShader/CPU, and Doe selects
llvmpipe/non-AMD. The evidence from this pass is SPIR-V structure plus
validation, not a comparable governed benchmark row.

Validation: `spirv-val` passed on the proof-backed matvec SPIR-V;
`zig build test-wgsl -Dlean-verified=true`, `zig build test-wgsl`,
`zig build test -Dlean-verified=true`, `zig build test`, and
`zig build -Doptimize=ReleaseFast -Dlean-verified=true` passed under
`runtime/zig`.

## Push: CSL operation graph contract and v1.4 parser fix validation (2026-04-18 UTC)

Added `config/csl-operation-graph.schema.json` as the additive receipt shape
for CSL host/device orchestration. The schema is discriminated by
`orchestrationMode`: `memcpy` for direct `cslc` plus `SdkRuntime.memcpy_*` /
`launch` flows, and `sdklayout` for Python `SdkLayout` code regions, ports,
connections, streams, and async `send` / `receive` flows. This keeps Gemma 4
E2B on the direct memcpy ladder while reserving a schema-backed path for 31B
streaming.

Registered two SDK-grounded memcpy samples:
`examples/csl-operation-graph.gelu-rpc-launch.sample.json` for the
`rpc_launch` path and `examples/csl-operation-graph.gemv-streaming.sample.json`
for the `streaming_memcpy_driven` path. The streaming graph targets memcpy
colors rather than exported device symbols for streamed tensors, mirroring
GEMV 9 / checkerboard. Tiny local CSL source fixtures live under
`examples/csl/` so source-level unblock checks are gateable without depending
on external docs pages.

`executionPattern` is now the memcpy-mode discriminator, and
`reservedResources` ships as optional day-one metadata for colors, queues,
task IDs, and memcpy channels. Added `bench/gates/csl_operation_graph_gate.py`
and wired it into `bench/runners/run_blocking_gates.py` after the schema and
fixture mirror gates. The gate checks exported-symbol or memcpy-color
references, memcpy ROI bounds against the declared PE grid, pattern-specific
presence of launch or streaming memcpy-color operations, required
`sys_mod.unblock_cmd_stream()` completion for RPC-launch memcpy functions, and
SdkLayout stream/port/region referential integrity. Updated
`docs/csl-architecture.md`, `docs/process.md`, and `bench/README.md` to make
the operation graph contract a named source of truth.

The CSL v1.4 parser fix was also applied to the checked-in Gemma 3 270M
manifest smoke compile fixture so the governed lane no longer feeds
`[chunk_size][4]f32` declarations to `cslc`. The source emitter already emits
`[chunk_size * 4]f32` for vector-backed runtime storage buffers and scalar
`[*]f32` exported pointers; the simulator fixture now matches that declaration
shape.

The governed 270M lane was rerun without a configured SDK compiler. It failed
closed as expected: host-plan parity matched, compile status was `blocked` with
reason `compiler_unavailable`, run status was `blocked` with reason
`compile_not_ready`, and the materialized `/tmp/compile/gemv/pe_program.csl`
contained only the flattened storage declarations. A real SDK v1.4 retry still
requires `DOE_CSLC_EXECUTABLE` or `--cslc-executable`.

## Push: SPIR-V artifact persistence, Dawn preflight fix, matvec bounds-elision Lean tightening (2026-04-18 UTC)

Three targeted changes aimed at unblocking the release pipeline and the one remaining AMD Vulkan regression.

**(1) Real SPIR-V artifact persistence behind `shader_artifact_gate.py --require-spirv-validation`.** Extended `runtime/zig/src/backend/common/shader_artifact_manifest.zig` with `StageArtifact` + `emit_shader_artifact_manifest_for_signature_with_artifacts`: the emitter now writes a sibling `.spv` file next to each manifest when the backend has the compiled SPIR-V bytes and records the file path in the `ir_to_spirv` stage record. Plumbed through the Vulkan backend (`runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/native_runtime.zig` stores `pending_spirv_bytes_owned`, `vk_pipeline.zig` captures words after `vkCreateShaderModule`, `mod.zig` exposes `pending_spirv_bytes_view` / `release_pending_spirv_bytes` methods on `ZigVulkanBackend` so the shared emitter can `@hasDecl`-gate the feature). Smoke: a fresh `doe-zig-runtime --execute --trace-meta /tmp/m.json` run emits `bench/out/shader-artifacts/vulkan_shader_artifact_2.json` with `ir_to_spirv.artifactPath=vulkan_shader_artifact_2.spv` plus a sibling 228-byte `.spv`; `spirv-val` accepts the binary (exit 0). Manifest still validates against `config/shader-artifact.schema.json` (artifactPath was already optional in the stage record).

**(2) Dawn sidecar preflight library-name drift fixed.** `bench/runners/preflight_bench_host.py` was looking for `bench/vendor/dawn/out/Release/libwebgpu.so` and `libwgpu_native.so`. Current vendored Dawn output is `libwebgpu_dawn.so` (the Zig runtime's dlopen loader at `runtime/zig/src/core/abi/wgpu_loader.zig` tries that first Dawn candidate) and `libwgpu_native.so` was a wgpu-native alternative-impl check unrelated to the Dawn-vs-Doe path. Preflight updated to check `libwebgpuDawn` only; `run_release_pipeline.py --dry-run` now plans cleanly through preflight тЖТ compare тЖТ gates, and `preflight_bench_host.py --strict-amd-vulkan` reports 10/10 ok including the Dawn adapter identity probe.

**(3) Matvec regression: tight-precondition Lean theorem landed.** Spirv-dis of the current `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32_naive_swizzle0` SPIR-V shows the inner loop still carries 4├Ч `OpArrayLength` + `OpExtInst UMin` robustness clamps per iteration (one per unrolled matrix row). Those access patterns match `MatchesGidLoopAffine` but the current Lean theorem `gid_affine_plus_scaled_loop_index_inbounds_when_dispatch_fits` uses the over-approximate precondition `total * gid_stride + limit * loop_stride + offset тЙд array_length`, which for the matvec shape (total=8192, gid_stride=2048, limit=512, loop_stride=1) computes `16,777,728` тАФ exceeds the exactly-packed 256 MB / 16,777,216-vec4f buffer by `gid_stride + loop_stride - 1 = 2048` elements. Elision therefore does not fire and RADV still schedules around the clamps.

Proven a tight-precondition variant `gid_affine_plus_scaled_loop_index_inbounds_when_dispatch_fits_tight` (and its matcher contract `gid_loop_affine_matcher_contract_sound_tight`) that uses `(total - 1) * gid_stride + (limit - 1) * loop_stride + offset + 1 тЙд array_length` тАФ the strict supremum of the indexed range plus one. For matvec this evaluates to `16,775,680 тЙд 16,777,216` тЬУ, unlocking elision. Both theorems added to `Doe/Extract.lean` and regenerated into `pipeline/lean/artifacts/proven-conditions.json`; `bash pipeline/lean/check.sh` тЖТ `lean-check: ok`; `python3 pipeline/lean/test_proof_pipeline.py` тЖТ 49/49 pass.

Wired Zig to the tight variant: `lean_proof.boundsProven(.gid_1d_storage_buffer_loop_affine)` now gates on `gid_loop_affine_matcher_contract_sound_tight`, and `dispatch_preconditions.required_buffer_bytes` for `.gid_component` kinds computes the tight formula (with an empty-dispatch short-circuit returning 0 bytes). Updated the 8 Zig preconditions tests to the tight expected values; both `zig build test` and `zig build test-wgsl` (and their `-Dlean-verified=true` variants) pass.

Does not include a fresh matvec benchmark тАФ that requires a bench run on the AMD Vulkan host and is not part of this change. Expected impact: the 4├Ч inner-loop UMin clamps become no-ops at SPV generation time in the `-Dlean-verified=true` build, removing ~4├Ч `OpExtInst UMin` + 4├Ч `OpArrayLength` + 4├Ч `OpISub` per inner iteration ├Ч 512 iterations ├Ч 8192 rows from the hot path.

Validation: `python3 bench/gates/schema_gate.py` тЖТ PASS; `python3 bench/gates/spec_diff_gate.py` тЖТ PASS; `python3 pipeline/lean/test_proof_pipeline.py` тЖТ 49/49 PASS; `zig build test` + `zig build test-wgsl` (both with and without `-Dlean-verified=true`) тЖТ PASS; `python3 bench/runners/preflight_bench_host.py --strict-amd-vulkan` тЖТ 10/10 ok.

## Push: spec-diff CI gate + render-lane option (b) audit (2026-04-18 UTC)

**Spec-diff gate landed.** New `bench/gates/spec_diff_gate.py` drives the programmatic-diff pattern from the earlier spec-audit passes as a blocking gate. Targets are declared in `config/spec-diff-targets.json` (validated by `config/spec-diff-targets.schema.json` and registered in `config/schema-targets.json`). The gate parses canonical identifiers from the in-tree chromium-sysroot headers (`browser/chromium/src/third_party/spirv-headers/src/include/spirv/unified1/spirv.h`, `vulkan-headers/.../vulkan_core.h`, `dawn/third_party/directx-headers/src/include/directx/d3d12.h`) and diffs their numeric values against the named Zig constants under matched namespaces in `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/spirv_spec.zig`, `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_constants.zig`, and `runtime/zig/src/backend/d3d12/d3d12_constants.zig`. Added to `docs/process.md` as a blocking gate alongside the schema hard gate.

First-run found one new latent bug (audit total: 27):

- `ImageOperandsMask.Offset`: 0x4 тЖТ **0x10**
- `ImageOperandsMask.Grad`: 0x8 тЖТ **0x4**
- `ImageOperandsMask.ConstOffset`: 0x10 тЖТ **0x8**

Three-way permutation in `spirv_spec.zig`. Callers live in `emit_spirv_texture.zig` (OpImageSampleExplicitLod / OpImageSampleDrefExplicitLod / OpImageFetch with explicit gradients, const offsets, or runtime offsets). Latent in the compute-only cohort тАФ storage-image paths do not emit these operands тАФ but any texture-sampling shader using those operand modes would have written the wrong operand bitset into the generated SPIR-V word. Fixed to canonical values; `zig build test` + `zig build test-wgsl` green.

**Render-lane option (b) audit.** The prior session's wrap-up flagged "~10 `implementation_gap` rows with 'timing sources differ between sides'" as mechanically fixable by per-row timing-source alignment. Current-state audit across every catalog under `bench/workloads/` finds exactly 4 such rows (all in `workloads.amd.vulkan.json`), and none are pure timing-source issues:

- `render_pixel_local_storage_barrier`, `render_pixel_local_storage_barrier_500`: Dawn reports `dispatch counts differ for row/success=(1, 1): [1] vs [0]` тАФ Dawn delegate does not execute the workload. Option (a) class, not option (b).
- `render_draw_indexed_200k`, `render_draw_redundant_pipeline_bindings_200k`: `baseline execution unsuccessful on some samples`, `baseline execution reported errors`, `row/success shape sets differ`, `execution shape (dispatch/row/success counts) differs`. Dawn partially-fails; the gap is not timing-instrument skew.

Conclusion: option (b) is not actionable against the current catalog. The addressable render rows (DrawCallPerf DynamicBindGroup_RenderBundle / DynamicPipeline_DynamicBindGroup_RenderBundle variants) were already promoted to `comparable` in commit 45cabfade. No workload edits were made in this pass тАФ forcing timing alignment on rows with execution-shape mismatch or Dawn-side partial failure would mask real comparability failures and violate the structural-work-equivalence discipline.

**Lean matcher contracts.** The wrap-up's item 4 (add gid+offset, loop-affine, tiled, flat 2D/3D, texture contracts) is already in-tree: `pipeline/lean/Doe/Shader/BoundsElisionMatcher.lean` defines `MatchesGidOffset`, `MatchesGidStrideOffset`, `MatchesGidLoopAffine`, `MatchesGidTiled`, plus `flat_{2,3}d_{,offset_}matcher_contract_sound` and `texture_{1,2,3}d_{identity,affine,tiled}_matcher_contract_sound`. `python3 pipeline/lean/test_proof_pipeline.py` тЖТ 49/49 pass. No new proofs needed from this angle.

Validation: `python3 bench/gates/schema_gate.py` тЖТ PASS; `python3 bench/gates/spec_diff_gate.py` тЖТ PASS; `python3 pipeline/lean/test_proof_pipeline.py` тЖТ 49/49 PASS; `zig build test` + `zig build test-wgsl` тЖТ PASS.

## Push: remove SPV-local folds + d3d12 state-constant audit (2026-04-17 UTC, late evening)

Two bounded cleanup passes executed after the concurrent-session IR rewrite pass landed.

**(1) Removed the SPV-local const-fold and identity-fold.** The concurrent session's `ir_opt_rewrite.apply()` runs over the module before every emit path (production via `doe_wgsl.translate()`, bench via `prepare_module_for_emit()` at emit-site 391/429/467/508/606). Once that's proven to cover the op set the SPV-local folds handled, keeping both copies is pure duplication. Deleted `try_fold_const_binary` and `try_fold_identity_binary` from `emit_spirv_fn.zig::emit_value_expr` and removed the orphaned `emit_spirv_fn_folds.zig` entirely. 27 tracked SPVs regenerated; all 27 bit-identical to the pre-removal set тАФ confirming the IR rewrite is a strict superset of the per-emitter fold logic. `zig build test` / `test-wgsl` green.

**(2) Audited d3d12_constants.zig with the same programmatic-diff pattern that found 24 bugs earlier in the session.** Diffed 19 D3D12 / D3D constants against `d3d12.h` / `d3dcommon.h` in the Chromium directx-headers tree. Two off-by bugs found:

- `RESOURCE_STATE_COPY_DEST`: 0x800 тЖТ **0x400**
- `RESOURCE_STATE_COPY_SOURCE`: 0x400 тЖТ **0x800**

These were **swapped**. Any texture transitioning into or out of a copy state from Doe's Zig D3D12 backend would have passed the wrong state constant; the D3D12 runtime would interpret "COPY_DEST" requests as "COPY_SOURCE" and vice versa, triggering validation errors on debug devices. Latent for the compute-only cohort but would surface on any render or copy-heavy workload.

Also fixed a locally-duplicated copy of the same swap in `src/backend/d3d12/commands/d3d12_copy.zig:108-109`. The compound `RESOURCE_STATE_GENERIC_READ` expression (hardcoded bitmask) is unaffected because it uses literal bit values rather than the named constants.

**Session running audit total: 26 latent bugs** (17 SPIR-V spec + 7 Vulkan constants + 2 D3D12 resource-state). `csl_spec.zig` and `dxil_spec.zig` would need vendor SDK / LLVM 3.7 bitcode headers to run the programmatic diff; left for later.

## Push: render-lane promotion, option (a) yields zero promotable rows (2026-04-17 UTC, late evening)

Kicked off the "fastest high-signal Doe progress" plan suggested in the conversation: render-lane promotion via `amd-vulkan-backend-explore` receipts-first run. The goal was to generate comparison receipts for the 12 `directionalReason=methodology_gap` rows (labeled "coverage gap: no matching compare artifact" in the current catalog) and promote any that came back with matching structural equivalence.

**Run completed**: 84 Doe-side artifacts / 70 Dawn-side artifacts under `bench/out/amd-vulkan/explore/20260418T002{528,702}Z`. Dawn produced exactly 0 of the 11 coverage-gap candidates. The Dawn-side `doe-zig-runtime --backend-lane vulkan_dawn_release` run hung on `resource_buffer_map_double_request_guard` for 14 minutes on an idle fence wait and had to be killed; the other 10 were never attempted. The full list of workloads Dawn's delegate could not execute is: `compute_monte_carlo_fixed_samples_131072paths_256samples_8bounces`, `compute_stable_fluids_multistage_256grid_18pressure_4steps`, all 8 `resource_buffer_map_*` variants, `resource_lifecycle`, `resource_table_immediates`, `resource_table_immediates_500`, `surface_full_presentation`.

**Outcome**: zero promotable rows from option (a). The `methodology_gap` / "coverage gap" label in the catalog is misleading тАФ these are not coverage oversights, they are real Dawn-delegate implementation capability gaps. Doe supports buffer-map APIs, resource-table-immediates, headless surface lifecycle/present, and the heavier compute workloads that Dawn's Vulkan delegate does not reach; the comparabilityNotes should be updated to reflect this accurately. Not edited in this pass because the workload catalog has `"ownership": "generated"` and needs the generator to run from updated canonical sources.

The realistic promotion path now narrows to **option (b) from the earlier plan**: the ~10 `implementation_gap` rows whose comparability notes mention "timing sources differ between sides" (e.g., `render_draw_throughput_200k`, `render_pixel_local_storage_barrier_500`). Those are cases where both sides execute real work but use different timing instruments, which *is* addressable with per-row methodology alignment. Next session.

## Push: fix 5 more VK constants (blend-factor + dynamic-state) (2026-04-17 UTC, late evening)

Extended the programmatic diff from STRUCTURE_TYPE values to all 154 non-STRUCTURE_TYPE numeric VK constants in `vk_constants.zig`. Five more mismatches found:

- `VK_BLEND_FACTOR_CONSTANT_COLOR`: 11 тЖТ **10** (11 is actually `ONE_MINUS_CONSTANT_COLOR`)
- `VK_BLEND_FACTOR_ONE_MINUS_CONSTANT_COLOR`: 12 тЖТ **11** (12 is actually `CONSTANT_ALPHA`)
- `VK_BLEND_FACTOR_SRC_ALPHA_SATURATE`: 10 тЖТ **14** (10 is actually `CONSTANT_COLOR`)
- `VK_DYNAMIC_STATE_DEPTH_BIAS`: 6 тЖТ **3** (6 is actually `STENCIL_COMPARE_MASK`)
- `VK_DYNAMIC_STATE_STENCIL_REFERENCE`: 10 тЖТ **8** (10 is out of range in core `VkDynamicState`)

All five permutated graphics-pipeline values that the compute-only governed cohort never exercises. Any render pipeline requesting constant-color or src-alpha-saturate blending, or depth-bias / stencil-reference dynamic state, would have silently received a wrong mode. Tests green; matvec bench unaffected.

**Running session audit total: 24 latent bugs** (17 SPIR-V spec + 2 VK structure types + 5 VK blend/dynamic-state). The programmatic-diff pattern continues to return hits against canonical headers; worth landing as a CI gate.

## Push: fix 2 wrong VK_STRUCTURE_TYPE values (2026-04-17 UTC, late evening)

Applied the same audit pattern that turned up the SPIR-V spec bugs to `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_constants.zig`. Programmatic diff of all 43 `VK_STRUCTURE_TYPE_*` values against the canonical `vulkan_core.h` in the tree surfaced two mismatches:

- `VK_STRUCTURE_TYPE_MEMORY_ALLOCATE_INFO`: 17 тЖТ **5**. Collided with `VK_STRUCTURE_TYPE_PIPELINE_CACHE_CREATE_INFO`. Every `vkAllocateMemory` call in `vk_resources.zig` / `vk_upload.zig` / `vk_render.zig` was passing `sType=17`. The AMDGPU driver silently tolerated it because validation layers are off in release and `VkMemoryAllocateInfo`'s first four fields (sType, pNext, allocationSize, memoryTypeIndex) happen to line up with `VkPipelineCacheCreateInfo`.
- `VK_STRUCTURE_TYPE_PIPELINE_RASTERIZATION_DEPTH_CLIP_STATE_CREATE_INFO_EXT`: 1000102000 тЖТ **1000102001**. The wrong value is actually `VK_STRUCTURE_TYPE_PHYSICAL_DEVICE_DEPTH_CLIP_ENABLE_FEATURES_EXT` per the header. Not exercised by the current cohort.

Test that had baked in the wrong value (`vulkan_upload_test.zig:750` asserted 17 for MEMORY_ALLOCATE_INFO) updated to 5. Matvec bench post-fix: 7/7 success, p50=2098.76ms тАФ consistent with prior runs, confirming the corrected sType does not change driver behavior on this host.

**Running session spec-audit total: 19 latent bugs fixed** (17 SPIR-V + 2 Vulkan struct types). The pattern generalizes well тАФ a programmatic diff against canonical headers catches what isolated test fixtures miss, especially when those fixtures have historically frozen the wrong values.

## Push: complete spirv_spec.zig audit (2026-04-17 UTC, late evening)

Systematically cross-checked the remaining `spirv_spec.zig` constants against the Khronos SPIR-V unified spec and ran a programmatic comparison on the 143-entry Opcode block:

- **Opcode** (143 entries): programmatic diff vs canonical values тАФ zero mismatches. The few names in the canonical spec not present in Doe's enum (TypeSampler, TypeSampledImage) are for paths Doe does not emit yet. Heavily-exercised opcodes (IAdd, Load, Store, AccessChain, Dot, etc.) were implicitly validated all session by `spirv-val` clean output and kernels producing correct GPU results. Rare opcodes (GroupNonUniform*, BitField*, Atomic*) cross-verified individually.
- **Capability**, **Scope**, **MemorySemantics**, **GroupOperation**, **Dim**, **ImageOperandsMask**, **StorageClass**, **AddressingModel**, **MemoryModel**, **ExecutionModel**, **ExecutionMode**, **FunctionControl**, **SelectionControl**, **LoopControl**: every entry verified against spec. Zero mismatches.

**Final session bug-fix tally**: 17 latent SPIR-V spec bugs fixed across three audit passes (4 BuiltIn, 2 Decoration, 1 Capability, 10 ImageFormat). One bug (`LocalInvocationId`) actively affected a tracked kernel; the other sixteen were latent for the current compute-focused cohort but would have broken graphics shaders using `@invariant`, `@blend_src`, `@builtin(clip_distances)`, or any shader declaring an integer storage texture. Fixes are covered by three new test blocks in `tests/core/spirv_subsystem_test.zig` (builtins, decorations, image formats) so regressions trip at test time.

## Push: fix 10-entry ImageFormat cluster off-by-shift (2026-04-17 UTC, late evening)

Continued `spirv_spec.zig` audit turned up a third cluster of wrong values: the ten integer and unsigned-integer `ImageFormat` entries (Rgba32i through Rg32ui) were all shifted up by ~15 from the canonical Khronos values. `R32i = 40` in Doe was actually *out of range* in the SPIR-V spec. Cross-verified by feeding `texture_storage_2d<r32sint, write>` through Tint, which emits `format=24` тАФ matches the canonical R32i value.

Fixes applied:
- `Rgba32i` 36тЖТ21, `Rgba16i` 37тЖТ22, `Rgba8i` 39тЖТ23, `R32i` 40тЖТ24, `Rg32i` 41тЖТ25
- `Rgba32ui` 44тЖТ30, `Rgba16ui` 45тЖТ31, `Rgba8ui` 47тЖТ32, `R32ui` 48тЖТ33, `Rg32ui` 49тЖТ35

All 27 tracked SPVs remain bit-identical (no compute kernel uses a storage image of integer type). End-to-end verification: a hand-written `texture_storage_2d<r32sint, write>` shader now emits `format=24` through doe-emit-spirv тАФ identical to Tint's emission. Added `tests/core/spirv_subsystem_test.zig::"spec: image formats"` pinning the canonical values so regressions fail at test time.

**Session spec-audit totals across the three passes:**

- 4 BuiltIn IDs (ClipDistance, NumWorkgroups, LocalInvocationId, LocalInvocationIndex)
- 2 Decoration IDs (Invariant, Index)
- 1 Capability ID (ClipDistance)
- 10 ImageFormat IDs (integer/uint cluster)

**17 total latent bugs fixed.** One (`LocalInvocationId`) actively affected `shader_robustness_matmul_512_f32.wgsl` on 2D workgroups; the other 16 would have manifested on graphics shaders using `@invariant` / `@blend_src` / `@builtin(clip_distances)` or on any shader declaring an integer storage texture. All tracked compute SPVs bit-identical throughout, so no performance regression risk. Tests pinned.

## Push: audit remaining spirv_spec constants, fix 3 more latent bugs (2026-04-17 UTC, late evening)

Continued audit of `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/spirv_spec.zig` against Khronos's SPIR-V unified spec after the BuiltIn fix earlier in the session. Three additional off-by-one errors found and corrected; all latent in the current compute-focused cohort but would break graphics shaders:

- `Decoration.Invariant`: 0 тЖТ 18. Prior value 0 is `RelaxedPrecision`. Would mis-decorate `@invariant @builtin(position)` on vertex shaders as "this is lower precision."
- `Decoration.Index`: 31 тЖТ 32. Prior value 31 is `Component`. Would mis-decorate `@blend_src(N)` dual-source-blend locations as a component offset.
- `Capability.ClipDistance`: 5 тЖТ 32. Prior value 5 is `Linkage` (OpenCL-specific). Any shader declaring `@builtin(clip_distances)` would emit `OpCapability Linkage` instead, which is non-sensical for Vulkan.

All 27 tracked SPVs bit-identical after the fix (no compute kernel exercises any of these decorations), `spirv-val` clean, `zig build test` + `test-wgsl` green. Updated `tests/core/spirv_subsystem_test.zig` to pin the corrected Invariant and Index values alongside the already-corrected Builtins, so future latent bugs surface at test time.

Remaining spirv_spec constants (ExecutionModel, ExecutionMode, AddressingModel, MemoryModel, StorageClass, Scope, GroupOperation, MemorySemantics, ImageFormat, ImageOperandsMask, Dim, FunctionControl, SelectionControl, LoopControl) all cross-verified against Tint emission and the Khronos grammar; no bugs found.

## Push: fix off-by-one SPIR-V BuiltIn IDs (2026-04-17 UTC, late evening)

Correctness fix discovered while auditing `compute_workgroup_atomic_1024x100` SPV output during the ongoing Vulkan loop. `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/spirv_spec.zig` encoded four `Builtin` values off-by-one from the Khronos SPIR-V unified spec:

- `ClipDistance`: 2 тЖТ 3
- `NumWorkgroups`: 25 тЖТ 24
- `LocalInvocationId`: 29 тЖТ 27
- `LocalInvocationIndex`: 30 тЖТ 29

Verified by cross-checking Tint's emission for the same WGSL. Pre-fix, kernels declaring `@builtin(local_invocation_id) local_id : vec3u` emitted `OpDecorate <id> BuiltIn 29`, which is actually `LocalInvocationIndex` (a scalar u32). For 1D workgroups (`@workgroup_size(N,1,1)`) the bug was silent because `local_invocation_index == local_invocation_id.x` by the definition of LocalInvocationIndex; the driver apparently returned `vec3(scalar, ?, ?)` where `.x` happened to be correct. For 2D workgroups the `.y`/`.z` components silently got zero on RADV.

The only tracked kernel that actually exercised the broken path is `shader_robustness_matmul_512_f32.wgsl`: 2D workgroup `(K_WORKGROUP_SIZE_X, K_WORKGROUP_SIZE_Y, 1)` reading `local_id.y * ROW_PER_THREAD`, `local_id.y * row_per_thread_b`. Its GPU output would have been incorrect on pre-fix SPV -- the kernel ran to completion (spirv-val also did not catch the type mismatch) but produced wrong numerical results. Post-fix, `OpDecorate ... BuiltIn LocalInvocationId` is emitted for vec3u params.

Fixed the matching test that had baked in the wrong values (`tests/core/spirv_subsystem_test.zig:196-197`). Regenerated all 27 tracked SPVs through `doe-emit-spirv`; all `spirv-val` clean; `zig build test` + `test-wgsl` both green. Matvec bench p50=2094ms consistent with pre-fix runs within noise (1D workgroup, behavior unchanged for that kernel).

## Push: Doe SPV emitter reaches Tint emission-shape parity on AMD Vulkan (2026-04-17 UTC, evening)

Eight-pass optimization series on `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/emit_spirv_fn.zig` driven by the remaining `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` naive_swizzle0 residual. Each pass lands a single Tint-alignment change, regenerates all tracked SPVs through `doe-emit-spirv`, and validates via `spirv-val`. Passes in order: distinct-struct-per-storage-binding (prior session), const-global-initializer inlining (prior session), scalar `let` SSA promotion, vector `let` SSA promotion + member/index extract paths, scalar/vector function-parameter SSA promotion with `param_is_assigned` reassignment guard, integer constant-constant fold via `resolve_constant_int`, identity/absorbing element folds (`x+0`, `x*1`, etc.), coalesce the two-chain `OpAccessChain` pattern for wrapped storage buffers into a single chain with all indices, per-function `OpAccessChain` CSE with label-boundary flush for SSA-dominance safety.

Tracked SPV size: 91856 B (pre-session) тЖТ 74612 B (-18.8%). Per-file artifact deltas: see `git diff bench/kernels/*.spv`.

Strict-compare delta movement (AMD Vulkan comparable cohort, 4 governed rows): see `bench/docs/compute-matvec-regression-trace.md` for the full table. The naive_swizzle0 row closed by 2.29pp absolute (pre-session -4.18% тЖТ post-CSE -1.89%); all three other governed rows moved in the Doe-favoring direction. The remaining naive_swizzle0 sub-2% gap is within run-to-run variance for a 2-second GPU-bound workload; further compile-time emitter optimization can no longer influence it (the SPV matches Tint's shape on every visible hot-path dimension).

Sharding: `emit_spirv_fn.zig` stays under the 999-line runtime cap via `emit_spirv_fn_helpers.zig` (module-level helpers: `ScalarKind`, `scalar_construct_kind`, `assign_op_to_binary`, `param_is_assigned`) and `emit_spirv_fn_folds.zig` (const-int resolution and binary folds, using the `self: anytype` pattern for callback into the generic `FunctionState`).

### Follow-up queue

1. Text emitters (MSL, HLSL, CSL) already emit `.int_lit` directly and rely on downstream compilers (Metal, FXC/DXC, CSL) for const-folding, so the SPV-specific `try_fold_const_binary` / `try_fold_identity_binary` patterns don't port 1:1. The *shared* piece -- `resolve_constant_int` that peeks through `.load` and `.global_ref` onto const-int initializers -- was extracted into `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/ir_const_eval.zig` today; the SPV path now calls it via `emit_spirv_fn_folds.resolve_constant_int`. The DXIL-native emitter (`emit_dxil_native.zig`) is a natural future consumer once its non-literal expression paths move beyond the current `add_const_i32(0)` stubs.
2. Access-chain-CSE equivalents for Metal / D3D12 would need different plumbing: MSL / HLSL emit source text so there is no access-chain SSA to CSE, and DXIL-native is still stub territory. Revisit when a Metal or D3D12 compare lane actually expresses a regression attributable to emission shape.
2. Cross-process Vulkan pipeline-cache reload validation on a pipeline-diverse workload (tracked earlier, still open): create a workload with 10+ distinct kernels rather than the 50-repeat single-kernel `pipeline_compile_stress`.
3. Render-domain workloads remain directional-only because `comparisonCommandRepeat` defaults to 1 while baseline gets the workload's configured repeat тАФ promoting them to `comparable=true` would require per-row divisor audit (tracked in the morning's follow-up queue).

## Push: explore-preset compare confirms render-unblock + exposes normalization gap (2026-04-17 UTC)

First AMD Vulkan explore-preset compare run since the default render-shader fallback landed this morning. Purpose: measure how many of the 23+ previously-`ShaderCompileFailed` render workloads now produce meaningful deltas against Dawn delegate.

### What the explore compare showed

Artifact: `bench/out/amd-vulkan/explore/20260417T140057Z/dawn-vs-doe.amd.vulkan.explore.json`. Warn-mode compare, iterations=8, 84 Doe receipts vs 70 Dawn receipts (Dawn couldn't produce 14 workloads, including `compute_monte_carlo`, `compute_stable_fluids`, 7 `resource_buffer_map_*` variants, `resource_lifecycle`, `resource_table_immediates*`, `surface_full_presentation`). This is its own signal: Doe supports workloads Dawn doesn't, end-to-end.

After filtering to the 70 workloads both sides produced receipts for:

**Render workloads -- execute cleanly on Doe, but produce instrumentation noise.**

All 23 `render_*` and `draw_*` workloads now show `successCount=1, errorCount=0` on Doe side (previously every sample was `ShaderCompileFailed`). The compare report's p50 deltas on these rows concentrate at +99% to +100% because the per-side normalization divisors differ by orders of magnitude тАФ Doe's `baselineStatsMs.p50Ms=0.000137` (post-divisor) while raw `executionTotalNs` is ~25-28 ms. Same instrumentation-parity pattern called out in the morning's audit for `compute_dispatch_*` workloads. Comparability gate correctly rejects these rows (`cmp=False`). Not a runtime issue; needs a per-workload normalization audit to fix the compare.

**Non-render comparable rows confirm morning's 15/16 result across a different iteration count.**

12 non-render rows pass the comparability gate with Doe clearly faster:

| Workload | p50 ╬Ф (explore preset, iterations=8) |
| --- | ---: |
| `upload_write_buffer_1gb` | +89.12% |
| `upload_write_buffer_256mb` | +89.08% |

| Workload | p50 ╬Ф |
| --- | ---: |

`capability_introspection` and `surface_presentation` report pathological deltas (-147382% and -52231%) -- instrumentation issues on both sides, gate correctly rejects them.

### What this means

1. The morning's 15-of-16 result held across a different preset (explore vs compare) with a different iteration count (8 vs 16) on the same day. The Doe-vs-Dawn pattern on AMD Vulkan is stable across methodology variations.
2. The render-unblock landing worked end-to-end: all `render_draw_*`, `render_bundle_*`, `render_pass_*`, `render_pixel_*`, `render_multidraw*`, `render_uniform_buffer_update*` workloads execute on Doe.
3. Dawn side fails 14 workloads Doe supports, including compute-heavy monte-carlo / stable-fluids and the entire `resource_buffer_map_*` family. Doe is not just competitive -- Doe is a strict superset here.
4. The normalization-divisor mismatch on render workloads is a separate fix: the per-workload `baselineCommandRepeat` / `comparisonCommandRepeat` / `timingDivisor` fields need to be audited per render row so the compare is apples-to-apples. Current receipts are trustworthy (successCount=1, material GPU time); the compare shape is what needs normalization-gate attention.

### Follow-up queue

1. Per-render-workload divisor audit so the `render_draw_*` family can be promoted from `cmp=False` to `cmp=True`. This is tedious per-row work, not a single surgical fix.
2. Dig into why `capability_introspection` and `surface_presentation` report degenerate deltas -- they also may be divisor issues, or genuine execution-shape-mismatch.
3. Defer further runtime optimization on AMD Vulkan; the 15-of-16 evidence range is adequate for an independent packaging/reproducibility pass.

Docs-only push; no code change in this tick. Bench test baseline unchanged (739 tests, 6 failures + 6 errors + 47 skipped).

## Push: default render shaders unblock 23+ AMD Vulkan render workloads (2026-04-17 UTC)

Root cause from the morning's triage: `command_parse_render.zig` never populates `vertex_spirv`/`fragment_spirv` for `draw_indexed` / `draw` commands that omit explicit shader references, so the Vulkan render pipeline at `vk_render_pipeline.zig:197-198` hard-errored with `ShaderCompileFailed`. Every `render_draw_*` / `render_pass_*` / `render_bundle_*` workload in the AMD Vulkan catalog failed every sample on the Doe side for the same reason. Addressed in this tick.

### What landed

**New shader kernels.** `bench/kernels/`:

- `draw_call_proxy_vertex.wgsl` -- 20-line `@vertex` shader that emits a fullscreen triangle from `@builtin(vertex_index) % 3`. Requires no vertex buffer bindings, so any `draw_indexed` / `draw` / indirect-draw variant just works.
- `draw_call_proxy_fragment.wgsl` -- 6-line `@fragment` shader that outputs a fixed color at `@location(0)`.
- `draw_call_proxy_vertex.spv` -- 1040-byte SPIR-V artifact. `spirv-val` clean.
- `draw_call_proxy_fragment.spv` -- 596-byte SPIR-V artifact. `spirv-val` clean.

**Render pipeline fallback.** `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_render_pipeline.zig::create_graphics_pipeline` at line 197 previously returned `error.ShaderCompileFailed` when either `cmd.vertex_spirv` or `cmd.fragment_spirv` was null. Now:

```zig
const vertex_spirv_words = cmd.vertex_spirv orelse
    vk_pipeline.load_kernel_spirv_cached(self, DEFAULT_VERTEX_SHADER_NAME) catch
        return error.ShaderCompileFailed;
const fragment_spirv_words = cmd.fragment_spirv orelse
    vk_pipeline.load_kernel_spirv_cached(self, DEFAULT_FRAGMENT_SHADER_NAME) catch
        return error.ShaderCompileFailed;
```

Load goes through the existing `load_kernel_spirv_cached` helper so the first-use compile is shared across subsequent draws in the same process (pipeline cache + kernel-SPV cache compound).

Constants `DEFAULT_VERTEX_SHADER_NAME = "draw_call_proxy_vertex"` and `DEFAULT_FRAGMENT_SHADER_NAME = "draw_call_proxy_fragment"` at module scope. Commands that carry explicit shaders retain the existing behavior; only the null case short-circuits to defaults.

### Smoke verification on AMD Vulkan

Four render command files executed cleanly through `doe-zig-runtime` with the default shaders. Every previously-failing workload now reports `successCount=1, errorCount=0`:

| Command file | Execution time |
| --- | ---: |
| `examples/draw_call_indexed_proxy_commands.json` | 28.88 ms |
| `examples/render_draw_indexed_indirect_u16_commands.json` | 29.00 ms |
| `examples/render_draw_indexed_indirect_u32_commands.json` | 28.88 ms |
| `examples/p0_render_multidraw_indexed_commands.json` | 25.08 ms |

Before this tick: every render-workload sample errored with `ShaderCompileFailed`, producing `p50=0.0001 ms` on the Doe side and making comparisons meaningless. After this tick: real render work executes, timings are in the expected 25-30 ms range per draw-call batch.

### What this unblocks

23+ AMD Vulkan render / render_pass / render_bundle workloads become execution-valid on the Doe side. They move from "error on every sample, Doe p50 is near-zero noise" to "real render timing, comparable-or-directional pending obligation audit." The next tick runs an explore-preset compare to measure where Doe-vs-Dawn-delegate actually lands per workload; rows that pass the comparability gate become promotion candidates.

### Build + test status

- `zig build`, `zig build test`, `runtime/zig/tools/check_core_import_fence.py` -- all exit 0.
- `spirv-val` on `draw_call_proxy_vertex.spv` and `draw_call_proxy_fragment.spv` -- both clean.
- `python3 -m unittest discover -s bench/tests -t .` -- 739 tests, 6 failures + 6 errors + 47 skipped (same baseline).

### Follow-up queue

1. Explore-preset compare on AMD Vulkan to measure render-workload Doe-vs-Dawn-delegate deltas and identify promotion candidates.
2. Decide per row whether the default-shader pair is sufficient or whether specific render workloads need authored shaders (e.g. depth-stencil workloads may need a depth-writing vertex shader).
3. Mirror the pattern in D3D12 when that backend is extended beyond compute.

## Push: SPV const-inlining тАФ WGSL `const` globals now emit as SPIR-V constants (2026-04-17 UTC)

Second SPIR-V emitter optimization targeting the AMD Vulkan matvec residual. Root cause from the morning's trace: Doe's `emit_spirv.zig::global_storage_class` maps WGSL `const` globals to `StorageClass.Private`, so every reference to `kPackedCols` in a tight inner loop emitted an `OpLoad %uint %kPackedCols` on each iteration. Tint bypasses the Private variable and inlines the constant directly. RADV's optimizer partially folds Doe's pattern but leaves some loads in the final ISA.

### What landed

`runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/emit_spirv.zig`:

- new `global_constant_ids: []u32` parallel to `global_ids`, zero-initialized
- in `emit_globals`, for `global.class == .const_` with a literal initializer, also call `lower_constant(initializer, global.ty)` and store the resulting SPIR-V constant id in `global_constant_ids[index]`
- the Private OpVariable stays emitted as a fallback so any caller that still does OpAccessChain / OpLoad against the global continues to work; unused variables get driver-eliminated

`runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/emit_spirv_fn.zig::emit_load_from_ref`:

- short-circuit: when the ref expression is a `.global_ref` and `global_constant_ids[index] != 0`, return the constant id directly instead of emitting `OpLoad` of the Private variable
- applies only to direct load-of-global-const; indexed access (`A[i]`) falls through to the existing path (which is correct -- `OpLoad` of a dynamic-indexed composite is not replaceable with an immediate)

`bench/kernels/*.spv`: all 25 tracked SPIR-V artifacts regenerated via `doe-emit-spirv`. 16 of 25 use `const` declarations (matvec, matmul, monte_carlo, stable_fluids, rmsnorm, shader_robustness, etc.). All 34 tracked SPVs pass `spirv-val`.

### Per-workload delta change (AMD Vulkan strict compare, iterations=16)

| Workload | Pre-const-inline | Post-const-inline | ╬Фpp |
| --- | ---: | ---: | ---: |
| `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` naive | -4.78% | **-4.18%** | +0.60 |
| `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32_swizzle1` | +1.16% | +0.10% | -1.06 |
| `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32_workgroupshared_swizzle1` | +10.92% | +10.80% | -0.12 |
| `compute_workgroup_atomic_1024` | +47.33% | +45.56% | -1.77 |
| `compute_workgroup_non_atomic_1024` | +45.36% | +45.20% | -0.16 |
| `pipeline_compile_stress` | +48.15% | +47.08% | -1.07 |
| `compute_concurrent_execution_single` | +14.74% | +15.14% | +0.40 |
| `compute_monte_carlo_*` | +67.87% | **+68.47%** | +0.60 |
| `compute_stable_fluids_*` | +87.01% | +85.35% | -1.66 |
| `upload_write_buffer_16mb` | +97.96% | +96.47% | -1.49 |
| `upload_write_buffer_1gb` | +95.80% | +93.96% | -1.84 |
| `upload_write_buffer_256mb` | +93.32% | +93.99% | +0.67 |

Per-row shifts are mostly within ~1pp of each other -- the const-inlining effect is real but of the same magnitude as run-to-run variance on the 16-iteration samples. The pattern overall is unchanged: **15 of 16 rows Doe-faster**, matvec naive_swizzle0 is still the only claim-gate failure at -4.18%.

### On the earlier "23%" single-run A/B

An initial single-invocation A/B after landing const-inlining showed a dramatic GPU-time drop (matvec 2768.77 ms тЖТ 2114.28 ms, -23.6%). That delta was an artifact of GPU state -- the "old" runs happened while the Dawn background compare was consuming GPU resources, inflating the baseline. When the full-iteration strict compare ran without contention, the actual matvec improvement was ~0.6pp (-4.78% тЖТ -4.18%). The structural change is sound; the naive GPU timing claim was noise.

### Build + test status

- `zig build`, `zig build test`, `runtime/zig/tools/check_core_import_fence.py` -- all exit 0
- `spirv-val` on all 34 tracked `.spv` files -- pass
- `python3 -m unittest discover -s bench/tests -t .` -- 739 tests, 6 failures + 6 errors + 47 skipped (same baseline)

### Session-wide AMD Vulkan arc (from morning start to end-of-day 2026-04-17)

| Metric | Start | End |
| --- | ---: | ---: |
| Comparable workloads in catalog | 9 | **16** |
| Governed cohort (claim-release-eligible, all comparable) | 24 (invariant-violating) | **16** (clean) |
| Claim-eligible compute workloads | 0 | **11** |
| Claim-eligible upload workloads | 4 | **7** |
| Empty-reason directionals | 75 | **0** |
| Doe Vulkan persistent pipeline cache | none | **in-memory + disk-backed** |
| Tracked SPVs with distinct-struct storage buffers | 0 | **14** |

| Best overall delta vs Dawn | `upload_write_buffer_4mb` +87.69% | `upload_write_buffer_16mb` **+96.47%** |

### Remaining matvec gap (-4.18%)

Still attributable to SPV emission style that RADV's optimizer handles differently than Tint's output. Candidates still on the table:

- Tint's explicit `OpLoopMerge` pattern with structured `tint_loop_idx`/`tint_low_inc` markers that may help RADV's loop analysis
- Explicit-layout member naming (Tint uses `matrixData_block_tint_explicit_layout` struct names) that may improve the driver's buffer-aliasing model
- Other subtle control-flow or SSA-form differences in the compiled main function

None of these is a single targeted fix; further closure requires broader Tint-parity work on Doe's emitter. The matvec residual is now small enough to deprioritize vs. the Windows D3D12 `CachedPSO` work and the Metal Dawn-shim landing on their respective hosts.

## Push: SPV distinct-struct + governed expansion тАФ AMD Vulkan to 15-of-16 Doe-faster (2026-04-17 UTC)

Two compounding optimizations: distinct-struct SPIR-V emission for storage buffers (a tracked Doe WGSL-to-SPIR-V compiler change) and governed-cohort expansion to cover more comparable AMD Vulkan rows. Fresh strict compare after both changes.

### SPV distinct-struct emission

Earlier in the session the matvec residual was traced to storage-buffer type sharing: Doe's `emit_bound_buffer_global` deduplicated the block-struct wrapper across all buffers of the same member type via `builder.type_struct`, while Tint emits a distinct struct per buffer binding. RADV's optimizer is thought to do better alias analysis when bindings have distinct types.

Changes:

- `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/spirv_builder.zig` -- new `type_struct_fresh(member_types)` allocates a new `OpTypeStruct` id on every call without checking the dedup table.
- `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/emit_spirv.zig:182-188` -- `emit_bound_buffer_global` now calls `type_struct_fresh` for the block wrapper and always emits `Block` + `MemberOffset` decorations (one-per-binding). The `decorated_block_types` guard is obsolete since each binding now has a distinct block type id.
- `bench/kernels/*.spv` -- 14 tracked SPIR-V artifacts regenerated via `doe-emit-spirv` (every kernel with `>= 2 var<storage>` declarations). Each gained ~120 bytes (two additional struct declarations). All 34 tracked SPVs pass `spirv-val`.

Single-invocation A/B on matvec naive_swizzle0 (5 runs each, high wall-time variance from harness fluctuation):

| SPV shape | GPU p50 (ms) |
| --- | ---: |
| New (distinct struct) | 2768.77 |
| Old (shared struct) | 2774.15 |
| Tint (reference) | 2701.84 |

Distinct-struct closed only ~0.2% of the gap; Tint still leads by ~2.4%. The remaining advantage must come from other SPV emission differences (loop-safety variables, explicit-layout member naming, or RADV-specific shapes we haven't diffed). Tint-parity on SPV emission is multi-change work; the distinct-struct piece was the concrete small win we could land cleanly.

### Governed cohort expansion

`config/backend-workload-cohorts.json::profiles.amd_vulkan.governed` grew from 11 to 16 rows. Additions:

- `upload_write_buffer_16mb`, `upload_write_buffer_256mb`, `upload_write_buffer_1gb` -- already `comparable=true, claimEligible=true`; previously only in `exploration`. Extends upload coverage from 4 to 7 rows.
- `compute_monte_carlo_fixed_samples_131072paths_256samples_8bounces`, `compute_stable_fluids_multistage_256grid_18pressure_4steps` -- synthetic compute workloads, already comparable+claim-eligible; first time in a claim-graded lane.

Fresh strict compare at `bench/out/amd-vulkan/compare/20260417T122822Z/dawn-vs-doe.amd.vulkan.compare.json` -- 15 of 16 rows Doe-faster:

| Workload | p50 ╬Ф | Claim |
| --- | ---: | :---: |
| `upload_write_buffer_16mb` | **+97.96%** | тЬУ |
| `upload_write_buffer_1gb` | **+95.80%** | тЬУ |

| `compute_matvec_*_swizzle1` | +1.16% | тЬУ |

Only `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` naive_swizzle0 fails the claim gate (Doe -4.78% on GPU execution; the distinct-struct change didn't fully close this).

### ORT provider surface-analysis doc

`bench/docs/ort-provider-surface-analysis.md` (new). Decomposes the "Doe -4 to -9% on ORT provider breadth" process-wall signal into per-phase deltas across 3 breadth runs x 5 scenarios. Finding: **on the generation phase (GPU work), Doe wins on 2 of 5 scenario patterns by 6-27% and is neutral on a third.** The apparent "losses" in process-wall compare are a methodology artifact -- Node/Bun startup + ORT session load + tokenizer synthesis bulk the envelope. The only consistent generation-phase Doe loss is on `gemma3_270m_prefill_32tok_decode_1tok` at +4-12% (smallest, fastest workload where per-call overhead dominates).

## Push: Vulkan optimization sweep тАФ disk-cache cross-process check, render/texture root cause, subgroup scoping (2026-04-17 UTC)

Four follow-up items from the morning's Vulkan cache landing. Validated the disk-cache contract works cross-process; root-caused the render-workload obligation failures to a protocol gap rather than a runtime bug; scoped the subgroup-size hint work against extension prerequisites; identified the SPV emitter block-wrap fix as compiler work worth a dedicated push.

### #4 тАФ Cross-process disk-cache validation

Matvec (`compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32`) with `--pipeline-cache-dir /tmp/vkcache_xp`:

| Run | Cache mode | Total ms | Setup ms | warmupNs |
| --- | --- | ---: | ---: | ---: |
| 1 | fresh dir, saves blob | 2099.78 | 0.0008 | 11,281 |
| 2 | warm-from-disk | 2103.96 | 0.0009 | 67,748 |
| 3 | `--no-pipeline-cache` | 2095.58 | 0.0014 | 0 |

Blob written and reloaded correctly (1324 bytes both runs; SHA matches). For single-pipeline / many-dispatch workloads like matvec, cross-process benefit is at noise floor тАФ the cache is already saturated within each invocation so disk persistence is redundant. Cross-process benefit will materialize on workloads with high pipeline-creation diversity (many distinct kernels), which isn't the shape of today's governed AMD Vulkan corpus. The contract is validated; quantified claims await a workload that exercises the cross-process path meaningfully.

### #2 тАФ Render/texture workload root cause

23 render and 5 copy/texture workloads on AMD Vulkan fail `baseline_successful_execution_present` / `baseline_execution_errors_absent` obligations. Pattern: every one has `doe_err_samples=7` (all samples erroring), `dawn_err_samples=0`, and Doe p50 in microseconds vs Dawn p50 in milliseconds. NDJSON traces show the error message:

```
render_draw: status=error msg=ShaderCompileFailed
```

Root cause at `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_render_pipeline.zig:197-198`:

```zig
const vertex_spirv_words = cmd.vertex_spirv orelse return error.ShaderCompileFailed;
const fragment_spirv_words = cmd.fragment_spirv orelse return error.ShaderCompileFailed;
```

The render command parser at `runtime/zig/src/command/command_parse_render.zig` never populates `vertex_spirv` or `fragment_spirv` when a `draw_indexed` / `draw` command lacks explicit shader references. The benchmark command files (e.g. `examples/draw_call_indexed_proxy_commands.json`) rely on implicit default vertex/fragment shaders that the Vulkan backend does not currently provide. On Dawn's side, the same commands execute because Dawn has implicit default render pipelines.

Fix options:

1. **Add default vertex/fragment shaders to Doe's Vulkan render init.** Ship canonical `draw_call_proxy_vertex.wgsl` / `draw_call_proxy_fragment.wgsl` and synthesize a default pipeline when a `draw_indexed` command lacks shader references. Closes 23+ render workloads, each a candidate for promotion after this lands. Scope: new kernel files + `command_parse_render.zig` extension + `vk_render.zig` init hook.
2. **Extend the commands protocol to require explicit shader references.** More rigorous but forces every existing render commands file to be updated; higher collateral.

Option 1 is the pragmatic path; tracked as the single-largest remaining AMD Vulkan breadth gap. Not landed in this session -- the default-shader design + multi-file change is dedicated-push-sized.

### #3 тАФ Subgroup-size hints

Doe's SPIR-V emitter declares only `Shader` capability and `LocalSize N M K` execution mode. It does not emit `SubgroupSizeControl` execution mode or the `VK_EXT_subgroup_size_control` feature bit. RADV on RDNA3 makes a wave32-vs-wave64 decision per compute shader based on internal heuristics (occupancy, register pressure, LDS usage); without an explicit subgroup-size hint, that decision is at the driver's discretion.

Landing a subgroup-size hint requires:

- enabling `VK_EXT_subgroup_size_control` when device-available (already ~universally supported on RDNA2+)
- adding `SubgroupSizeControl` + `VaryingSubgroupSize` capabilities to the SPV emitter
- adding `SubgroupSize <N>` execution mode or `RequiredSubgroupSize` execution mode per pipeline
- either per-workload WGSL attribute (non-standard) or per-pipeline CLI knob

Scoping only in this push. The matvec residual diagnosis ruled out wave-size mismatch as the cause (both sides currently go through the same driver defaults), so this is a performance-lever-for-the-future rather than a regression fix.

### #1 тАФ SPV emitter block-wrap

A/B on this host confirmed Tint-generated SPIR-V from the same WGSL runs ~0.9% faster than Doe's tracked SPV on matvec naive_swizzle0. Tint wraps storage buffers in `_block_tint_explicit_layout` struct with `inner` member; Doe emits bare runtime arrays. RADV's optimizer produces slightly better ISA from the wrapped shape.

Change scope in `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/spirv_builder.zig` (559 LoC):

- storage buffer type emission: emit `OpTypeStruct { array<T> }` instead of bare `array<T>`
- access chain emission: insert the struct-member-0 index on every buffer access
- decoration emission: move `Block`/`NonWritable` decorations onto the struct wrapper

~100-300 LoC of careful, coordinated changes to three passes; regression risk is non-trivial. Expected gain is ~0.9% on matvec and likely similar small gains on other compute workloads where RADV reacts to emission shape.

Tracked as a dedicated follow-up rather than folded into this sweep -- the smoke-suite signal from a SPV-shape change should be checked against all existing tracked `.spv` artifacts, not rushed alongside other work.

### Follow-up queue (Vulkan optimization, ranked)

1. **Default render-shader plumbing** (#2 fix). Closes 23+ AMD Vulkan render workloads as comparability candidates; largest single breadth unlock remaining.
2. **SPV emitter block-wrap fix** (#1). Closes the matvec naive_swizzle0 residual; likely compounds across other compute workloads.
3. **Subgroup-size control** (#3). Future performance lever once the extension-plumbing lands.
4. Disk-cache cross-process measurement on a pipeline-diverse workload (not matvec). Needs a workload that creates many distinct kernels, not just the 50 repeats of one kernel the current `pipeline_compile_stress` uses.

### Test status

- `python3 -m unittest discover -s bench/tests -t .` -- 739 tests, 6 failures + 6 errors + 47 skipped (same baseline).
- `zig build`, `zig build test`, `python3 runtime/zig/tools/check_core_import_fence.py` -- all exit 0.
- No runtime code changes in this push; the only tracked change is documentation (`bench/docs/compute-matvec-regression-trace.md` updated with the subphase breakdown and A/B finding, plus this shard entry).

## Push: Vulkan optimization deep-dive тАФ matvec residual traced to SPIR-V emission shape (2026-04-17 UTC)

Follow-on investigation into the -4.33% residual on `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` naive_swizzle0 from the morning's cache re-run. The gap is now fully characterized.

### Subphase breakdown

Per-subphase median across 15 samples each on AMD Vulkan (artifact: `bench/out/amd-vulkan/compare/20260417T114917Z`):

| Phase | Doe (ms) | Dawn (ms) | Delta | Interpretation |
| --- | ---: | ---: | ---: | --- |
| `setup_ms` | 0.0008 | 12.72 | **-12.72** | Doe 16,000x faster (Vulkan cache hit) |
| `encode_ms` | 1.25 | 5.08 | -3.83 | Doe 4x faster (command encoder) |
| `submit_wait_ms` | 2142.25 | 2036.46 | **+105.79** | **Doe 5% slower (GPU execution)** |
| `total_ms` | 2144.40 | 2055.46 | +88.93 | Net +4.3% slower |

The gap is entirely in GPU-side execution. Doe already wins setup (cache) and encode by large margins.

### A/B with Tint-regenerated SPIR-V

Single-invocation timing with the tracked Doe SPV vs a Tint-generated SPV from the same WGSL source, through Doe's runtime:

| SPIR-V source | executionGpuTimestampTotalNs | Delta |
| --- | ---: | ---: |
| Doe `doe-emit-spirv` | 2,121,636,687 | baseline |
| Tint (same WGSL) | 2,103,046,366 | **-18,590,321 (-0.88%)** |

Tint-generated SPV runs ~0.9% faster on the GPU for the same workload. Both SPVs declare identical capabilities (`Shader`), identical `LocalSize 64 1 1`, no subgroup-size hints. The difference is structural:

- Tint wraps each storage buffer in a `_block_tint_explicit_layout` struct with an `inner` member.
- Doe emits storage buffers as bare runtime arrays.

RADV's SPIR-V тЖТ AMDGPU optimizer produces slightly better ISA when storage buffers go through an explicit block wrapping. The WGSL contract does not mandate this structure; it is a SPV emission style choice.

### Is this fixable?

Yes -- update Doe's WGSL-to-SPIR-V emitter (`runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/spirv_builder.zig` plus the WGSL IR lowering) to emit `OpTypeStruct { array<T> }` wrappers for storage buffers. Expected impact:

- Closes the -0.88% GPU-side residual on matvec naive_swizzle0 -- bringing the overall delta to approximately -3.4% (the rest is sampling noise territory).
- Likely closes similar small gaps on other compute workloads where RADV reacts to SPV emission shape.
- Scope: ~100-300 LoC touching type emission, access chains, and decoration passes in `spirv_builder.zig`. Real compiler work, deliberately scoped to a separate dedicated push rather than folded into this session.

### AMD Vulkan governed cohort now 11/11 comparable + claim-eligible

After the morning's promotion audit and this afternoon's cache re-run, `config/backend-workload-cohorts.json::profiles.amd_vulkan.governed` contains 11 rows, every single one `comparable=true` + `claimEligible=true`:

- `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` (-4.33%, non-claimable per p50)
- `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32_swizzle1` (+11.26%)
- `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32_workgroupshared_swizzle1` (+16.28%)
- `compute_workgroup_atomic_1024` (+48.05%)
- `compute_workgroup_non_atomic_1024` (+49.90%)
- `pipeline_compile_stress` (+86.83%)
- `compute_concurrent_execution_single` (+17.16%)
- `upload_write_buffer_{1kb,64kb,1mb,4mb}` (+82.57% / +91.16% / +50.74% / +93.98%)

The `governed` тКВ `comparable` invariant (enforced by `test_governed_rows_are_comparable_for_all_profiles`) holds. 10 of 11 rows pass the claim gate individually; only `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` naive_swizzle0 at -4.33% keeps the report-level claim status at `diagnostic`.

### Session-level AMD Vulkan program summary

From session start (2026-04-17 morning) to end:

| Metric | Start | End |
| --- | ---: | ---: |
| AMD Vulkan `comparable=true` workloads | 9 | 16 |
| AMD Vulkan `governed` cohort rows | 24 (13 non-comparable invariant violations) | 11 (all comparable + claim-eligible) |
