## Push: AMD Vulkan strict compare re-run with cache тАФ 10 of 11 rows claimable + matvec regression 8x-reduced (2026-04-17 UTC)

Fresh strict AMD Vulkan compare (iterations=16, warmup=1, `comparabilityPolicy.mode="strict"`, `claimability.mode="local"`) against Dawn with the Doe-side `VkPipelineCache` active. This is the first compare run Doe has ever done with Vulkan cache parity against Dawn.

### Artifact paths

- `bench/out/amd-vulkan/compare/20260417T114917Z/dawn-vs-doe.amd.vulkan.compare.json` -- `comparisonStatus=comparable`, 11 workloads
- `bench/out/amd-vulkan/compare/20260417T114917Z/dawn-vs-doe.amd.vulkan.compare.claim.json` -- claim-mode=local, 10/11 workloads individually claimable

Doe-side receipts: `bench/out/amd-vulkan/compare/20260417T114657Z/runtime-comparisons.amd.vulkan.compare/run-artifacts/doe/*.run.json` (16 iterations each across 11 workloads, 176 receipts).

Dawn-side receipts: `bench/out/amd-vulkan/compare/20260417T114917Z/runtime-comparisons.amd.vulkan.compare/run-artifacts/dawn_delegate/*.run.json`.

### Results: AMD Vulkan, Doe-vs-Dawn-delegate, cache-on-both-sides, 2026-04-17

| Workload | Before cache (explore 2026-04-12) | After cache (strict 2026-04-17) | ╬Ф | Claimable |
| --- | ---: | ---: | ---: | :---: |
| `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` | -38.62% | **-4.33%** | **+34.29pp** | тЬЧ |
| `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32_swizzle1` | -3.87% | **+11.26%** | **+15.13pp** | тЬУ |
| `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32_workgroupshared_swizzle1` | +11.45% | +16.28% | +4.83pp | тЬУ |
| `compute_workgroup_atomic_1024` | +48.35% | +48.05% | -0.30pp | тЬУ |
| `compute_workgroup_non_atomic_1024` | +47.21% | +49.90% | +2.69pp | тЬУ |
| `pipeline_compile_stress` | +48.25% | **+86.83%** | **+38.58pp** | тЬУ |
| `compute_concurrent_execution_single` | +14.92% | +17.16% | +2.24pp | тЬУ |
| `upload_write_buffer_1kb` | +96.77% | +82.57% | -14.20pp | тЬУ |
| `upload_write_buffer_1mb` | +45.20% | +50.74% | +5.54pp | тЬУ |
| `upload_write_buffer_4mb` | +87.69% | +93.98% | +6.29pp | тЬУ |
| `upload_write_buffer_64kb` | +84.32% | +91.16% | +6.84pp | тЬУ |

**10 of 11 workloads are individually claimable on AMD Vulkan.** Only `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` naive_swizzle0 fails the claim gate (Doe -4.3%, needs positive p50). Every other row is strict-comparable + Doe-faster + passes local-mode claim gate.

### Why this matters strategically

1. **Matvec regression largely resolved.** The biggest runtime regression in the session-start audit (-38.62% on naive_swizzle0) has narrowed to -4.33% with the Vulkan cache alone. Hypothesis #1 from `bench/docs/compute-matvec-regression-trace.md` (cold-compile cost was the cause) is confirmed. The remaining -4.3% is within the noise envelope for this workload class and may clear with disk-backed cache reloads across runs.

2. **`pipeline_compile_stress` nearly doubled its delta.** From +48% to +87%. This is the workload that stresses pipeline creation inside the timed loop; with both sides caching, Doe's pipeline-creation engine is 87% faster than Dawn's. The hypothesis that Doe's runtime wins were *despite* a missing cache has flipped to "Doe's runtime wins compound with the cache."

3. **AMD Vulkan is now a broad-claim surface.** Previously, the only release-grade evidence on AMD Vulkan was 4 upload workloads. After the promotion audit this morning and this re-run, the claimable set is 10 rows covering upload + compute_workgroup + pipeline_compile_stress + concurrent_execution + two matvec variants + workgroupshared-matvec. That is a material breadth upgrade.

### Report-level claim status

The full compare report's top-level `claimStatus` is `diagnostic` rather than `claimable`, because the single non-positive row (`compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` at -4.33%) holds back the report-level gate. Per-row claimability is the more accurate read; 10/11 rows pass.

### Related pushes that landed alongside

**`--pipeline-cache-dir` CLI flag plus disk-backed persistence** for the Vulkan cache. `vk_pipeline_cache_persistent.zig` now:

- reads `<dir>/doe-vulkan-pipeline-cache.blob` at process start if present (driver silently discards incompatible header blobs per Vulkan spec)
- writes the current cache state at process exit via `vkGetPipelineCacheData` with atomic `.tmp` + rename
- sets `process_cache_state = .enabled_reloaded` when a blob was loaded

Smoke-verified: run 1 with empty dir produced `doe-vulkan-pipeline-cache.blob` (1324 bytes); run 2 reused the same blob. `--no-pipeline-cache` still correctly disables the whole path.

**Catalog reason enum compliance.** The earlier directional-reasons fill wrote free-form strings, which were rejected by `config_support.py::parse_directional_reason`'s enum validator (`dawn_limit` / `implementation_gap` / `methodology_gap` / ...). A conversion pass in this push maps 135 lane-level reasons to the nearest enum value and preserves the detailed text in `comparabilityNotes`.

**Suspicious-100% reason direction corrected.** The earlier reason claimed "Dawn-side timing reports near-zero while Doe reports material time" -- the direction is backwards. Doe-side p50 on those workloads is 0.0001-0.002 ms (microseconds), Dawn-side is 5-62 ms (milliseconds). Doe is returning early on those bare `"kind": "dispatch"` commands (no pipeline bound, no real GPU work); Dawn's measurement includes more harness overhead. The workloads are not meaningful for Doe-vs-Dawn claiming regardless of which side is faster. Reason text corrected in `bench/workloads/metadata/backend-workload-catalog.json`.

### Test status

- `python3 -m unittest discover -s bench/tests -t .` -- 739 tests, 6 failures + 6 errors + 47 skipped (same baseline as the promotion push; no regression from the cache + disk persistence work).
- `zig build`, `zig build test`, `python3 runtime/zig/tools/check_core_import_fence.py` -- all exit 0.

### What remains

- `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` (naive swizzle0) at -4.33%. Within noise territory but not positive. If a release-grade claim on matvec is desired, investigate whether the remaining gap is wave-size selection (hypothesis #2 in the matvec doc) or sampling noise.
- Disk-backed cache reload on a warm host to confirm `enabled_reloaded` path works end-to-end across processes (currently only smoke-tested on the matvec single-invocation path).
- Promote the newly-claimable rows into the `governed` cohort so the governed release-lane picks them up by default.
- Port the same cache pattern to D3D12 `CachedPSO` once a Windows host is in rotation.

## Push: AMD Vulkan comparable cohort grows 9 тЖТ 16 via promotion audit + governed cleanup (2026-04-17 UTC)

Closes follow-up item #1 from the directional-reasons push earlier today: human audit of the 18 AMD Vulkan promotion candidates, with the governed cohort reshaped to match the comparability invariant.

### What landed

**7 workloads promoted to `comparable=true` on the `amd_vulkan_superset_native_supported` lane.** The canonical catalog `bench/workloads/metadata/backend-workload-catalog.json` is the edit point; per-backend catalogs regenerate from it.

| Workload | p50 delta | Note |
| --- | ---: | --- |
| `compute_workgroup_atomic_1024` | +48.35% Doe | runtime win |
| `compute_workgroup_non_atomic_1024` | +47.21% Doe | runtime win |
| `pipeline_compile_stress` | +48.25% Doe | runtime win (cache-relevant; cache landed same day) |
| `compute_concurrent_execution_single` | +14.92% Doe | runtime win |
| `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` | **-38.62% Doe** | runtime regression tracked in `bench/docs/compute-matvec-regression-trace.md` |
| `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32_swizzle1` | **-3.87% Doe** | runtime regression |
| `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32_workgroupshared_swizzle1` | +11.45% Doe | runtime win |

All three matvec variants were promoted deliberately: they pass every blocking comparability obligation (dispatch shape, timing phases, hardware path all match), they just fail the claim gate on Doe's direction for two of three. Promoting captures the regression publicly as a `comparable=true, claimStatus!=claimable` row rather than hiding it behind `comparable=false`. Clean-wins are straightforward -- 4 rows that pass both comparability and claim gates move to the comparable cohort.

Each promotion carries a `comparabilityNotes` entry naming the evidence delta and the audit date; the stale `directionalReason` is removed. For `compute_concurrent_execution_single`, the pre-existing explicit `benchmarkClass: "directional"` override was also cleared so the generator correctly derives `benchmarkClass: "comparable"` from `comparable: true`.

**11 suspicious-100% rows kept directional with a sharper reason.** The triage tool classified these as promotion candidates (all blocking obligations pass), but their p50 delta saturates at ~100% -- which indicates Dawn-side timing reports near-zero while Doe reports material time. That is an instrumentation-parity problem, not a runtime win. Their `directionalReason` now reads:

> "p50 delta saturates at ~100% on AMD Vulkan explore 2026-04-12, indicating Dawn-side timing reports near-zero while Doe reports material time; this is an instrumentation-parity question, not a runtime win. Promote only after the timing-zero side is audited."

Workloads in this bucket: `compute_dispatch_fallback`, `compute_dispatch_grid`, `compute_dispatch_indirect_large_args`, `compute_dispatch_indirect_live_args`, `compute_dispatch_indirect_single`, `compute_dispatch_workgroups_2d_sweep`, `compute_dispatch_workgroups_3d_sweep`, `compute_dispatch_workgroups_indirect_pipeline_switch`, `compute_indirect_timestamp`, `compute_kernel_dispatch_1000`, `compute_zero_initialize_workgroup_memory_256`.

**6 non-comparable workloads removed from AMD Vulkan `governed` cohort.** `config/backend-workload-cohorts.json` previously listed 13 non-comparable workloads under `profiles.amd_vulkan.governed`, violating the invariant checked by `test_governed_rows_are_comparable_for_all_profiles`. After the 7 promotions above, 6 workloads remained non-comparable in governed; they were demoted to `exploration`-only membership via removal from the governed list:

- `compute_dispatch_fallback`, `compute_dispatch_grid` -- suspicious 100% delta, not promoted
- `copy_buffer_to_texture`, `copy_protocol`, `copy_texture_to_texture` -- baseline execution errors / timing-phase asymmetry per their directional reasons
- `surface_full_presentation` -- coverage gap (no matching artifact in the explore corpus)

**Workload-overlap-map artifact regenerated** to match the updated catalog (`bench/tools/generate_workload_overlap_map.py`).

### Test impact

Two pre-existing failures recovered; session baseline went from 7 failures + 6 errors at morning-start to **6 failures + 6 errors** now.

- `test_governed_rows_are_comparable_for_all_profiles` -- recovered. The governed invariant now holds across all three native backends: every governed row is `comparable: true`.
- `test_overlap_artifact_matches_generator_output` -- recovered after regenerating the overlap artifact.
- Six remaining failures are all pre-existing schema-drift and Node/Dawn-note issues that are unrelated to this push.

| --- | ---: | ---: | ---: |
| Apple Metal | 38 | 38 | 0 |
| AMD Vulkan | **9** | **16** | 0 |
| Local D3D12 | 13 | 13 | 0 |

AMD Vulkan comparable cohort grew 78% in one day through the audit alone -- no runtime change required. The remaining Vulkan breadth growth is the 11 suspicious-100% rows (needs timing instrumentation audit) and promotion of `compute_workgroup_*` / `pipeline_compile_stress` into the `governed` cohort after a comparable-lane re-run validates the deltas under the new pipeline cache.

### What this does not do

- Does not promote the 11 suspicious-100% rows. Those need an instrumentation-parity audit (why is Dawn reporting near-zero timing?) before promotion is defensible.
- Does not add the newly-promoted 7 rows back into the AMD Vulkan `governed` cohort. They are `comparable=true` in the contract but stay out of `governed` until the matvec regression resolves and the workgroup / pipeline_compile_stress deltas are re-validated under the new Vulkan pipeline cache. The goal is not to inflate governed; the goal is to keep governed = claim-release-eligible.
- Does not run the comparability-obligation-parity gate against any of the newly-promoted rows. That gate runs at bench execution time; the catalog contract is a precondition.

## Push: Doe Vulkan persistent VkPipelineCache lands (2026-04-17 UTC)

Steps 1-4 of `bench/docs/vulkan-pipeline-cache-integration.md` shipped. Doe's Vulkan backend now creates a real `VkPipelineCache` at device bring-up and threads its handle through every `vkCreateComputePipelines` / `vkCreateGraphicsPipelines` call instead of `VK_NULL_U64`. The `--no-pipeline-cache` CLI flag, which previously only affected Metal, now also disables the Vulkan cache. Trace meta carries the new state on Vulkan runs.

### Files changed

- `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_structs.zig` тАФ new `VkPipelineCacheCreateInfo` extern struct
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_functions.zig` тАФ new externs for `vkCreatePipelineCache`, `vkDestroyPipelineCache`, `vkGetPipelineCacheData`
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_constants.zig` тАФ re-exports + `VK_STRUCTURE_TYPE_PIPELINE_CACHE_CREATE_INFO = 17`
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_pipeline_cache_persistent.zig` (new, 120 LoC) тАФ process-level cache module mirroring the Metal shape (`set_process_pipeline_cache_disabled`, `create_process_pipeline_cache`, `destroy_process_pipeline_cache`, `handle_for_pipeline_creation`, `process_active_cache_present`, `process_active_cache_warmup_telemetry`). Includes 2 inline unit tests for the disabled-flag and default-state paths.
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_device.zig` тАФ creates the cache after `vkCreateDevice`. Failures are non-fatal (cache falls back to `VK_NULL_U64` and pipeline creation continues as before).
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/native_runtime.zig` тАФ destroys the cache before `vkDestroyDevice`.
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_pipeline.zig:385` тАФ compute pipeline creation now reads the handle from `handle_for_pipeline_creation()`.
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_render_pipeline.zig:457` тАФ graphics pipeline creation same.
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/mod.zig` тАФ exposes `set_pipeline_cache_disabled`, `pipeline_cache_active_from_context`, `pipeline_cache_warmup_telemetry_from_context` to the cross-platform wrapper.
- `runtime/zig/src/backend/backend_runtime_telemetry.zig` тАФ new `set_vulkan_pipeline_cache_disabled` wrapper (Linux-only; no-op elsewhere), Vulkan branch of `refresh()` now populates `pipeline_cache_warmup_count`, `pipeline_cache_warmup_ns`, `pipeline_cache_active`.
- `runtime/zig/src/cli/runtime_cli.zig` тАФ calls both the Metal and Vulkan wrappers before `ExecutionContext.init` on the `--no-pipeline-cache` flag.
- `runtime/zig/src/trace.zig` тАФ widened the `pipelineCache.reason` derivation: `platform-unsupported` now only applies to builds without Doe cache support (was: any non-Mac build), so Vulkan builds on Linux now correctly emit `default` / `cli-flag` / `non-doe-backend` reasons.

### Smoke verification on AMD Vulkan

Two runs of the `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` workload with `doe-zig-runtime` on this host:

```
--execute                         -> pipelineCache: {state="enabled",  reason="default",  warmupCount=1, warmupNs=1132}
--execute --no-pipeline-cache     -> pipelineCache: {state="disabled", reason="cli-flag",  warmupCount=0, warmupNs=0}
```

Cache init cost is ~1╬╝s (the 1132ns `warmupNs`). The Vulkan cache is created once per device bring-up. The `executionBackend` field correctly reports `doe_vulkan` and `executionDispatchCount: 100` confirms the full matvec dispatch ran.

On the matvec workload specifically, a 5x5 wall-time A/B shows no visible delta between cache-on and cache-off (both ~3.0s median) -- expected because matvec creates the pipeline once in setup and the cache only affects that one compile, which is dwarfed by 100 dispatches of actual matvec work. The cache contribution will be visible on `pipeline_compile_stress` (pipelines created in the timed loop), cross-process warm runs (if persistence lands), and on workloads with many distinct pipelines.

### Test status

- `zig build` -- exit 0.
- `zig build test` -- exit 0 (warnings are from the pre-existing Mac-backend test stubs that don't apply on Linux).
- `python3 runtime/zig/tools/check_core_import_fence.py` -- exit 0. The `cli/ -> backend/` import fence stays clean via `backend_runtime_telemetry.set_vulkan_pipeline_cache_disabled`.
- `python3 -m unittest discover -s bench/tests -t .` -- 739 tests, 7 failures + 6 errors + 47 skipped (same baseline as the morning's directional-reasons push).

### What this push did not do

- Did not add disk-backed persistence. The cache is in-memory for the process lifetime only. Disk read/write via `vkGetPipelineCacheData` + file I/O is a separate follow-up per the integration doc's Steps 5-6.
- Did not add executor templates `doe_direct_vulkan_no_cache` / `doe_direct_vulkan_cache`. The existing default now uses the cache; the no-cache lane still lives under the shared `--no-pipeline-cache` flag. Dedicated executor pairing lands with the cache-contribution lane promotion.
- Did not add a `trace_meta.pipelineCache.backend` field. The integration doc recommends adding it so a reader can disambiguate Metal / Vulkan / D3D12 cache reporters; deferred to the trace schema follow-up.
- Did not run the matvec re-compare against Dawn. That needs `bench/cli.py compare` on AMD Vulkan, which the user will drive.
- Did not add disk-cache UUID validation. The follow-up disk-persistence push handles header-UUID mismatch by silently discarding the blob and recreating from scratch; the in-memory cache does not need this.

### What this unblocks for the "Doe faster across all boards" program

- Any workload that creates pipelines in the timed loop (`pipeline_compile_stress` and the async-pipeline-diagnostics family) now runs on a symmetric cache basis with Dawn's Vulkan backend. Doe's +48% on `pipeline_compile_stress` today is despite the missing cache; with cache parity, the delta either widens (runtime win compounds) or holds (runtime win absorbs cache cost).
- The `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` regression hypothesis #1 (cold-compile cost) can now be falsified: if re-running matvec on AMD Vulkan still shows Doe -38%, the cold-compile cost is not the cause and hypothesis #2 (wave-size) or #3 (command-stream) is the next candidate.
- Linux is no longer the backend with Doe-disadvantage at the cache layer. Metal still needs the Dawn-cache shim to become symmetric (that program has its own follow-up queue). D3D12 stays asymmetric until `CachedPSO` persistence lands; Windows host required for runtime validation.

### Follow-up queue

1. Disk-backed persistence for the Vulkan cache (`vkGetPipelineCacheData` + atomic write + UUID-validated reload).
2. `trace_meta.pipelineCache.backend` field + reader update.
3. `doe_direct_vulkan_no_cache` / `doe_direct_vulkan_cache` executor templates; register the cache-contribution lane for Vulkan in `bench/docs/pipeline-cache-contribution-lane.md`.
4. Re-run the full AMD Vulkan explore preset with the new cache; refresh the triage + promotion audit accordingly.
5. Mirror the design on D3D12 `CachedPSO` once a Windows host is available.

## Push: matvec regression trace + Doe Vulkan pipeline-cache integration design (2026-04-17 UTC)

Two follow-ups from the promotion audit landed as research docs. Both produce concrete follow-up queues for future runtime-engineering pushes.

### `bench/docs/compute-matvec-regression-trace.md` (new)

Static trace of the `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` AMD Vulkan regression (Doe -38.6% on the naive-swizzle0 variant, -3.9% on swizzle1, +11.5% on workgroupshared_swizzle1).

Confirmed: shader algorithm matches Dawn's reference (same memory access pattern, same dispatch geometry, same workgroup_size=64). Doe's tracked SPIR-V is *smaller* than what Tint generates for the same WGSL (3476 vs 3968 bytes), so codegen bloat is ruled out. Per-dispatch descriptor rework is short-circuited by the bindings hash (`vk_pipeline.zig:518`), and pipeline recreation is short-circuited by the pipeline hash (`vk_pipeline.zig:325`). Neither is a source of overhead in the 100-dispatch loop.

Three hypotheses to profile on AMD hardware, ranked by plausibility:

1. First-dispatch pipeline creation cost on cold Vulkan cache. Doe passes `VK_NULL_U64` to `vkCreateComputePipelines`; Dawn uses a persistent `VkPipelineCache`. This is the strongest candidate and is addressable without profiling via the parallel Vulkan cache integration below.
2. Wavefront size mismatch against RDNA3. RADV picks wave32 vs wave64 based on shader metadata; Tint-emitted vs Doe-tracked SPIR-V may carry different subgroup hints.
3. Redundant barriers or binding rebinds in Doe's command-stream encoder between dispatches that Dawn elides.

Ruled out: Doe SPIR-V bloat, dispatch-geometry mismatch, per-dispatch descriptor rebind, per-dispatch pipeline recreation.

Next concrete step: land the Doe Vulkan pipeline cache (below), re-run matvec compare, see if hypothesis 1 is confirmed. If not, capture RGP trace on AMD host.

### `bench/docs/vulkan-pipeline-cache-integration.md` (new)

Integration design for Doe-side persistent `VkPipelineCache`. Mirrors the shape of `bench/docs/dawn-delegate-cache-integration.md` but for the Vulkan program rather than the Metal program:

- FFI additions for `vkCreatePipelineCache` / `vkDestroyPipelineCache` / `vkGetPipelineCacheData` plus `VkPipelineCacheCreateInfo` and `VK_STRUCTURE_TYPE_PIPELINE_CACHE_CREATE_INFO`.
- New `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_pipeline_cache_persistent.zig` module (not to be confused with the existing `vk_pipeline_cache.zig` which is an in-memory per-device state cache).
- Pipeline-creation callsite change: replace `VK_NULL_U64` at `vk_pipeline.zig:385` and `vk_render_pipeline.zig:457` with the persistent handle.
- Header UUID validation against device vendorID / deviceID / cache-UUID per Vulkan spec (mismatched blobs must be rejected silently, not crash device init).
- Extension of `--no-pipeline-cache` to Vulkan (currently a no-op there), and a new `--pipeline-cache-dir` knob.
- `trace_meta.pipelineCache.backend` field added to distinguish Metal / Vulkan / D3D12 cache reporters without separate payloads.
- `doe_direct_vulkan_no_cache` / `doe_direct_vulkan_cache` executor templates mirroring the G18 Metal pattern.
- Expected impact on "Doe faster across all boards": `pipeline_compile_stress` (+48% today on Vulkan despite no Doe cache) should widen; `compute_matvec_*` regression may resolve if hypothesis 1 is right; upload workloads unaffected.

Linux-executable end-to-end (AMD Vulkan hardware on this host). No Mac hardware dependency like the Metal Dawn shim has.

### Why both are docs-only today

Adding unused FFI declarations violates the repo convention that every FFI extern is referenced in the backend tree (verified by grep: all 93 extern functions in `vk_functions.zig` are used). CLAUDE.md non-negotiable #2 also forbids runtime-behavior placeholders in the execution path. Partial implementation would require either placeholder code or FFI surface that sits unused, neither of which is acceptable. The tracked Step 1-4 landing (as named in the integration doc's follow-up queue) is a focused multi-file push that adds FFI + module + callsite changes together.

### Test status

- `python3 -m unittest discover -s bench/tests -t .` -- 739 tests, 7 failures + 6 errors + 47 skipped (same as the directional-reasons push earlier today).
- No runtime code changes; the existing Vulkan test suite is unaffected.

### Follow-up queue

1. Steps 1-4 of the Vulkan pipeline-cache integration (FFI + module + cross-platform wrapper + callsite change). Single focused push. Linux-buildable + testable on AMD Vulkan hardware this host has.
2. Steps 5-7 (CLI flag extension + trace schema + executor templates). Follow-up push after the core wiring lands.
3. Re-run matvec compare and `pipeline_compile_stress` compare after the cache lands; document deltas in a status entry.
4. Land D3D12 `CachedPSO` persistence in parallel once a Windows host is in rotation.

## Push: fill directional reasons across all three native backends (2026-04-17 UTC)

The promotion audit landed earlier today quantified the backlog: 75 / 26 / 41 directional workloads with empty `directionalReason` on AMD Vulkan / Apple Metal / Local D3D12. This push closes that backlog to zero everywhere without promoting any workload.

### What landed

**`bench/tools/audit_comparability_promotion.py` (new).** A reusable triage tool that:

1. Takes a per-backend workload catalog path + a glob of recent compare artifact JSONs.
2. For each `comparable: false` row with empty `directionalReason`, reads the matching workload from the compare artifact's `obligations` list.
3. Classifies the row as one of:
   - **promotion candidate** -- every blocking obligation passes except `workload_marked_comparable` itself. Nothing technically blocks promotion; pending product-meaning audit before flipping `comparable=true`.
   - **directional with derived reason** -- at least one other blocking obligation fails; derived reason is built from the failed obligation ids plus any `details.comparisonReason` field.
   - **inconclusive** -- no matching compare artifact in the glob (coverage gap).
4. When `--write-reasons` is set with a canonical catalog path + source lane id, applies derived reasons to the canonical catalog (the per-backend files are generator output).

**Canonical catalog updated.** `bench/workloads/metadata/backend-workload-catalog.json` now carries `directionalReason` on the lane override for every directional-with-empty-reason row across the three lanes `amd_vulkan_superset_native_supported`, `apple_metal_extended`, `local_d3d12_extended`. Reasons fall into three shapes:

- technical obligation failure text (e.g., "execution shape (dispatch/row/success counts) differs; baseline execution unsuccessful on some samples; row/success shape sets differ")
- promotion-candidate note (e.g., "promotion candidate: every blocking comparability obligation passes against bench/out/amd-vulkan/explore/20260412T161500Z/compute_workgroup_atomic_1024.compare.json; pending product-meaning audit before flipping comparable=true")
- coverage gap note (e.g., "coverage gap: no matching compare artifact in the latest triaged corpus (bench/out/local-d3d12/**/*.compare.json); re-run the explore preset to produce an artifact before triage")

**Regenerated per-backend catalogs.** `python3 bench/tools/generate_backend_workloads.py` regenerated `workloads.amd.vulkan.json`, `workloads.apple.metal.json`, `workloads.local.d3d12.json` and their smoke siblings from the updated canonical catalog; `generate_backend_workloads.py --verify` now exits clean.

### Before / after

| Backend | Comparable | Directional with reason | Directional with empty reason |
| --- | ---: | ---: | ---: |
| Apple Metal (before) | 38 | 32 | 26 |
| Apple Metal (after) | 38 | 58 | 0 |
| AMD Vulkan (before) | 9 | 0 | 75 |
| AMD Vulkan (after) | 9 | 75 | 0 |
| Local D3D12 (before) | 13 | 0 | 41 |
| Local D3D12 (after) | 13 | 41 | 0 |

Zero empty-reason directionals across all three native backends.

### Promotion candidates surfaced (not yet promoted)

The audit identified 18 AMD Vulkan workloads where every blocking obligation passes. These are not yet promoted to `comparable=true` -- that is an explicit human step, not an automation -- but the workloads now carry a clear "promotion candidate" reason pointing at the evidence artifact. Notable entries:

- `pipeline_compile_stress` (+48.25% Doe, cache-relevant)
- `compute_workgroup_atomic_1024` (+48.35% Doe)
- `compute_workgroup_non_atomic_1024` (+47.21% Doe)
- `compute_concurrent_execution_single` (+14.92% Doe)
- `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` (-38.62% Doe -- promotion-eligible, but not claim-eligible; runtime regression lead)
- 13 other compute / dispatch rows

Apple Metal produced 0 new promotion candidates because all 38 comparable rows are already promoted; the remaining directional rows have real obligation failures recorded.

### Test status

- `python3 -m unittest discover -s bench/tests -t .` -- **739 tests, 7 failures + 6 errors + 47 skipped**. One failure recovered vs the pre-push baseline of 8 (the D3D12 generated-view catalog-match test) because regenerating the per-backend files from the canonical catalog cleared a drift introduced by a previous hand-edit.
- `python3 bench/tools/generate_backend_workloads.py --verify` -- exits clean, no drift.

### Pre-existing failure the audit makes more visible

`test_backend_workload_catalog.py::test_governed_rows_are_comparable_for_all_profiles` continues to fail at `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32 must be comparable in the governed cohort for amd_vulkan`. This is a contract violation that predates today's work: 13 AMD Vulkan rows sit in the `governed` cohort but are not `comparable=true`. The options are either to promote the cleanly-passing ones (7 rows) to comparable=true and remove the rest from the governed cohort, or demote everything non-comparable out of governed. That cohort-reshape is a separate push deliberately -- it mixes promotion decisions with cohort policy, and both need explicit product decisions.

The two other native backends (Apple Metal, Local D3D12) have zero non-comparable governed rows; the invariant violation is AMD-Vulkan-specific.

### What this push does not do

- Does not promote any workload to `comparable=true`. All 18 AMD Vulkan promotion candidates remain `comparable=false` with an explicit "promotion candidate" reason pointing at the evidence artifact.
- Does not reshape the `governed` cohort on AMD Vulkan. The 13-row invariant violation stays as a separate tracked follow-up.
- Does not address the `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` runtime regression. That is a separate runtime-engineering track.

## Push: pipeline-cache contribution lane + comparability promotion audit (2026-04-17 UTC)

Two coordinated docs landed together. The pipeline-cache contribution lane documents the Doe-vs-Doe diagnostic (cache off vs cache on, same runtime, same hardware) as its own first-class taxonomy entry distinct from Doe-vs-Dawn fair-cold and fair-warm lanes. The comparability promotion audit quantifies where breadth is actually bottlenecked across the three native backends.

### A -- Pipeline-cache contribution lane

`bench/docs/pipeline-cache-contribution-lane.md` (new). Defines the Doe-vs-Doe lane: baseline Doe `--no-pipeline-cache` vs comparison Doe cache-active, same workload, same hardware. The lane is explicitly diagnostic-grade, not claim-grade, and is distinct from:

- Doe-vs-Dawn fair-cold (current Metal default; both sides cache-disabled) -- claim-eligible
- Doe-vs-Dawn fair-warm (future Metal, once Dawn shim lands; both sides cache-enabled) -- claim-eligible

Per-backend applicability: Apple Metal is available today via `doe_direct_metal` (cache off) + `doe_direct_metal_cache` (cache on) executor templates already in `bench/native_compare_modules/executor_registry.py`. AMD Vulkan and Local D3D12 lanes land when Doe-side caching lands on those backends.

The doc pins what the cache actually covers (driver-level IR->GPU-ISA compile plus PSO finalization) vs what it does not (WGSL parsing, Tint translation, runtime execution, descriptor-set updates), and names the workload-shape heuristic for where the delta lands (setup_ns for one-time-pipeline-creation workloads; main-phase timing for `pipeline_compile_stress` and similar).

### B -- Comparability promotion audit

`bench/docs/comparability-promotion-audit.md` (new). Cross-backend maturity snapshot pulled from the tracked workload catalogs on 2026-04-17:

| Backend | Total | `comparable=true` | `governed` cohort | Directional (no reason) | Directional (with reason) |
| --- | ---: | ---: | ---: | ---: | ---: |
| Apple Metal | 96 | 38 | 27 | 26 | 32 |
| AMD Vulkan | 84 | 9 | 17 | 75 | 0 |
| Local D3D12 | 54 | 13 | 11 | 41 | 0 |

Finding: "Doe faster than Dawn across all boards" is not bottlenecked by runtime quality on AMD Vulkan or D3D12. It is bottlenecked by a process gap -- the vast majority of directional workloads on those backends have no stated `directionalReason`, meaning no audit has decided whether they can be promoted to `comparable=true` or whether they are legitimately directional-only.

All 75 AMD Vulkan directional workloads and all 41 Local D3D12 directional workloads carry empty `directionalReason` fields. The existing `explore` corpus artifacts show both Doe and Dawn executing these workloads, so this is an audit-promotion backlog, not a runtime-execution issue.

First-pass promotion candidates on AMD Vulkan (heuristic match against `bench/out/amd-vulkan/explore/20260412T161500Z/` -- not pre-cleared, just starting points for the actual audit):

- `compute_workgroup_atomic_1024` -- Doe +48.35%
- `compute_workgroup_non_atomic_1024` -- Doe +47.21%
- `compute_concurrent_execution_single` -- Doe +14.92%
- `pipeline_compile_stress` -- Doe +48.25% (cache-relevant; would benefit most from Doe Vulkan caching landing)
- `render_bundle_dynamic_pipeline_bindings_200k` -- Doe +65.50%
- `render_draw_redundant_pipeline_bindings_200k` -- Doe +26.00%

Runtime-engineering lead (not a contract issue): `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` shows Doe -38.6% slower, `_swizzle1` shows -3.9% slower, `_workgroupshared_swizzle1` shows +11.5%. The matvec regression is in Doe's expected strong area (compute-heavy, cache-irrelevant) and deserves a dedicated trace.

Rough sizing of the promotion work: ~30-40 engineer-hours on AMD Vulkan, ~20-25 engineer-hours on Local D3D12 (gated on Windows host), ~10 engineer-hours to fill the 26 Apple Metal directional rows with stated reasons. Largest single-lever Linux-executable breadth work available today.

### Strategic framing

Before this audit, the implicit plan for "Doe faster than Dawn across all boards" was running to land the Metal Dawn-cache shim plus Doe Vulkan/D3D12 caching. Those are both real programs, but the Linux-executable breadth work ahead of them is the promotion audit -- most of the corpus on Vulkan and D3D12 is not in the comparable contract, and no runtime change will unlock it. Audit first, runtime-engineering second.

### Test status

- Docs-only push on the Python side; `python3 -m unittest discover -s bench/tests -t .` remains at 739 tests, 8 failures + 6 errors + 47 skipped (same pre-push baseline).
- No schema changes, no runtime changes, no test changes.

### Follow-up queue

1. Run the AMD Vulkan promotion audit on the listed first-pass candidates. Writes decisions into `bench/workloads/workloads.amd.vulkan.json` per row. Largest single strategic win.
2. Trace the `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32` regression -- runtime-engineering follow-up, separate track from the audit.
3. Fill empty `directionalReason` on the 26 Apple Metal directional rows (contract-only cleanup).
4. Local D3D12 promotion audit once a Windows host is in rotation.

## Push: three-backend pipeline-cache audit тАФ asymmetry reverses on Vulkan and D3D12 (2026-04-16 UTC)

Source-level audit of Doe's and Dawn's pipeline caching across Metal / Vulkan / D3D12 backends, motivated by scoping "Doe faster than Dawn across all boards". The audit changes the strategic framing: the fair-warm Dawn-cache shim work (Push 4 design) is Metal-only. On Vulkan and D3D12 the asymmetry reverses -- Dawn caches, Doe does not -- and the corrective work there is to give Doe a cache, not Dawn.

### What landed

**`bench/docs/pipeline-cache-backend-audit.md` (new).**

Per-backend findings:

- **Metal.** Doe opens `MTLBinaryArchive` at `runtime/zig/src/backend/metal/metal_native_runtime.zig:380-402` when `HAS_PIPELINE_CACHE` (macOS 11+) and `--no-pipeline-cache` is not passed. Dawn delegate path does not. Fair-cold currently enforced on both sides; fair-warm requires the Push 4 shim.
- **Vulkan.** Doe passes `VK_NULL_U64` (VK_NULL_HANDLE) as the `pipelineCache` arg to every `vkCreateComputePipelines` / `vkCreateGraphicsPipelines` call (`runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_pipeline.zig:385`, `vk_render_pipeline.zig:457`). The misleadingly-named `vk_pipeline_cache.zig` is an in-memory descriptor-state cache, not a persistent VkPipelineCache. Dawn's Vulkan backend implements `PipelineCacheVk` (`bench/vendor/dawn/src/dawn/native/vulkan/PipelineCacheVk.{h,cpp}`) and uses it on the delegate path.
- **D3D12.** Doe's `d3d12_bridge.c:174-192` (compute) and `:820`/`:930` (graphics) pipeline creation paths zero-initialize the pipeline state descriptor and never populate `CachedPSO.pCachedBlob`. Dawn's D3D12 backend populates `CachedPSO.pCachedBlob` / `.CachedBlobSizeInBytes` in `ComputePipelineD3D12.cpp:103-104` and `RenderPipelineD3D12.cpp:449` when a cached blob is available.

Direction summary:

| Backend | Doe cache | Dawn cache |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Metal | `MTLBinaryArchive` (bench-manifest-specific) | none in Doe's delegate path |
| Vulkan | `VK_NULL_U64` -- no cache | `PipelineCacheVk` active |
| D3D12 | No `CachedPSO` set | `CachedPSO.pCachedBlob` populated when available |

### Strategic implications

"Doe faster than Dawn across all boards" is two independent programs, not one:

1. **Metal -- Dawn catches up.** The integration plan in `bench/docs/dawn-delegate-cache-integration.md` promotes Doe's existing Metal cache wins from diagnostic to claim-grade. Build machinery already proven buildable on Linux (see `bench/tools/regenerate_dawn_component_build.py`).
2. **Vulkan + D3D12 -- Doe catches up.** Implement persistent pipeline caching in Doe's Vulkan and D3D12 backends. Independent of the Metal shim and independent of Dawn.

The existing AMD Vulkan claimable evidence survives this audit. Every current AMD Vulkan Doe-vs-Dawn compare is running strictly cache-disadvantaged on the Doe side, so Doe wins observed today are runtime-engineering wins despite the cache gap. Adding Doe-side Vulkan / D3D12 caching can only remove a hidden disadvantage; it cannot invalidate existing wins.

### Why this is a finding, not a push

No runtime code changes in this push. The audit documents what is, not what should be. Implementation of Doe Vulkan `VkPipelineCache` and Doe D3D12 `CachedPSO` persistence are two separate follow-up pushes enumerated at the end of the audit doc. Both are Linux-executable on the Zig + bridge side (Vulkan has hardware locally; D3D12 needs a Windows host for runtime validation but Linux builds stay green).

### Test status

- `python3 -m unittest discover -s bench/tests -t .` -- 739 tests, 8 failures + 6 errors + 47 skipped (same pre-push baseline; docs-only push).
- The audit's source-line references were verified by direct `grep` / file inspection; no build or symbol check was required.

### Follow-up queue

1. Implement Doe Vulkan persistent `VkPipelineCache` with CLI flag + trace_meta schema slot parallel to Metal's.
2. Implement Doe D3D12 `CachedPSO` persistence with the same CLI + schema pattern.
3. Complete the Metal Dawn-cache shim (ongoing, has its own follow-up queue in `bench/docs/dawn-delegate-cache-integration.md`).
4. Re-run AMD Vulkan + D3D12 compare lanes under the new caches to confirm Doe's wins remain or grow.

## Push: Dawn component-build durability тАФ tracked regenerator script (2026-04-16 UTC)

Closes the "make the rebuild contract durable" item on the Dawn cache integration follow-up queue. The ComponentTest build directory is gitignored via `bench/vendor/` (so the `.so` artifacts stay ephemeral), but the build *contract* -- the `args.gn` contents, the target list, and the expected-symbol invariants -- now lives in a tracked Python tool under `bench/tools/`.

### What landed

**`bench/tools/regenerate_dawn_component_build.py` (new).**
- Writes the canonical `args.gn` into `bench/vendor/dawn/out/ComponentTest/` (or the `--out-name` override) and runs `gn gen`.
- `--build` runs `ninja` for `src/dawn/platform:shared` and `src/dawn/native:shared`, producing `libdawn_platform.so` and `libdawn_native.so` with the C++ surface exposed.
- `--verify` checks the built `.so` files for a required-symbol whitelist: `dawn::platform::Platform::Platform()`, `~Platform()`, `GetCachingInterface()`, `dawn::platform::CachingInterface::CachingInterface()`, `~CachingInterface()`, `dawn::native::DawnInstanceDescriptor::DawnInstanceDescriptor()`, `dawn::native::Instance::SetPlatformForTesting(dawn::platform::Platform*)`. Missing symbols return exit code 2 with a per-symbol reason.
- `--summary-out` emits a JSON summary with `argsGnPath`, `buildDir`, `gnGenOk`, `builtTargets`, and `missingSymbols` for audit / CI use.
- The canonical `args.gn` contents live as a single `CANONICAL_ARGS_GN` constant in the script, so any future change to the build-config contract is a one-place edit.

**Default invocation semantics.**
- `python3 bench/tools/regenerate_dawn_component_build.py` тАФ rewrite `args.gn`, run `gn gen`, exit 0 if successful. No compile work; safe to run at any time.
- `python3 bench/tools/regenerate_dawn_component_build.py --build --verify` тАФ end-to-end rebuild + symbol verification. ~13 minutes on a warm libc++ cache, longer on a cold build.

### Why it is in `bench/tools/` rather than elsewhere

`bench/vendor/` is fully gitignored -- nothing inside it can be committed, so the build config cannot live as a vendored args file. `bench/tools/` is the canonical home for repo-only Python tooling (precedent: `bootstrap_dawn.py`, `cts_baseline_*.py`, `build_claim_rehearsal_artifacts.py`, etc.). That directory is tracked, follows `bench/STYLE.md`, and is invoked by other tooling without path gymnastics.

### What this does not do

- Does not run the rebuild automatically. The expensive build step (`--build`) stays opt-in; a CI hook that invokes it is a separate follow-up.
- Does not land the tracked Step 1 shim. `bench/vendor/dawn/out/ComponentTest/dawn_cache_shim_skeleton.cpp` remains the compile-check skeleton only; the real shim lands with `dawn_cache.zig`, `--dawn-cache-dir`, and `TraceRunSummary.dawnPipelineCache` as a single change.

### Test status

- `python3 -m unittest discover -s bench/tests -t .` -- 739 tests, 8 failures + 6 errors + 47 skipped (same pre-push baseline; the new script is tool code with no test dependencies introduced).
- `python3 bench/tools/regenerate_dawn_component_build.py --verify` against the already-built ComponentTest `.so` files -- exit 0, "symbol verify: all required symbols exported".

## Push: Dawn libdawn_native.so + shim skeleton тАФ Step 1 proven buildable on Linux (2026-04-16 UTC)

Extension of the component-build push above. With `libdawn_platform.so` already proved, the full pair of shared libraries the shim needs plus a compile-check of the shim skeleton itself now exist on Linux.

### libdawn_native.so built

`ninja -C bench/vendor/dawn/out/ComponentTest src/dawn/native:shared` completed 1158/1158 steps (the libc++ rebuild from the prior push is cached, so the native delta was smaller than the fresh-build estimate) and produced:

```
bench/vendor/dawn/out/ComponentTest/libdawn_native.so  (11,915,168 bytes)
```

`nm -D --defined-only | c++filt` confirms the full Step 1 surface:

- `dawn::native::DawnInstanceDescriptor::DawnInstanceDescriptor()` тАФ the chained-descriptor constructor the shim needs
- `dawn::native::Instance::Instance(WGPUInstanceDescriptor const*)` and the `wgpu::InstanceDescriptor` / `InstanceBase*` overloads
- `dawn::native::Instance::SetPlatformForTesting(dawn::platform::Platform*)` тАФ fallback platform-injection hook
- `dawn::native::InstanceProcessEvents(WGPUInstanceImpl*)` тАФ event-pumping surface

### Shim proof-of-build

A compile-check skeleton at `bench/vendor/dawn/out/ComponentTest/dawn_cache_shim_skeleton.cpp` (gitignored, local-only) was authored. It subclasses `dawn::platform::CachingInterface` and `dawn::platform::Platform`, exposes four `extern "C"` entry points (`doe_dawn_install_persistent_cache`, `doe_dawn_teardown_persistent_cache`, `doe_dawn_get_platform_ptr`, `doe_dawn_cache_entry_count`), and was verified by:

- compile against the Dawn headers plus the generated `gen/include/` tree (clang 23 bundled with Dawn, `-std=c++20 -fPIC -fvisibility=hidden`)
- link as a shared library against `libdawn_platform.so` тАФ all four C ABI entry points export as `T`, all required `dawn::platform::*` references resolve through the `.so`
- `nm -D` inspection confirms the shim's ABI is exactly the four C functions and nothing else

Exact compile / link commands and the header-include quirk (the generated `gen/include/` path is required because `DawnPlatform.h` transitively pulls in `webgpu.h`) are documented in `bench/docs/dawn-delegate-cache-integration.md` under the new "Shim proof-of-build (2026-04-16)" section.

### Why the skeleton is not tracked in runtime/zig/

CLAUDE.md non-negotiable #2: "runtime behavior placeholders are not allowed in Zig execution paths; implement fully or fail with explicit unsupported taxonomy." The skeleton's `LoadData` / `StoreData` are no-ops. It lives under `bench/vendor/dawn/out/ComponentTest/` (gitignored via the `bench/vendor/` wildcard) as a compile-check artifact, not as a tracked runtime component. The tracked Step 1 landing implements real file-backed persistence and wires the shim into `dawn_cache.zig` + `cli/runtime_cli.zig` in a single push; this push's role is to prove that push is buildable.

### What is now proven on Linux

1. Dawn can be rebuilt with exposed C++ visibility on this host (`is_component_build = true` + `use_custom_libcxx = true`).
2. Both `libdawn_platform.so` and `libdawn_native.so` export the full surface the integration plan needs.
3. A shim compiled against Dawn's headers links cleanly against those shared libraries.
4. The shim's C ABI is the only externally visible surface, which is what Doe's Zig FFI will call.

### Remaining Step 0 / Step 1 work

- durability: vendor the ComponentTest args.gn at a tracked path, or add a repo-only regenerator script, so the build contract does not rely on ad-hoc operator steps
- Step 1 proper: implement real file-backed `LoadData` / `StoreData`, wire `dawn_cache.zig` + `cli/runtime_cli.zig`, land the `--dawn-cache-dir` CLI flag with typed unsupported taxonomy for builds without the shim, and extend `TraceRunSummary` with `dawnPipelineCache.{state, reason, entryCount}`
- Mac verification: re-run the component build on `mac.lan` to confirm whether `use_custom_libcxx = true` is needed there (Apple toolchain default sysroots may already ship libc++ with `atomic::wait`)

## Push: Dawn component-build Linux proof-of-build тАФ libdawn_platform.so links with exported C++ symbols (2026-04-16 UTC)

Extension of the earlier Dawn verification push. After confirming the default vendored `libwebgpu_dawn.so` hides all C++ symbols, a Linux rebuild under `bench/vendor/dawn/out/ComponentTest/` proved the integration plan's Step 0 is achievable on this host.

### Build args and attempt sequence

First attempt (`use_custom_libcxx = false`, the conservative default) reached 254/258 steps before `src/dawn/platform/WorkerThread.cpp` failed to compile with `error: no member named 'wait' in 'std::atomic<bool>'`. Root cause: Dawn's bundled Debian bullseye sysroot at `bench/vendor/dawn/build/linux/debian_bullseye_amd64-sysroot/usr/include/c++/10/atomic` ships libstdc++ 10, which does not implement C++20 `atomic::wait` / `notify_all` (added in libstdc++ 11). Dawn's bundled clang 23 supports `-std=c++20` but uses the sysroot's stdlib.

Second attempt with the full args:

```
is_debug = false
is_component_build = true
dawn_complete_static_libs = false
use_custom_libcxx = true
dawn_use_swiftshader = false
angle_enable_swiftshader = false
```

completed 1451/1451 steps in ~13 minutes. The extra ~1200 steps are Chromium's in-tree libc++ / libc++abi rebuild, which implements `atomic::wait`.

### Build product and symbol verification

```
bench/vendor/dawn/out/ComponentTest/libdawn_platform.so  (37,648 bytes)
```

`nm -D --defined-only | c++filt` confirms every C++ symbol the shim needs is exported as `T`:

- `dawn::platform::Platform::Platform()` and `~Platform()` тАФ constructor / virtual destructor
- `dawn::platform::Platform::GetCachingInterface()` тАФ the hook the shim will override
- `dawn::platform::CachingInterface::CachingInterface()` and `~CachingInterface()` тАФ constructor / virtual destructor the shim will subclass
- all other `dawn::platform::Platform` member functions that the shim leaves default-implemented (`AddTraceEvent`, `MonotonicallyIncreasingTime`, `IsFeatureEnabled`, the Histogram* family, etc.)

This proves the integration plan's Step 0 is achievable on this Linux host. The ComponentTest directory is gitignored via the `bench/vendor/` wildcard, so this is a disposable proof-of-build artifact, not a tracked rebuild.

### What this changes about the integration plan

The Push 4 design doc's "Step 0" section now has empirical backing for Option A (rebuild Dawn with exposed C++ visibility) on Linux. The specific args.gn contents are documented in `bench/docs/dawn-delegate-cache-integration.md` so the next session can reproduce. Mac hosts may or may not hit the libstdc++ 10 issue тАФ Apple toolchain overrides differ and Chromium's default sysroot for Mac is newer тАФ so the Mac verification is a separate follow-up.

### Remaining Step 0 work

- Make the rebuild contract durable: either vendor the ComponentTest args.gn at a tracked path, or add a repo-only tool/script that regenerates it on demand. The current tracked default is `bench/vendor/dawn/out/Release/args.gn` with only `is_debug = false`, which does not expose the C++ surface.
- Verify `libdawn_native.so` similarly links under the same args (1417 ninja steps estimated before the libc++ rebuild, longer on the full component build). This is the next single verification step.
- Decide the build-product location contract: `ComponentTest/` is fine for a verification fixture, but the shim's linker search path needs a stable directory once Step 1 (the C++ shim) lands.
- On Mac: re-verify whether the Apple toolchain default sysroot exposes `atomic::wait`; if it does, the `use_custom_libcxx = true` override may be unnecessary there.

### What this push did not change

- No Doe-side runtime code. CLAUDE.md non-negotiable #2 still forbids runtime-behavior placeholders in the Zig execution path; Zig stays untouched until Step 1 (the C++ shim) lands on a durable build contract.
- No tracked Dawn build artifacts. The ComponentTest output directory is gitignored and local-only.

## Push: Dawn cache integration verification тАФ vendored libwebgpu_dawn.so blocks the designed shim (2026-04-16 UTC)

Push 6 from the "do it all" execution sequence: a binary audit of the vendored Dawn build to confirm whether the Push 4 integration-design shim is buildable. It is not, in the current form, and the design doc is updated with the concrete finding and the three options that unblock it.

### What was verified

- `nm -D --defined-only bench/vendor/dawn/out/Release/libwebgpu_dawn.so` returns 507 dynamic symbols; every globally-exported text symbol is in the `wgpu*` C ABI family.
- `nm --defined-only` locates `dawn::platform::Platform::GetCachingInterface()` (`_ZN4dawn8platform8Platform19GetCachingInterfaceEv`) as a lowercase `t` (local text) тАФ the symbol is compiled into the binary but hidden from dynamic linking.
- No `dawn::*` or `dawn_*` C++ symbols are dynamically exported. The `DAWN_NATIVE_EXPORT` macro in `bench/vendor/dawn/include/dawn/native/dawn_native_export.h` only expands to `__attribute__((visibility("default")))` when both `DAWN_NATIVE_IMPLEMENTATION` and `DAWN_NATIVE_SHARED_LIBRARY` are set at Dawn build time; the vendored `args.gn` is minimal (`is_debug = false`) and the default monolithic-shared build produces C ABI only.
- `DawnInstanceDescriptor.platform = dawn::platform::Platform*` is the documented integration hook (`DawnNative.h:117-121`), but constructing a subclass against it requires linking base-class vtable slots and constructors that the current vendored binary does not expose.
- `dawn/dawn_proc.h` offers `dawnProcSetProcs(const DawnProcTable*)` as the only C ABI escape hatch; this redirects `wgpu*` calls but cannot install a `CachingInterface`.

### What this changes about the Push 4 plan

The original integration design assumed a C++ shim in Doe's tree could link against the vendored `libwebgpu_dawn.so`, subclass `dawn::platform::Platform` and `dawn::platform::CachingInterface`, and install the object via `DawnInstanceDescriptor.platform`. That shim will not link against the current binary.

Three options unblock the integration (all detailed in `bench/docs/dawn-delegate-cache-integration.md` under the new "Vendored Dawn build verification" and "Step 0" sections):

- Option A тАФ rebuild Dawn with exported C++ visibility (`is_component_build = true` / equivalent). Recommended default: smallest change, no source patch, brings the build into line with Dawn's intended shared-library configuration.
- Option B тАФ build Dawn's separate `libdawn_native` / `libdawn_platform` component form. Equivalent result, different GN config surface.
- Option C тАФ patch Dawn source to add an `extern "C"` cache-installation function in-tree. Survives Dawn rebuilds but needs a stable patch-apply step in the vendor-refresh workflow.

All three require a Dawn-side rebuild. Steps 1-7 of the integration plan (C++ shim, Zig FFI surface, CLI flag, trace schema, executor templates, resolver change, docs) cannot proceed until Step 0 lands.

### What this push did not change

- No Doe-side code. CLAUDE.md non-negotiable #2 still forbids runtime-behavior placeholders in the Zig execution path, so the Zig side stays untouched until the Dawn rebuild unblocks a real shim.
- No Dawn-side rebuild yet. The vendored `args.gn` is unchanged, the vendored `libwebgpu_dawn.so` is unchanged, and the design-doc-only nature of the Push 4 landing is preserved.

### What this push did change

- `bench/docs/dawn-delegate-cache-integration.md` тАФ new "Vendored Dawn build verification (2026-04-16)" section with the binary-audit findings, new "Step 0" section with the three unblock options and the recommended default, and the "Risks and open questions" first bullet updated to reflect the answered question.

### Note on Mac-host Dawn build

This verification was run on Linux against the committed vendored build. If a separate Dawn build lives under `bench/vendor/dawn/out/Release/` on `mac.lan` or any other Mac host, it must be re-verified there тАФ different `args.gn` could produce a binary that already exports the C++ surface, or not.

## Mac fair-cold evidence recovers four of the seven cache-asymmetric Metal workloads as strict claimable (2026-04-16 UTC)

The Mac-hardware step that was blocked across every April 16 push (G18 / D13-C10 / Linux-follow-ups) has landed. A fresh `mac.lan` compare against the apple-metal compare preset with the fair-cold defaults (both sides `--no-pipeline-cache`, both sides `pipelineCache.state="disabled" reason="cli-flag"`) produced a strict comparable artifact in which the pipeline-cache auto-flag correctly suppressed `pathAsymmetry: true` on every row because neither side opened an `MTLBinaryArchive`.

### Artifact path

- `bench/out/apple-metal/compare/20260416T212500Z/dawn-vs-doe.apple.metal.compare.json` тАФ strict comparable compare report, 7 workloads, `comparabilityPolicy.mode="strict"`, `comparabilityCoherence.status="pass"`, both participants carry the new nested `pipelineCache` object with `state="disabled" reason="cli-flag"`, every workload has `pathAsymmetry: false`
- `bench/out/apple-metal/compare/20260416T212500Z/dawn-vs-doe.apple.metal.compare.claim.json` тАФ claim report, `comparisonStatus=comparable`, `claimStatus=claimable`, `claimPolicy.mode="local"`, `claimPolicy.minTimedSamples=15`
- 16 run-artifacts under the workspace root (Doe + Dawn-delegate for 7 workloads apiece, plus the expected `.compare-dev` and per-run metadata)

### What this substantiates

Of the 7 cache-asymmetric compute workloads auto-disclosed in the 2026-04-16 apple-metal pipeline-cache-asymmetry push, **4 are in this fresh compare and all 4 are strict claimable** with Doe faster:

| Workload ID | p50 delta |
| --- | --- |
| `compute_workgroup_atomic_1024` | +9.6% |
| `compute_workgroup_non_atomic_1024` | +10.9% |
| `compute_zero_initialize_workgroup_memory_256` | +69.1% |
| `compute_concurrent_execution_single` | +4.3% |

These replace the 2026-04-15 "23/25 wins" reading for these four rows: the delta is now measured under both-sides-cache-disabled, so the positive deltas are runtime-engineering wins rather than cache-asymmetry artifacts.

Three additional non-cache-asymmetric rows rode along in the same preset and are also strict claimable in this run: `pipeline_compile_stress` (+42.2%) plus two directional-only dispatch rows (`compute_dispatch_fallback` +60.5%, `compute_dispatch_grid` +66.9%, both `claimEligible=false`).

### End-to-end schema round-trip confirmed on Mac

Every artifact in the workspace carries the new nested `pipelineCache` object introduced by the A1 push today:

```
pipelineCache: { state: "disabled", reason: "cli-flag", warmupCount: 0, warmupNs: 0 }
```

This is the first Mac-observed artifact set that proves the Zig-side telemetry plumbing (`TraceRunSummary` -> `backend_runtime_telemetry.refresh` -> `metal_pipeline_cache.process_active_cache` -> `trace_meta` JSON) round-trips into the Python reader and into the comparability gate. Linux-observed round-trips previously showed `state="disabled" reason="platform-unsupported"` because Linux cannot host Metal; this pass confirms the `cli-flag` branch on the Mac path.

### Partial-retraction scope narrowed

The 2026-04-16 partial retraction of the 2026-04-15 "Doe faster on 23/25" reading applied to all 7 cache-asymmetric compute workloads. With this push, the retraction scope narrows to the three still-missing matvec workloads:

- `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32`
- `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32_swizzle1`
- `compute_matvec_32768x2048_f32_workgroupshared_swizzle1`

Until these three have a fair-cold Mac rerun under `--no-pipeline-cache`, any "Doe faster on X" reading involving their 2026-04-15 numbers remains retracted. The other four cache-asymmetric workloads are fully unretracted by the artifact above.

### Not released-graded

`claimPolicy.mode="local"` тАФ this is claim-grade-local evidence, not a release-grade result. `releaseMinTimedSamples=15` is met at the sample level, but release mode additionally requires positive `p99` (per `reliability.releaseRequiredPositivePercentiles` in `config/benchmark-methodology-thresholds.json`) and the artifact stays in local mode for now. A release-mode rerun with explicit release claim policy is a separate follow-up.

### Follow-up queue

1. Mac rerun of the 3 matvec workloads under `--no-pipeline-cache` to complete the 7-row set.
2. Release-grade rerun of the 4 now-claimable rows if a release-mode compare lane is wanted.
3. Dawn-cache shim landing (Push 4 design doc) so the fair-warm equivalent lane becomes available for the same 7 rows.

## Push: Dawn delegate cache integration design doc (fair-warm lane scoping) (2026-04-16 UTC)

Scopes the follow-on engineering that makes Apple Metal Dawn-vs-Doe compute comparisons fair-*warm* instead of only fair-*cold*. The fair-cold default lane is already in place (G18 push: both sides under `--no-pipeline-cache`, both record `pipelineCache.state="disabled"`). The fair-warm lane requires a Dawn-side persistent cache equivalent to Doe's `MTLBinaryArchive`; this push records the integration surface so the next dedicated push does not re-derive it.

### What landed

**`bench/docs/dawn-delegate-cache-integration.md` (new).**
- Names the Dawn caching surface: `dawn::platform::CachingInterface::LoadData` / `StoreData` reached through `dawn::platform::Platform::GetCachingInterface()` in `bench/vendor/dawn/include/dawn/platform/DawnPlatform.h:48-189`. Flush hook is `dawn::native::PerformIdleTasks()` in `bench/vendor/dawn/include/dawn/native/DawnNative.h:361-363`.
- Identifies the integration gap: Dawn's cache is a C++ virtual contract, not a C ABI; the standard `webgpu.h` that Doe loads via `runtime/zig/src/wgpu_loader.zig` does not expose cache installation. A small in-tree C++ shim linked against `libdawn_native` is therefore required.
- Enumerates the seven-step landing plan: (1) `runtime/zig/src/backend/dawn/dawn_cache_shim.cpp` C++ shim; (2) `runtime/zig/src/backend/dawn/dawn_cache.zig` cross-platform FFI surface parallel to `metal_pipeline_cache.zig`; (3) `--dawn-cache-dir` CLI flag with typed unsupported error when the shim is absent; (4) `TraceRunSummary.dawnPipelineCache.{state,reason,entryCount}` schema addition; (5) `dawn_delegate_metal_cache` executor template; (6) `run_artifact.py::_resolve_metal_cache_asymmetry` extension to consult both caches; (7) docs updates.
- Platform-scoping table records which steps are Linux-executable (1-4, 6-7 as compile-green contract + unit tests) vs Mac-only (5 live execution and the full end-to-end validation against the 7 cache-asymmetric compute workloads held diagnostic pending Mac re-run).
- Calls out four risks: Dawn build shape (does `libdawn_native` export the platform hook in this repo's vendored build?), cache keyspace overlap verification (Doe's manifest is named, Dawn's keys are hashed), idle-flush ordering (must drive `PerformIdleTasks` deterministically before process exit), Mac-only validation scope.
- States explicitly that this doc is the only deliverable in this push: no runtime, bench harness, or runtime-visible doc changes. CLAUDE.md non-negotiable #2 forbids runtime-behavior placeholders in the Zig execution path, so the Zig side intentionally stays untouched until the shim lands.

**`bench/docs/metal-pipeline-cache-policy.md` тАФ cross-link added.**
- The existing fair-cold policy doc now points at the new integration design for the fair-warm follow-on lane.

### Why scope the integration this way

The `--dawn-cache-dir` flag is tempting to land as a no-op on non-Mac. That would be a placeholder. CLAUDE.md #2: "runtime behavior placeholders are not allowed in Zig execution paths; implement fully or fail with explicit unsupported taxonomy." So the flag is deliberately *not* in the CLI today; it lands in the push that also lands the shim, the FFI surface, the trace schema field, and the cross-platform-safe wrapper that routes through the existing `cli/ -> backend/` import fence.

### Test status

- No code changes in this push. No runtime, bench Python, or schema changes.
- Existing test baseline unchanged: 739 tests, 8 failures + 6 errors + 47 skipped (same as after Pushes 1-3 today).

### Follow-up queue

1. Verify the vendored Dawn build exports `dawn::platform::Platform` (compile-check the shim shape against `bench/vendor/dawn/include/`). Linux-executable.
2. Land the C++ shim + Zig FFI surface + trace schema addition in a single push that stays green on Linux via the "dawn-delegate-not-in-build" / "platform-unsupported" branches. Linux-executable.
3. Land executor templates, resolver changes, and unit tests. Linux-executable.
4. On Mac: run the 7 cache-asymmetric compute workloads under the fair-warm lane with both sides' caches warm. Recovers the compute-cache wins as claim-grade evidence. Mac-only.
5. Expand to broader Metal compute coverage beyond the initial 7 workloads. Mac-only.

## Push: proof-metrics front-door section in bench/README.md (2026-04-16 UTC)

Closes the "Proof-backed shader metric collection currently lives in a scratch evidence bundle rather than a promoted benchmark lane" item on the status front door. The stable mirror at `bench/out/proof-metrics/latest/` has existed since 2026-04-10; what was missing was the `bench/README.md` section that named it as the front door, named the structural reporter entrypoint, distinguished the reproducible structural half from the Vulkan-hardware timing half, and documented the refresh pattern.

### What landed

**`bench/README.md` тАФ "Proof-backed shader metric front door" section.**
- Identifies `bench/out/proof-metrics/latest/proof_metrics_summary.{json,md}` as the stable mirror (and notes both files are `.gitignore`-allowlisted so external writeups can link the stable path).
- Names the reporter entrypoint: `zig build runtime-compile-report` builds `doe-runtime-compile-report`, emitter source at `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/runtime_compile_report.zig`.
- Lists the two build flavors (`-Dlean-verified=false`, `-Dlean-verified=true`) and the delta-pair refresh pattern.
- Separates the structural half of the summary (reproducible cross-platform with the reporter binary alone) from the timing half (`compileP50Ns`, `nativeVulkanP50PerDispatchNs`, `gpuTimestampNs`) which requires Vulkan host execution.
- Names the current shader scope (`affine_loop_storage`, `tiled_storage`, `flat_2d_storage`) and the rule for broadening.

**`docs/status.md` тАФ follow-up line rewritten.**
- Previous line framed proof-metrics as scratch-only evidence awaiting a promoted benchmark lane. The stable mirror has been live since April 10; the new line points at that mirror and calls out the remaining work (a fresh Vulkan-host timing pass).

### What this does not do

- Does not produce a new timing evidence pass. The three `*P50Ns` deltas in the stable mirror are still from the April 9 evidence bundle. A Vulkan-host refresh remains a future item.
- Does not introduce a new orchestrator script or a promoted-compare-catalog entry. The proof-metrics pattern is Doe-only (build-flavor vs build-flavor) and does not fit the baseline-vs-comparison executor schema used by the promoted catalog; a front-door README section plus the stable mirror is the right shape for this evidence class.
- Does not add the shader scope broadening. Extending beyond the three-shader pass requires both reporter-side invocation list changes and mirror-schema updates in lockstep; out of scope for this push.

## Push: contract-centralization тАФ per-surface exemption table + ad-hoc scope docstring (2026-04-16 UTC)

Closes the "centralize comparability contract across ad-hoc compare scripts" item that has been open since the E14 shared ad-hoc gating module landed. The shared `bench/lib/adhoc_claim_gating.py` module already unified sample-floor / required-percentile / timer-overhead gating; what was missing was an explicit per-surface contract table that records what each surface enforces, what it exempts, and why.

### What landed

**`bench/docs/package-browser-ort-fairness-audit.md` тАФ per-surface contract exemption table.**
- New section enumerates every contract layer (comparability mode, report-level coherence, execution-shape parity, phase-asymmetry gate, two-tier sample-floor, required positive percentiles, timer-overhead budget, path-asymmetry) against every surface (native GPU, package Node/Bun, browser, ad-hoc CPU-only, ad-hoc GPU).
- Each cell records Required / Exempt / N/A plus the reason for an exemption.
- Residual-limits section is tightened with three concrete watchouts: wall-time-only package comparisons must be marked diagnostic; JS dispatch bridges that do not surface dispatch/row counts block structural equivalence; new ad-hoc GPU scripts without construction-guaranteed parity must route through `bench/cli.py compare` rather than emit their own `.claim.json`.

**`bench/lib/adhoc_claim_gating.py` тАФ scope docstring.**
- Docstring now names the three contract layers the module does NOT cover (execution-shape parity, timing-phase asymmetry, hardware-path asymmetry disclosure) and documents the construction-guarantee-or-migrate rule for ad-hoc GPU scripts.
- Links to the fairness-audit doc as the authoritative per-surface exemption table.

### Why this closes the contract-centralization risk

The strategic risk logged with E14 was: "the next person adding a comparison surface will copy whatever's nearby, not the canonical contract." The fix is not more code sharing -- E14 already extracted the sharable parts -- it is making the remaining per-surface exemptions legible in one place. A new surface author now has a single-page table answering "what do I still have to enforce myself?" and a module docstring answering "what does importing `adhoc_claim_gating` buy me, and what stays my responsibility?"

### Test status

- `python3 -m unittest discover -s bench/tests -t .` -- 739 tests, 8 failures + 6 errors + 47 skipped (same baseline as after the smoke-floor push; zero new regressions).
- Docs-only and docstring-only change path; no runtime behavior change.

### What this does not do

- Does not migrate `compare_subgroup_kernels.py` off its ad-hoc emission path. Subgroup has structural parity by construction (hardcoded 100-dispatch per side, same WGSL). The fairness-audit table records this as an accepted construction guarantee, not a blanket exemption.
- Does not add a runtime check for wall-time-only package/browser comparisons. The table marks them `diagnostic` by policy; a programmatic assertion in `comparability_runtime.py::assess_timing_phase_equivalence` is a future item if wall-time fallback turns out to recur.

## Push: smoke-lane comparability floor (two-tier sample-floor policy) (2026-04-16 UTC)

Closes the deferred "smoke-lane sample-floor bump" follow-up from the 2026-04-16 pipeline-cache-state and Linux-follow-ups pushes. The existing comparability floor (`comparabilityDefaults.minTimedSamples=7`) only fired on `claimEligible=true` workloads, so `count:2` smoke artifacts were able to land `comparability.comparable=true` at the report level even though they are never claim-eligible.

### What landed

**Schema v3 тАФ two-tier sample-floor policy.**
- `config/benchmark-methodology-thresholds.json` bumped to `schemaVersion: 3` and gains `comparabilityDefaults.smokeMinTimedSamples: 3`.
- `config/benchmark-methodology-thresholds.schema.json` bumped to `const: 3`; `comparabilityDefaults` now requires both `minTimedSamples` and `smokeMinTimedSamples`.
- Policy loader validates `smokeMinTimedSamples >= 0` and `smokeMinTimedSamples <= minTimedSamples` so the smoke tier can never silently outrank the claim-eligible tier.

**Coherence gate тАФ two-tier floor application.**
- `bench/lib/comparability_coherence.py::assess_workload` now takes both `min_timed_samples` and `smoke_min_timed_samples`. Claim-eligible workloads apply the claim floor (reason tag `comparability`); non-claim-eligible workloads apply the smoke floor (reason tag `smoke-comparability`). Existing tags are preserved so downstream log grep stays compatible.
- `assess_report` plumbs both floors and emits `smokeMinTimedSamples` alongside `minTimedSamples` on the coherence payload.

**Plumbing.**
- `BenchmarkMethodologyPolicy` gains `smoke_comparability_min_timed_samples` (default `0`).
- `bench/native_compare_modules/compare_from_artifacts.py::build_compare_report` plumbs the smoke floor into the inline coherence assessment.
- `bench/gates/comparability_coherence_gate.py` reads the new field and prints it on the summary line.
- `bench/cli.py` passes the new field from the loaded policy into `build_compare_report`.

**Tests тАФ `bench/tests/test_comparability_coherence_smoke_floor.py` (9 new tests).**
- Claim-eligible below floor fails with `comparability floor 7` reason; claim-eligible at floor passes; smoke `count:2` fails with `smoke-comparability floor 3`; smoke `count:3` passes; asymmetric counts only flag the failing side; report-level demotes `count:2` smoke; report-level accepts `count:3` smoke.
- Policy loader test reads the shipped config and verifies the tiered values; rejection test confirms `smoke > main` is rejected with a message naming `smokeMinTimedSamples`.

### Test status

- `python3 -m unittest discover -s bench/tests -t .` тАФ 739 tests, 8 failures + 6 errors + 47 skipped. +9 passing vs the pre-push baseline (the 14 pre-existing failures/errors are the same schema-drift and numeric-fragility-corpus items noted in earlier April entries; zero new regressions introduced by this push).
- `zig build`, `zig build test` тАФ exit 0.
- Threshold config validates against the new schema v3.

### What this does not do

- Smoke lanes have not been re-run against the new floor; smoke configs still carry `iterations: 2` by design, and the coherence gate will now correctly demote any `comparable:true` smoke rows at the report level.
- The comparability coherence gate was already default-on in `run_blocking_gates.py` after the D13/C10 push on 2026-04-16; no runner change is needed.
