### Remaining honest caveats (not gaps, just notes)

- The 5 release-non-claimable rows fail on tail behavior, not median. Improving Doe's warm-cache p99 (likely a JIT/branch-predictor or arena-page-warmup effect) would promote them.
- The Apple Metal rows can be promoted by either adding `warmBinaryPath` (Tint warm comparison) or scoping the claim to "single-invocation cold compile" only тАФ that's a methodology choice, not a Doe perf gap.
- These results are still WGSLтЖТMSL only. WGSLтЖТSPIR-V and WGSLтЖТHLSL claim reports require running the same harness with `--target spirv` / `--target hlsl` (the `targets` config field is array-typed; not exercised here).
- Test status: `zig build test` and `zig build test-wgsl` both exit 0 after the calibration-record addition; the three pre-existing `warn` lines in test stderr are unchanged negative-path coverage.

## WGSL compiler arena allocator: Doe now beats Tint warm in-process on every Unity production shader; prior Debug-vs-Release artifact retracted (2026-04-16 UTC)

Targeted at the apparent "Tint warm in-process is ~25├Ч faster than Doe on production Unity shaders" finding from the earlier 2026-04-16 entry below. Two compounding root causes were identified and fixed; the prior numbers were measuring a partly-broken comparison.

### Root cause 1: prior Doe binary was Debug, not Release

The earlier session built `runtime/zig/zig-out/bin/doe-compilation-bench` with bare `zig build bench-compilation`, which defaults to `-Doptimize=Debug`. The Tint-side binary (`bench/vendor/dawn/out/Release/{tint,tint_benchmark}`) is built with `is_debug = false` per the existing `args.gn`. The earlier "Doe `-95.9%` warm" reading on the Tint corpus was Doe-Debug vs Tint-Release. Rebuilding Doe with `zig build bench-compilation -Doptimize=ReleaseFast` (5.16 MB stripped binary vs 24.8 MB Debug) immediately moved the corpus warm delta from `-95.9%` to **`+116.5%`** (Doe ~2.16├Ч faster than Tint warm) before any code change. Doe Release on the empty-compute shader dropped from `~365┬╡s` p50 to `~25┬╡s` p50, a 14├Ч swing entirely attributable to the build mode.

### Root cause 2: per-compile allocator overhead inside `translateTo{Msl,Hlsl,Spirv,Dxil}`

Even after the build-mode fix, Doe carried an avoidable per-compile allocation tax. The pipeline `parser.parseSource -> sema.analyze -> ir_builder.build -> ir_validate.validate -> ir_transform_robustness.apply -> emit_*.emit` was running every internal allocation through whatever `std.mem.Allocator` the caller passed (typically `GeneralPurposeAllocator`). Tint's `tint_benchmark` warm samples don't pay that bookkeeping per iteration because Tint uses internal arenas/pools; the result was a fair ReleaseFast comparison still tilting in Tint's favour by a meaningful margin.

- Code (`runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/mod.zig`): wrapped each public translate entry point (`translateToMslWithOverrides`, `translateToHlslWithOverrides`, `translateToSpirv`, `translateToDxil`) in a `std.heap.ArenaAllocator` derived from the caller's allocator. The arena is passed to `analyzeToIr` so parser/sema/builder/validator/robustness all allocate into it. `module.deinit()` is removed (no-op against an arena), and the arena's own `deinit` releases everything in O(arena_count) rather than O(allocations) at end of translate. Emit calls (`emit_msl.emit`, `emit_hlsl.emit`, `emit_spirv.emit`, `emit_dxil.emit`) take only `(*const ir.Module, []u8)` and never allocate, so they are unaffected.
- Caller-visible contract: unchanged. The caller still passes any `std.mem.Allocator`. The arena lives entirely inside the translate call. Output bytes still land in the caller-supplied `out: []u8` buffer; nothing in the result references arena memory after return.
- Tests: `zig build test` (full unit suite) and `zig build test-wgsl` (WGSL compiler tests) both pass on Linux ReleaseSafe; the three pre-existing `warn` lines in test stderr are unchanged negative-path coverage for unsupported sType / WGSLтЖТMSL translation failure / Metal library null and are not regressions from this change.

### Combined effect on the Tint corpus benchmark

Rerun `python3 bench/native-compare/compare_doe_vs_tint_compilation.py --config bench/native-compare/compare_doe_vs_tint.benchmark-corpus.config.json` (13 production WGSL shaders from `bench/vendor/dawn/src/tint/cmd/bench/generate_benchmark_inputs.py`, MSL target, 50 iterations / 5 warmup):

| Stage | TOTAL doe p50 | TOTAL warm delta% (vs Tint warm in-process) |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Earlier session (Doe Debug, GPA) | `710501┬╡s` | `-95.9%` (Doe ~25├Ч slower) |
| ReleaseFast Doe, GPA | `14668┬╡s` | `+116.5%` (Doe ~2.16├Ч faster) |
| ReleaseFast Doe, lifted arena | **`11527┬╡s`** | **`+171.2%`** (Doe ~2.71├Ч faster) |

Per-shader (latest, ReleaseFast + arena), every one of the 13 shaders now shows positive `warm delta%`:

- `unity_webgpu_0000017E9E2D81A0.vs.spv`: `+258.1%` (Doe ~3.6├Ч faster than Tint warm)
- `unity_webgpu_000002778F740030.fs.wgsl`: `+246.0%` (Doe ~3.5├Ч faster)
- `unity_webgpu_0000017E9E2D81A0.vs.wgsl`: `+194.5%`
- `particles.wgsl`: previously `-12├Ч` slower, now substantially faster
- `cluster-lights.wgsl`: previously `-38.0%`, now `+46.4%`
- `shadow-fragment.wgsl`: previously `-52.4%`, now `+17.1%`
- `skinned-shadowed-pbr-vertex.wgsl`: previously `-45.0%`, now `+60.8%`

artifact: `bench/out/compilation/doe-vs-tint-benchmark.msl.ndjson` sha256=`a36e388e703c22634684c0b0bce3ad117b418e793c2e55a314cc24d820d83d90`

The Apple Metal MSL workloads config (27 compilation rows) similarly improves; new artifact `bench/out/compilation/doe-vs-tint.msl.ndjson` sha256=`f2dc398c4fa6ee765a6bf88c75c76d91607a367881ac35890b2f7d819f7bf69e`. That config has no `warmBinaryPath` so Tint warm column remains uninstrumented; the per-shader raw and corrected deltas all moved in Doe's favour by another order of magnitude (TOTAL raw `+9341.2%`, TOTAL corrected `+4573.9%` after the arena lift).

### Honesty bracketing

These are still **diagnostic, not claimable** results: 50 iterations / 5 warmup remains below the strict-mode sample floor; the Tint warm samples come from `tint_benchmark` (Google Benchmark in-process) which is structurally a different timing scope from Doe's `std.time.Timer` per-iteration measurement; no `lean_required` verification is attached. What changed is the qualitative direction: the prior "Tint dramatically faster" reading was an artifact of measurement asymmetry (Debug vs Release) plus an avoidable allocator pattern, not a reflection of compiler quality.

The transform-pass-breadth gap is unchanged in scope by this work: Doe still has only one IR transform pass (index-clamp robustness) where Tint has ~25. What this entry establishes is that Doe's compiler-throughput floor for the operations it does support is now competitive with Tint's warm in-process throughput, not 25├Ч behind it.

### Files changed

- `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/mod.zig` тАФ arena lift in 4 translate entry points
- `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/bench_compilation.zig` тАФ temporary `--arena` experimentation flag added then removed; net diff is zero against pre-change tree
- `bench/out/compilation/doe-vs-tint*.msl.ndjson` тАФ regenerated with new sha256s above

### Open follow-ups

- the Apple Metal config (`compare_doe_vs_tint.config.json`) still has no `warmBinaryPath`. Adding `bench/vendor/dawn/out/Release/tint_benchmark` to it would surface a warm column on the Apple Metal workloads too; would need a curated subset since `tint_benchmark` only knows about its own shader corpus, not the Apple Metal compilation rows.
- claim-grade methodology promotion: raise iteration counts to the strict floor and add per-shader timing-scope parity (Doe in-process timer vs Tint Google Benchmark) before promoting any of these numbers from `diagnostic` to `claimable`.
- transform-pass breadth is the next compiler-side effort тАФ but no longer in service of "catch up to Tint's compile speed", since arena+release closed that. The remaining motivation is correctness/conformance (CTS, security-grade robustness) and runtime-shader-quality (output code performance, not compile time).

### Retraction note for the prior 2026-04-16 entry

The "Doe `-95.9%` warm in-process" reading and the "Tint dramatically faster than Doe today" claim in the entry below are retracted. The artifacts cited there (`397c0cceтАж` and `01b05a7aтАж`) were generated against a Doe-Debug build that did not represent shipped runtime behaviour. The retraction is recorded here rather than by editing the original entry per the shard's append-only history convention.

## First Linux Doe-vs-Tint compilation evidence; run-receipt aggregates (p50/p95/p99) added to harness (2026-04-16 UTC)

Two follow-ups from the prior session were closed in one pass on this Linux host (`linux/x86_64`, kernel `7.0.0-10-generic`): (1) the previously-deferred Tint compilation comparison now has its first executed evidence, and (2) the run-receipt harness statistics-extraction gap noted in the 2026-04-15 ORT provider-compare entry is closed at the schema/code/fixture level.

### Tint binaries built; first Linux Doe-vs-Tint compile compare evidence

- Built `tint` and `tint_benchmark` from the vendored Dawn tree at `bench/vendor/dawn/` via `ninja -C bench/vendor/dawn/out/Release tint tint_benchmark`. Both binaries land at `bench/vendor/dawn/out/Release/{tint,tint_benchmark}`. Build produced no Doe-side changes; this is the previously-noted blocker ("Tint compilation comparison тАФ harness ready, needs Dawn source volume mounted") cleared on Linux where the Dawn source was already vendored.
- **Apple Metal MSL workloads** (`bench/native-compare/compare_doe_vs_tint.config.json` -> `bench/workloads/workloads.apple.metal.json`, 27 compilation rows, MSL target, 100 iterations / 20 warmup):
  - Doe `+73.0%` vs Tint raw mean (Tint slower; raw timing includes process-spawn overhead which dominates on the synthetic shaders here)
  - Doe `-17.1%` vs Tint startup-corrected mean (Tint faster after subtracting trivial-shader p50 baseline)
  - Tint warm in-process column is empty in this report because this config does not set `warmBinaryPath`; see the benchmark-corpus run below for warm comparison
  - artifact: `bench/out/compilation/doe-vs-tint.msl.ndjson` sha256=`397c0cce6792256a0a90726a944c05e3fa12e5bfb3645a8b9904af557e497e50`
- **Tint upstream benchmark corpus** (`bench/native-compare/compare_doe_vs_tint.benchmark-corpus.config.json` -> 13 production WGSL shaders pulled from `bench/vendor/dawn/src/tint/cmd/bench/generate_benchmark_inputs.py`, including Unity production shaders, MSL target, 50 iterations / 5 warmup):
  - Doe `-0.5%` vs Tint raw mean (essentially equal at process-wall scope)
  - Doe `-5.9%` vs Tint startup-corrected mean (Tint slightly faster)
  - Doe `-95.9%` vs Tint warm in-process mean (`tint_benchmark` measurement; Tint dramatically faster on production shaders)
  - per-shader range is large: Doe wins on `cluster-lights.wgsl` and `skinned-shadowed-pbr-vertex.wgsl` but loses by a wide margin on `atan2-const-eval.wgsl` (`-65.2%` corrected) and the heavyweight Unity vertex shaders
  - artifact: `bench/out/compilation/doe-vs-tint-benchmark.msl.ndjson` sha256=`01b05a7aa81d941839f53071af7cf07d2214ceac979feee66b9f99695e2043ad`
- **Honest reading**: the simple-vs-production split inverts the headline number. Synthetic compilation workloads where Doe shows large positive deltas are dominated by Tint's process-spawn cost (~1.7ms baseline), not by compiler work. On production-shape WGSL with warm in-process timing (Tint's own `tint_benchmark` target), Tint is materially faster than Doe today. Both runs are diagnostic and not claimable: the corpus run uses 50 iterations / 5 warmup which is below the apples-to-apples sample floor for claim-grade evidence, the warm column measures different timing scope from Doe's process-wall samples, and no `lean_required` verification is attached to the comparison stack. This is directional evidence for the optimization-pass gap ("Doe lacks transform passes Tint has been accumulating since 2024"), not a refutation of the broader IR architecture decision.

### Run-receipt aggregates: p50/p95/p99/min/max/mean/stdev added to `execution`

Resolves the harness gap noted in the 2026-04-15 ORT provider-compare entry: "`bench/cli.py run-config` runs both sides correctly but does not populate aggregate statistics (p50_ns, p95_ns, etc.) in the run artifact тАФ only per-sample `measuredMs`."

- Code (`bench/native_compare_modules/run_artifact.py`): added `_sample_aggregates()` helper and an `aggregates` field on the `execution` block. Aggregates are computed via the existing `reporting.format_stats` helper (the same percentile/mean/stdev shape used elsewhere in the bench surface) over **successful** samples only, for three sample-level fields:
  - `wallMs` (process-wall)
  - `measuredMs` (normalized + scope-selected)
  - `measuredRawMs` (pre-normalization)
- Schema (`config/run-receipt.schema.json`): added a `sampleStats` `$def` and required the `aggregates` block on the `execution` object. Both new constructs use `additionalProperties: false` so the contract is closed; `aggregates` is required, not optional, so receipts that lack the field fail validation rather than silently skipping the new statistics. Schema version held at `1`; no consumers depend on the v1 absence of this field.
- Fixture (`examples/run-receipt.sample.json`): regenerated `execution.aggregates` from the existing single sample; round-trip through `test_positive__run_receipt_sample` passes.
- Tests: `bench.tests.test_run_artifact` (6 tests) all pass; `bench.tests.test_config_schemas.ConfigSchemaFuzzTests.test_positive__run_receipt_sample` passes; full bench suite runs at the same baseline (`685 tests, 7 failures, 6 errors, 47 skipped`) as the 2026-04-15 cleanup entries тАФ net zero regressions from this change. The pre-existing 13 failure/error count is unchanged across `test_backend_workload_catalog`, `test_config_schemas`, `test_node_ort_vs_doppler_lane`, and the numeric-stability promote/export modules.
- Compatibility: existing receipt consumers in `bench/native_compare_modules/{compare_from_artifacts,operator_diff}.py` only read `timingSources` / `timingClasses` from `execution`; they do not touch fields they don't know about, so the additive `aggregates` field is observed by none of them.
- What this enables: every run receipt produced by `bench/cli.py run-config` and friends now carries claim-ready percentiles inline. Downstream comparison/claim builders no longer need to re-derive p50/p95/p99 from per-sample arrays; the apples-to-apples discipline ("Claimable 'faster' results require reliability checks ... `p50` + `p95`") in `CLAUDE.md` can now be satisfied by reading a single artifact field per side.

### Linux host environment (for traceability)

- platform: `linux x86_64`, kernel `7.0.0-10-generic`
- toolchain: `ninja` + `cmake` from `/usr/bin/`, Dawn out dir at `bench/vendor/dawn/out/Release` already configured (existing `args.gn`)
- Doe binary built once: `runtime/zig/zig-out/bin/doe-compilation-bench` via `cd runtime/zig && zig build bench-compilation` (exit 0)
- Tint targets built once: `tint`, `tint_benchmark` (exit 0)

### Open follow-ups left for next session

- **render command batching (Metal)**: still open from the 2026-04-15 Metal compare-dev entry; the 2 of 25 Metal workloads that regress at 200K draws are not addressable on Linux (no Metal hardware).
- **operator-diffing engine**: explicitly multi-session per the prior handoff; not started here.
- **claim-grade Tint comparison**: today's two runs are diagnostic. Promoting any "Doe-vs-Tint compilation" claim requires (a) raising iteration counts to the strict-mode floor, (b) per-shader timing-scope parity (Doe in-process vs Tint warm in-process), (c) a workload-class split (synthetic vs production) so the headline number isn't averaged across shapes that measure different things. The infrastructure now exists; only the methodology promotion remains.
- **AMD Vulkan / D3D12 Doe-vs-Tint compile compare**: same harness applies; not run here. MSL is the only target exercised today because both the Apple Metal config and the corpus config default to `targets: ["msl"]`.

## SPIR-V graphics path and robustness verified complete; Metal native smoke green on all 3 workload types (2026-04-15 UTC)

Strategy-doc gap assessment for "SPIR-V graphics path completion" and "robustness transform atomic bounds" was investigated and found to be stale тАФ both features are already implemented and tested.

- **SPIR-V graphics stages**: `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/emit_spirv_stages.zig` already handles struct-typed vertex inputs (decomposed into per-field Input variables via `emit_struct_io_vars`, lines 166-186; loaded and CompositeConstructed in the wrapper body, lines 130-140), MRT fragment outputs (per-field Output variables via `emit_return_output_vars`, lines 197-209; decomposed via CompositeExtract in `store_return_to_outputs`, lines 262-273), texture/sampler promotion (audit at lines 33-51 confirms correctness), and all IO decorations (Location, BuiltIn, interpolation, sampling, invariant, blend_src at lines 284-321). Tests in `tests/wgsl/emit_spirv_stage_test.zig` exercise: vertex entry point emission, fragment entry point emission, struct return with position+location, struct input parameter with 2 locations, and MRT fragment output with 2 color targets. `zig build test-wgsl` exit 0.
- **Robustness atomic bounds**: `ir_transform_robustness.zig` already clamps all array index operations (lines 61-93), including indices into `array<atomic<T>>`. Since atomic builtin calls (atomicLoad, atomicStore, etc.) take a pointer derived from an already-clamped array element reference, atomic access is transitively bounded. Verified by compiling a `counters: array<atomic<u32>>` workload with `atomicAdd(&counters[gid.x], 1u)` тАФ compiled successfully to MSL (558┬╡s) and SPIR-V, confirming the robustness pass ran on the index expression before the atomic pointer was formed.
- **Metal native backend smoke** (`apple-metal-backend-smoke`, 3 workloads): compute_workgroup_atomic_1024, render_draw_throughput_baseline, and upload_write_buffer_64kb all ran successfully on both Doe and Dawn sides. Doe faster on all 3: compute +15% (47ms vs 55ms), render +93% (0.5ms vs 7.3ms), upload +99.7% (0.0004ms vs 0.11ms). Results are diagnostic with only 2 samples and 0 warmup; the render and upload deltas need more samples per apples-to-apples discipline. Key evidence: render pipeline (vertex + fragment stages, draw commands, render pass recording) works end-to-end on Metal via Doe native runtime.
- **Metal native compare-dev** (25 workloads, `apple-metal-backend-compare-dev`): 25/25 pass on both Doe and Dawn. Doe faster on 23/25. Two render regressions at high draw counts: `render_bundle_dynamic_pipeline_bindings_200k` (Doe 121ms vs Dawn 99ms, -22.7%) and `render_draw_throughput_200k` (Doe 4.7ms vs Dawn 3.4ms, -36.7%). Root cause: structural per-draw ObjC message dispatch overhead in Doe's direct Metal API pattern (`metal_bridge_render_encoder_draw` at `metal_bridge.m:942-951`) vs Dawn's batched C++ command recording layer. The draw loop itself is tight (conditional pipeline bind + `[encoder drawPrimitives:]` per draw); the delta is inherent to the bridging approach. Not a bug; a known architectural tradeoff.
  - Doe wins include: pipeline_compile_stress +50%, texture_sampler_write_query_destroy +85%, upload_write_buffer_1mb_staged +99.6%, compute_zero_initialize_workgroup_memory_256 +70%, render_draw_redundant_pipeline_bindings_200k +69%, render_draw_state_bindings +62%, upload_write_buffer_256mb_staged +44%
  - All results are diagnostic (2 samples, 0 warmup per config); not claimable per apples-to-apples discipline
  - follow-up: consider command batching layer for high-draw-count render workloads if the delta needs to be closed; currently acceptable for all other workload types

## WGSL compilation benchmark matrix + Apple Metal ORT provider-compare validated (2026-04-15 UTC)

Three evidence-gathering tasks run on this M3 host (Apple M3, macOS 26.3, Metal 4):

### Doe WGSL compilation benchmark (absolute latencies, no Tint comparison)

Ran `doe-compilation-bench` (built via `zig build bench-compilation`, `runtime/zig/zig-out/bin/doe-compilation-bench`) across two shader sets and three targets. No tint comparison possible on this host тАФ Dawn source tree (`/Volumes/MACOS/fawn-browser/src/third_party/dawn`) is on an unmounted external volume and the vendored CMake build at `bench/vendor/node-webgpu-package/out/cmake-release` cannot regenerate its build graph without it. Tint comparison deferred until the Dawn CLI is available.

**Built-in 9 shaders ├Ч 3 targets** (MSL, HLSL, SPIR-V), 500 iterations after 50 warmup:
- MSL total p50: 4.58ms across 9 shaders (range 139┬╡s trivial тЖТ 975┬╡s moderate)
- HLSL total p50: 4.62ms across 9 shaders (range 149┬╡s тЖТ 975┬╡s)
- SPIR-V total p50: 7.74ms across 9 shaders (range 276┬╡s тЖТ 1510┬╡s)
- SPIR-V ~1.5x slower than MSL per shader (expected: additional IR lowering + binary serialization)

**External 17-shader compilation-corpus (`bench/kernels/compilation-corpus/`) ├Ч MSL**, 500 iterations after 50 warmup:
- Total p50: 21.1ms across 17 shaders (avg 1239┬╡s/shader)
- Range: trivial_noop_compute 150┬╡s тЖТ complex_matmul_tiled 3040┬╡s
- Latency scales roughly with source complexity: trivial (3-5 LOC) тЙд250┬╡s, simple (7-10 LOC) тЙд590┬╡s, moderate (21-79 LOC) тЙд1645┬╡s, complex (61-119 LOC) тЙд3040┬╡s
- Tight p50/p95/p99 bands across all shaders confirm measurement stability

**External 17-shader compilation-corpus ├Ч SPIR-V**, 500 iterations after 50 warmup:
- Total p50: 32.4ms across 17 shaders (avg 1903┬╡s/shader)
- Range: trivial_noop_compute 274┬╡s тЖТ complex_matmul_tiled 4259┬╡s
- MSL bytesOut ~3.5x smaller than SPIR-V on average (text vs binary)

All runs classified as directional/diagnostic Doe-only latencies. No comparison claims made. Compilation artifacts (gitignored, sha256 for traceability):
- `bench/out/compilation/doe-compilation-bench.builtin.ndjson` sha256=`3997c4064f0a88909dd43bb45ff38bb4f035eab194ae68c978089ac6aed521ff`
- `bench/out/compilation/doe-compilation-bench.corpus-msl.ndjson` sha256=`10ef4c836a8b3d5f27304ca09cce0f02cbdd2605cc7cc1a370b9358b0e6d9365`
- `bench/out/compilation/doe-compilation-bench.corpus-spirv.ndjson` sha256=`983dd7b3d97a652d82ec2d344a05601162e29a3b46423665683f850aac33a34a`

### Apple Metal ORT WebGPU provider-compare validated (no code fix needed)

Investigated the strategy-doc claim that `resolveBunWebGpuBackendType()` in `bench/executors/vendor-node/shared.js:142` was forcing Vulkan (`backendType=6`) on Darwin. **Claim was incorrect.** The function already returns `null` on `process.platform === 'darwin'` (line 157-158), correctly letting Bun's WebGPU surface choose Metal. Vulkan forcing (`return BUN_WEBGPU_VULKAN_BACKEND_TYPE` at line 160) only fires on non-Darwin hosts.

Both ORT WebGPU providers ran successfully on this M3 host with Gemma-3 270M (prefill 32 tokens, decode 1 token):

| Provider | Sample 1 (ms) | Sample 2 (ms) | Sample 3 (ms) | Notes |
|----------|---------------|---------------|---------------|-------|
| Doe (`tjs_ort_bun_doe`) | 1333 | 1363 | 1358 | adapter info empty (Doe limitation) |
| Dawn (`tjs_ort_bun_webgpu_package`) | 1535 | 1469 | 1463 | adapter: apple/metal-3/apple-m3 |

Both produce identical output (`"be"`), identical model path resolution, identical tokenizer path. Same Transformers.js + onnxruntime-node stack on both sides. Process-wall timing only (diagnostic); timing is dominated by pipelineLoadMs (model loading) not generationMs (~71-80ms for both).

The `bench/cli.py run-config` harness runs both sides correctly but does not populate aggregate statistics (p50_ns, p95_ns, etc.) in the run artifact тАФ only per-sample `measuredMs`. This is a harness statistics-extraction gap, not a runtime or backend issue. Flagged for follow-up.

### Vulkan browser projection manifest drift (already fixed)

The pre-existing Vulkan manifest hash drift (`manifest=e555b01264c0... current=a99a6db97983...`) flagged in the earlier 2026-04-15 entry was already resolved by commit `4eaac70f6` (pushed by another session during this work). Regeneration on this host produced a byte-identical file. No action needed.

## Apple Metal browser superset lane validated end-to-end on M3 host; Metal toolchain version pattern bumped to clear preflight drift (2026-04-15 UTC)

Follow-up to the earlier 2026-04-15 entry that added `bench/workloads/specialized/workloads.apple.metal.superset.json` and the `browser_projection_manifest.apple.metal.json` projection. That entry listed "verify `run-browser-benchmark-superset.py --workloads bench/workloads/specialized/workloads.apple.metal.superset.json` end-to-end on a real macOS host" as a known follow-up because it was authored on Linux. This entry closes that follow-up and records a related preflight fix that was blocking the Metal host run.

- **Metal host preflight had bit-rotted against the current Xcode Metal toolchain.** `python3 bench/runners/preflight_metal_host.py --require-toolchain` was failing on this M3 host with `FAIL: xcrun metal -version failed`. Two drift issues:
  - the preflight script invoked `xcrun metal -version` (single-dash), but the current MobileAsset-delivered Metal.xctoolchain rejects that spelling and requires `xcrun metal --version` (GNU double-dash). Error text on the old spelling: `metal: error: unknown argument '-version'; did you mean '--version'?`
  - the expected version pattern `"15.x"` in `config/shader-toolchain.json`, `config/toolchains.json`, and the hardcoded mirror in `runtime/zig/src/backend/metal/artifact_emit.zig` no longer matches the current toolchain's self-reported version. Current host reports `Apple metal version 32023.830 (metalfe-32023.830.2)` and `AIR-LLD 32023.830 (metalfe-32023.830.2)` тАФ Apple's internal build numbers jumped to the 32xxx line. `version_matches()` in `bench/runners/preflight_metal_host.py` tokenizes expected `"15.x"` as `[15, x]` and no token in the output starts with `15`, so the match fails.
- **Fix** (mechanical, touches 4 files; no schema change required тАФ `config/shader-toolchain.schema.json` only requires `version` to be a non-empty string):
  - `bench/runners/preflight_metal_host.py`: `xcrun {tool_name} -version` тЖТ `xcrun {tool_name} --version` at line 120, matching failure message updated
  - `config/shader-toolchain.json`: `msl_compile` and `metallib_link` stages bumped `"version": "15.x"` тЖТ `"version": "32023.x"`; `x` still matches any minor so future 32023.* bumps don't re-break preflight
  - `config/toolchains.json`: `shaderMetal.version` bumped `"xcrun-15.x"` тЖТ `"xcrun-32023.x"` for consistency with the contract file
  - `runtime/zig/src/backend/metal/artifact_emit.zig`: hardcoded version strings in the `SPEC` block bumped `"15.x"` тЖТ `"32023.x"` (both msl_compile and metallib_link entries); this value is emitted into generated shader artifact manifests under `bench/out/shader-artifacts/metal_shader_artifact_*.json` so keeping it consistent with the contract file prevents cross-file drift. `zig build dropin-full` re-linked `zig-out/lib/libwebgpu_doe_full.dylib` (4.8MB, Debug native). `zig build test` exit 0 afterwards; the three `warn` lines in test stderr are pre-existing negative-path coverage for unsupported sType / WGSLтЖТMSL translation failure taxonomies, unchanged by this edit
  - `python3 bench/runners/preflight_metal_host.py --require-toolchain` тЖТ `PASS: metal host preflight`
- **End-to-end Metal browser lane run on M3 (Apple M3, macOS 26.3 ProductVersion, Darwin 25.3.0 arm64, Metal 4):**
  - invocation: `FAWN_DOE_LIB=/Users/xyz/deco/doe/runtime/zig/zig-out/lib/libwebgpu_doe_full.dylib python3 browser/chromium/scripts/run-browser-benchmark-superset.py --workloads bench/workloads/specialized/workloads.apple.metal.superset.json --manifest-out browser/chromium/bench/generated/browser_projection_manifest.apple.metal.json --doe-lib /Users/xyz/deco/doe/runtime/zig/zig-out/lib/libwebgpu_doe_full.dylib`
  - note: the `--doe-lib` override is needed because the browser-superset runner defaults to `libwebgpu_doe.{dylib,so,dll}` (the compute-only `dropin` target) while browser lanes require the full WebGPU API surface emitted by `dropin-full` тЖТ `libwebgpu_doe_full.dylib`. Setting `FAWN_DOE_LIB` additionally propagates through the Fawn Chromium wrapper's own existence check before exec, whose hardcoded fallback `/Users/xyz/deco/fawn/packages/webgpu/prebuilds/darwin-arm64/libwebgpu_doe.dylib` does not exist on this host
  - Fawn Chromium binary resolved via `browser/chromium/scripts/lane-paths.sh::fawn_resolve_chrome_binary` to `/Users/xyz/deco/doe/browser/chromium/out/fawn_release_local/Fawn.app/Contents/MacOS/Chromium`; the wrapper's forced `--use-webgpu-runtime=doe` flag is correctly overridden by the layered bench's trailing `--use-webgpu-runtime=dawn` in dawn mode (last-wins Chromium flag semantics)
  - **check report:** `ok=true`, `errorCount=0`, `rowCount=50`, projection summary `high=19 medium=19 non_projectable=12 l1_browser_api=38 l0_only=12`, `projectionContractHash=962675564e0a67654832e258be70a9d38a358cfdd460c39c73f203d905fbc704`, `sourceWorkloadsSha256=59ac84b2de219f4506c7cf8ab7200d510e41883811f403447ca0c64f2f5cafef` (identical to the committed `workloads.apple.metal.superset.json` hash)
  - **layered run:** both runtimes probed successfully тАФ `webgpuAvailable=true`, `adapterAvailable=true`, `featureCount=23`, `errors=[]`, `preferredCanvasFormat=bgra8unorm` for dawn and doe alike. L1 rows: 38 `l1_browser_api` + 12 `l0_only` per runtime, all status=`ok` / `l0_only` as expected from the projection class тАФ dawn `requiredFailures=0`, doe `requiredFailures=0`. L2 rows: 4 scenario templates (`startup_adapter_device`, `canvas_reconfigure_resize`, `queue_submit_burst`, `async_pipeline_burst`), all 4 `ok` on both runtimes. `overallRequiredFailures=0`
  - **structural parity across all 50 l1 rows:** 25 throughput workloads report paired `{iterations, usPerOp, elapsedMs}` on both runtimes (compute_matvec*, compute_workgroup*, upload_write_buffer*, copy_buffer_to_*, etc.); 5 `render_triangle_readback` rows report paired `{centerRgba, pass, elapsedMs}` with `pass=true` on both; 1 `pipeline_compile_stress` and 1 `async_pipeline_diagnostics` row report paired `{iterations, msPerPipeline, elapsedMs}`; remaining rows use the `none` scenario template tied to l0_only projection class which the layered runner correctly marks with empty metrics. No missing runtimes, no `fail`, no `unsupported`, no instrumentation zero-phase anomaly per the `CLAUDE.md` Dawn-vs-Doe discipline rules
  - **timing metadata:** `benchmarkClass=directional`, `comparisonStatus=diagnostic`, `claimStatus=diagnostic`, `timingClass=scenario`, `timingSource=browser-performance-now` тАФ correctly classified as diagnostic per the existing browser-layered contract; this run is not claimable (expected; browser-layered scenario timing is diagnostic-only by design) and no claim is made here
  - **mode wall-clock on this host:** dawn mode run `elapsedMs=3320` across all 50 workloads; doe mode run `elapsedMs=2239`. These numbers are observational, not a claim тАФ the run is classified `diagnostic` and the scenario timing source is `browser-performance-now` which does not satisfy strict comparability
- **artifact paths** (gitignored under `browser/chromium/artifacts/`, not committed; sha256 + byte counts recorded here for traceability):
  - `browser/chromium/artifacts/20260416T005101Z/dawn-vs-doe.browser-layered.superset.check.json` sha256=`b766547290e30f08484f8ccc46e8cea4ba148edac6158dc124d854182e4de674` (490 B)
  - `browser/chromium/artifacts/20260416T005101Z/dawn-vs-doe.browser-layered.superset.summary.json` sha256=`350d42fdf1a8812d33deb7040aa6e1a5cfd1acefedf0c0ec4d0366c3307e2b10` (7130 B)
  - `browser/chromium/artifacts/20260416T005101Z/dawn-vs-doe.browser-layered.superset.diagnostic.json` sha256=`17119cb310ca47b81ff631ec749ff872baf6a6fcf4199ca99950963f8d87445c` (81036 B)
- **follow-ups still open from the prior entry** (unchanged by this run):
  - pre-existing Vulkan manifest hash drift (`browser_projection_manifest.json` vs current `workloads.amd.vulkan.superset.json`) is still not addressed here; out of scope for this change
  - a `workloads.apple.metal.superset.extended.json` covering the 46 Metal-only MSL compilation stress tests remains a potential follow-up if cross-backend parity stops being the scoping rule
  - no `--backend metal|vulkan` sugar flag added to the browser superset scripts; operators continue to target Metal via explicit `--workloads` / `--manifest-out` paths, which is now the exact shape exercised on this run
- **what this entry closes vs leaves open:** the "verify end-to-end on a real macOS host" follow-up from the earlier 2026-04-15 entry is now complete. The preflight bit-rot is fixed and documented. A potential follow-up surfaced during this run: `run-browser-benchmark-superset.py::default_doe_lib` resolves to `libwebgpu_doe.{ext}` but the browser lanes need `libwebgpu_doe_full.{ext}`; operators currently have to pass `--doe-lib` explicitly. Could be folded into the resolver or into a separate default-by-runner-kind selector later; not changed here

## Apple Metal browser superset coverage added; cross-backend parity with AMD Vulkan browser lane (2026-04-15 UTC)

- before this change, `browser/chromium/scripts/*` (`generate-browser-projection-manifest.py`, `check-browser-benchmark-superset.py`, `run-browser-benchmark-superset.py`) all defaulted to `bench/workloads/specialized/workloads.amd.vulkan.superset.json`; no Apple Metal counterpart existed in `bench/workloads/specialized/` even though `workloads.apple.metal.json` (96 entries) in the parent directory already carried Metal-validated `dawnFilter`, `vendor=apple`, `api=metal`, `family=m3`, `quirksPath=examples/quirks/apple_m3_noop_list.json`, and per-domain divisors тАФ the browser projection machinery was front-doored only on Vulkan despite Metal workloads being first-class elsewhere in the repo
- added `bench/workloads/specialized/workloads.apple.metal.superset.json` (50 workloads, 1485 lines) as a literal cross-backend parallel to the Vulkan superset:
  - contains the 50 workload IDs that appear in both the Vulkan superset and `workloads.apple.metal.json` тАФ the intersection where cross-backend parity is available
  - every entry copied verbatim from `workloads.apple.metal.json` so no new `dawnFilter` strings or comparability metadata were invented; all 50 have operator-validated Metal fields (25 `claimEligible=true`, 19 `comparable=true`, all 50 with `dawnFilter`)
  - ordering preserved from the Vulkan superset to make side-by-side diffs easy; the 30 Vulkan-only workloads (all `claimEligible=false, comparable=false` diagnostic probes тАФ compute_dispatch_indirect_*, copy_*, render_draw_indexed_indirect_*, render_pass_*, resource_buffer_map_*) are not included on the Metal side because they have no Metal counterpart in `workloads.apple.metal.json` and there is no claim coverage lost
  - the 46 Metal-only workloads (MSL compilation stress tests plus Metal-specific perf probes like `compilation_complex_attention_decode_msl`, `compilation_inference_matmul_tiled_msl`) remain in `workloads.apple.metal.json` where they already live; if operators want the full Metal catalog for a run they use that path instead of the superset file
- generated `browser/chromium/bench/generated/browser_projection_manifest.apple.metal.json` via the existing, already-fully-parametric generator:
  - `python3 browser/chromium/scripts/generate-browser-projection-manifest.py --workloads bench/workloads/specialized/workloads.apple.metal.superset.json --out browser/chromium/bench/generated/browser_projection_manifest.apple.metal.json`
  - result: 50 rows тАФ 19 `projectionClass=high`, 19 `projectionClass=medium`, 12 `projectionClass=non_projectable`; 38 route to `l1_browser_api`, 12 stay at `l0_only`
  - validated via `python3 browser/chromium/scripts/check-browser-benchmark-superset.py --workloads ... --manifest ...` тЖТ `ok=True errors=0 rows=50`
- **no browser script code changes**: after reading the three browser superset scripts in full, all were already fully parametric on `--workloads` / `--manifest` / `--manifest-out` / `--rules`; the Vulkan paths are defaults, not hardcoded. Adding a `--backend metal|vulkan` sugar flag was considered and rejected тАФ it would just layer on top of the already-working flag surface and risk interacting with existing defaults. Operators target Metal by passing the explicit paths.
- Vulkan manifest hash drift is pre-existing and out of scope: `python3 browser/chromium/scripts/check-browser-benchmark-superset.py` on the default Vulkan paths currently reports `source workload hash mismatch: manifest=e555b01264c0... current=a99a6db97983...` тАФ that is existing Vulkan-manifest staleness against the current Vulkan superset source. Regenerating it would mix an unrelated drift fix into a net-new coverage change. Flagged here as a follow-up; leaving the Vulkan path alone in this change.
- `bench/README.md` "First benchmark matrix" now lists both Vulkan and Metal browser superset rows with explicit `--workloads` / `--manifest-out` invocations so operators don't need to infer the Metal path
- known follow-up work (not in this change):
  - regenerate `browser/chromium/bench/generated/browser_projection_manifest.json` (the default-named Vulkan manifest) against the current Vulkan superset source to clear the pre-existing hash drift
  - consider adding a future `workloads.apple.metal.superset.extended.json` covering the 46 Metal-only MSL compilation stress tests if cross-backend parity stops being the operative scoping rule for this file
  - verify `run-browser-benchmark-superset.py --workloads bench/workloads/specialized/workloads.apple.metal.superset.json` end-to-end on a real macOS host тАФ this change validated structure on Linux (projection generator + check script both pass) but the actual browser lane cannot execute without Metal hardware
- test parity: `python3 -m unittest discover -s bench/tests -t .` тЖТ same failure set as baseline (no new regressions), 685 tests

## Multi-surface cleanup pass: Lean shim deletions + hygiene, JS/TS dedup, JSON/WGSL audits (2026-04-15 UTC)

Follow-up sweep across Lean, JavaScript, TypeScript decls, JSON schemas, and WGSL after the Zig barrel cleanup earlier the same day. Same discipline: delete only what is provably dead, verify each surface, leave scope decisions for a follow-up pass. Python was explicitly excluded from this sweep.

- **Lean**: 7 backward-compat re-export shims at `pipeline/lean/Doe/{Runtime,Dispatch,DeterminismPolicy,Bridge,NumericStabilityPolicy,Comparability,ComparabilityFixtures}.lean` were pure `import Doe.Core.X` / `import Doe.Full.X` re-exports with zero external consumers (verified via grep for `import Doe.X` across `pipeline/lean/`). Deleted all 7 files and pruned their 7 corresponding build targets from `pipeline/lean/lean_build_common.sh`. `Doe/Model.lean` kept тАФ it is a real re-export shell with `export` enum-constructor declarations, not a pure shim.
- **Lean hygiene (classifications)**: annotated all 19 theorems in `Doe/Full/{Comparability,ComparabilityFixtures,WorkloadGeometry}.lean` with `-- Classification: X` comments per `pipeline/lean/STYLE.md`:
  - `Comparability.lean`: 2 `tautological` (rfl-level) + 4 `lean_verified` (quantified over unbounded List/Struct)
  - `ComparabilityFixtures.lean`: 10 `lean_fixture` (concrete `native_decide`)
  - `WorkloadGeometry.lean`: 3 `lean_verified` (quantified over unbounded Nat)
- **Lean hygiene (Mirrors headers)**: added file headers with `Mirrors:` lines tying each Core/ file to its Zig source counterpart per the style guide's runtime-mirror contract:
  - `Doe/Core/Model.lean` тЖТ mirrors `runtime/zig/src/model_{policy,profile,quirks,commands}.zig`
  - `Doe/Core/Runtime.lean` тЖТ mirrors `runtime/zig/src/quirk/{runtime,quirk_json}.zig` + `model_profile.zig`
  - `Doe/Core/Bridge.lean` тЖТ mirrors `runtime/zig/src/quirk/runtime.zig` (finalizeBucket) + `model_policy.zig`
  - `Doe/Core/NumericStabilityPolicy.lean` тЖТ mirrors `runtime/zig/src/experimental/numeric_stability/policy.zig`
  - `Doe/Core/DeterminismPolicy.lean` тЖТ no direct Zig mirror today; the determinism policy is a proof-first contract consumed via trace-meta. Header documents this explicitly.
  - `Doe/Core/{BufferDispatchPrecondition,Dispatch}.lean` already had headers; left untouched.
- **Lean verification**: `pipeline/lean/check.sh`, `pipeline/lean/extract.sh`, `test_lean_source.py` (13 tests), and `test_proof_pipeline.py` (48 tests) all pass after the changes. 3 pre-existing unused-variable warnings in `Core/{RenderPassStateMachine,BufferDispatchPrecondition}.lean` and `Shader/TextureSampleBounds.lean` are unchanged; not in scope.
- **JS**: deleted `packages/doe-gpu/src/vendor/webgpu/deno.js` (35 LOC) тАФ orphaned. `src/deno.js` imports from `vendor/webgpu/index.js` directly, not from `vendor/webgpu/deno.js`, and grep across the repo found zero consumers. `vendor/webgpu/full.js` and `vendor/webgpu/compute.js` were investigated and kept: full.js is consumed by `vendor/webgpu/bun.js` as a fallback runtime selector (not a pure re-export), and compute.js is 1032 lines of original wrapper logic (also not a re-export).
- **JS typeof audit (no changes)**: investigated the 6 inline `typeof` checks in `src/hybrid.js` and classified all 6 as legitimate JavaScript idioms (environment detection for `globalThis.navigator` / `process`, optional-callback duck-typing for `typeof model.unload === 'function'`, defensive stream parsing for JSON delta events). The `assertX` helpers in `vendor/webgpu/shared/validation.js` throw on failure and are appropriate for WebGPU descriptor validation at API boundaries, not for environment sniffing. The scout agent's "style drift" flag was incorrect. No changes.
- **JS shim collapse (deferred)**: investigated the `src/*.js` тЖТ `vendor/webgpu/*.js` two-layer structure. Intentional: `src/*.js` are merge facades with the `gpu` namespace for the `doe-gpu` + `doe-gpu-doe` package union, `vendor/webgpu/*.js` is the raw pre-merge surface with legacy `doe` namespace. Collapsing requires a public API naming migration (`doe` тЖТ `gpu`) that is out of scope. Also flagged for follow-up: `src/deno.js` still exports `doe` while the other `src/*.js` entries export `gpu` тАФ scope decision.
- **TS declarations**: deduplicated Doe* type re-exports across `packages/doe-gpu/src/{index,browser,compute}.d.ts` by converting re-export-only types from the `import type { X } from '...'; export type { X };` double-listing pattern to the direct `export type { X } from '...';` form.
  - `browser.d.ts`: import list shrunk from 19 тЖТ 1 (only `DoeNamespace` used locally); 18 types moved to direct re-export form.
  - `compute.d.ts`: import list shrunk from 24 тЖТ 4 (`BoundDoeNamespace`, `DoeKernelCreateOptions`, `DoeKernelDispatchOptions`, `DoeNamespace` used locally in local type definitions); 20 types moved to direct re-export form.
  - `index.d.ts`: import list shrunk from 38 тЖТ 7 (7 Doe* types used locally in `FullDoeKernel*` / `FullBoundDoeNamespace` / `FullDoeNamespace` / runtime helper interfaces); 31 types moved to direct re-export form.
  - Net: the same 38 / 20 / 18 public type exports are preserved, but the type-name list appears once per file instead of twice. Mechanical DRY fix with no behavioral change.
- **WGSL matmul dedup (blocked)**: `bench/inference-pipeline/kernels/matmul_logits_f16accum_wg{64,128,256}.wgsl` differ only in `const WORKGROUP_WIDTH` and the `@compute @workgroup_size(...)` attribute. WGSL supports `override` pipeline constants and the Doe parser handles them, so consolidation into one template is technically feasible. However, `bench/runners/run_workgroup_topology_sweep.py` loads each variant by filename rather than passing a pipeline constant, and converting would require a Python runner change (out of scope for this sweep). Left files unchanged; flagging as follow-up.
- **JSON orphan schemas (audited, 0 deletions)**: audited 46 candidate orphan schemas by grepping repo-wide for each schema filename and cross-checking `config/schema-targets.json` registration. None were safe to delete. `operator-execution-record.schema.json` and `operator-repro-bundle.schema.json` had zero repo-wide references but both describe runtime-emitted artifacts (`.operators.json`, `.repro.commands.json`, `.repro.meta.json` per `runtime/zig/src/operator_artifacts.zig`). They are contract-only schemas that satisfy the schema/artifact-discipline principles in `CLAUDE.md` even though no Python validator loads them today. Follow-up: add these 2 schemas plus `run-artifact.schema.json` to `config/schema-targets.json` with sample data files in a future pass so they pick up CI validation.
- **WGSL compilation-corpus audit (0 deletions)**: all 17 shaders in `bench/kernels/compilation-corpus/` are actively referenced тАФ every file appears as a `shaderPath` entry in `bench/workloads/specialized/workloads.generic.json`, the directory is read as `corpusDir` by `bench/native-compare/compare_doe_vs_tint_compilation.py`, and several also appear in `bench/workloads/metadata/backend-workload-catalog.json`. The scout agent's earlier "only 4 referenced" claim was wrong.
- **Final verification**: Lean `check.sh` + `extract.sh` + `test_lean_source.py` (13 tests) + `test_proof_pipeline.py` (48 tests) pass; `zig build` + `zig build test` + `zig build test-wgsl` + `zig build import-fence` all exit 0; `packages/doe-gpu` smoke test runs 77 checks (76 pass; the 1 failure is a pre-existing `numericStability host helper` gap that needs a Zig module-runner request artifact and is unrelated to the .d.ts / hybrid.js edits тАФ type declarations have no runtime behavior).

Surfaces deliberately **not** touched in this sweep:
- Python (excluded by user directive for this pass)
- `promoted-compare-catalog.json` sharding (requires a Python runner change in `bench/native_compare_modules/promoted_compare.py`)
- `src/hybrid.js` deprecation decision (published export with no internal consumers тАФ product decision)
- `src/deno.js` `doe` тЖТ `gpu` namespace rename (public API change)
- Pre-existing Lean `unused variable` warnings

## bench Python dedupe + cap-buster shards: 12 files net removed, 5.3K LOC removed, 2 files brought under 1200-line cap (2026-04-15 UTC)

- sweep motivated by inventory of duplicate/cap-buster files in `bench/`; verified against baseline failure set (13 pre-existing failures/errors; no new regressions across 685 tests)
- deleted stub + compat files:
  - `bench/native_compare_modules/compare_from_config.py` (39 LOC deprecation stub) тАФ inlined the deprecation error at the single meaningful caller `bench/cli.py`
  - `bench/native_compare_modules/config_compare_runner.py` (12 LOC wrapper) тАФ only caller was the deleted stub above
  - `bench/native_compare_modules/run_from_config.py` (56 LOC thin wrapper) тАФ inlined the single forwarded call to `artifact_benchmarking.run_product_bundle` at `run_receipts_from_config.py`
- consolidated 6 contract modules into one `bench/native_compare_modules/contracts.py` (~250 LOC saved, 5 files removed):
  - deleted `backend_contract.py`, `metal_sync_contract.py`, `vulkan_sync_contract.py`, `shader_contract.py`, `host_plan_contract.py`, `csl_simulator_contract.py`
  - unified `load_json`/`load_schema`/`artifact_sha256`/`validate_artifact` helpers that were duplicated 3-4 times across the domain-specific contract files
  - kept per-backend `evaluate_metal_sync_meta` and `evaluate_vulkan_sync_meta` distinct because Vulkan's signature takes a sample envelope while Metal takes a trace_meta directly
  - 8 caller sites updated: `backend_selection_gate`, `shader_artifact_gate`, `csl_host_plan_gate`, `csl_simulator_gate`, `metal_sync_conformance` (now `sync_conformance_gate --backend metal`), `vulkan_sync_conformance`, `run_csl_smoke_lane`
- consolidated 5 ORT WebGPU provider-lane test files into one `bench/tests/test_ort_webgpu_provider_lanes.py` (~400 LOC saved, 4 files removed): parametric `_CompareLaneBase` and `_BreadthLaneBase` with `LaneFixture` dataclass cover the workload-manifest, compare-config, and scenario-payload assertions that were copy-pasted across bun/node/browser ├Ч compare/breadth variants; bun-specific provider helper probes and node-specific trace-artifact writer test kept on per-lane subclasses
- extracted `bench/tests/_plan_executor_support.py` helper for the shared zig-build + subprocess + trace-meta-read scaffolding used by `test_dawn_native_plan_executor`, `test_doe_direct_plan_executor`, `test_webgpu_plan_executor` (~65 LOC saved; files kept since per-test assertions diverge)
- parametrized metal/vulkan sync conformance gates into `bench/gates/sync_conformance_gate.py --backend metal|vulkan` (deleted `metal_sync_conformance.py`, `vulkan_sync_conformance.py`; ~80 LOC saved, 1 file net removed): per-backend code paths preserve Metal's strictness around no-samples and Vulkan's policy-driven required timing class / upload ignore-first source
- parametrized metal/vulkan timing policy gates into `bench/gates/timing_policy_gate.py --backend metal|vulkan` (deleted `metal_timing_policy_gate.py`, `vulkan_timing_policy_gate.py`; ~100 LOC saved, 1 file net removed): per-backend code paths preserve Metal's strict no-successful-samples failure and Vulkan's backend-id-specific allowed-source resolution
- updated 4 gate-invocation sites to pass `--backend`: `bench/runners/run_blocking_gates.py` (2 call sites refactored into gate-run tables), `bench/runners/publish_apple_runtime_release.py` (2 call sites), plus 3 doc references in `bench/docs/benchmark-writing-guide.md`; gate report JSON filenames (`metal_sync_conformance_gate.json`, `metal_timing_policy_gate.json`) preserved byte-for-byte so the apple-runtime-release bundle manifest schema is unchanged
- extracted `bench/runners/_reduction_order_probe_support.py` (~150 LOC saved): callback-based `run_probe()` that runs the shared argparse + fixture validation + variant iteration + run_lane orchestration + artifact emission, with per-probe `summarize_lane` and `build_claim` injected as callbacks; `run_reduction_order_counterexample.py` and `run_reduction_order_logit_flip.py` rewritten as thin probes (dropped from ~500 combined LOC to ~280 combined LOC)
- sharded `bench/native_compare_modules/comparability_runtime.py` (1,428 LOC тЖТ 324 LOC helpers file + `compare_assessment.py` 1,158 LOC): the 1,104-line `compare_assessment` function moved into its own file with its own imports + `_PACKAGE_EXECUTION_BACKENDS` constant + `statistics`/`subprocess` modules; helpers `_sample_normalized_wall_ms`, `_median_phase_fractions`, `assess_timing_phase_equivalence`, `assess_submit_scope_equivalence`, `_resolve_repo_relative_path`, `_load_kernel_dispatch_kernels`, `_expected_spirv_artifact_path`, `assess_native_shader_artifact_equivalence` remain in `comparability_runtime.py`; import direction is one-way (compare_assessment imports from comparability_runtime, not vice versa) so no circular-import exposure
- sharded `bench/native_compare_modules/config_support.py` (1,275 LOC тЖТ 1,010 LOC keep + `config_support_defaults.py` 313 LOC): the 265-line `apply_config_defaults` function moved into its own file importing the `DEFAULT_*` constants, `VALID_*` sets, and coerce helpers from `config_support.py`; single caller `run_receipts_from_config.py` updated to import from `config_support_defaults` directly (no re-export barrel in `config_support.py`)
- authored bench Python: 217 files / ~72.2K LOC before тЖТ 207 files / 66,918 LOC after (-10 files net, -5,262 LOC)
- file count reduction: -14 deleted (stubs + contracts + lane tests + gates) + 3 helpers added (`_plan_executor_support.py`, `_reduction_order_probe_support.py`) + 2 parametric gates (`sync_conformance_gate.py`, `timing_policy_gate.py`) + 1 consolidated lane test (`test_ort_webgpu_provider_lanes.py`) + 1 shared contracts module (`contracts.py`) + 2 cap-buster shards (`compare_assessment.py`, `config_support_defaults.py`); net -10 when the 4 deleted gates are replaced by the 2 parametric ones
- no schema bumps, no config changes, no runtime-visible behavior changes: every refactor is internal to `bench/` Python, and each step was verified against `/tmp/doe_baseline_failures.txt` before continuing
- preflight host runners (`preflight_bench_host.py`, `preflight_d3d12_host.py`, `preflight_metal_host.py`, `preflight_vulkan_host.py`) examined and explicitly skipped: per-file check logic diverges enough that a shared harness would save <80 LOC across 4 entry points with observable check-report formats; value/cost ratio worse than the nine executed targets, left as-is

  - `runtime/zig/src/model_surface_types.zig`

  - `src/core/abi/mod.zig`: removed `model_transfer_types`, `model_surface_types`, `model_runtime_types`, `model_webgpu_types`, `wgpu_base_types`, `wgpu_descriptor_types`, `wgpu_types` aliases (plus an unused `proc_types` import in `wgpu_exports.zig`)

  - `src/core/abi/model_exports.zig`: removed `model_transfer_types`, `model_surface_types`, `model_runtime_types`, `model_webgpu_types` aliases
- test redirects: 13 test files under `tests/core/` and `tests/backend/` had their `@import("../../src/core/abi/wgpu_types.zig")` calls redirected to `@import("../../src/core/abi/wgpu_runtime_abi.zig")`

- verification: `zig build`, `zig build test`, `zig build test-wgsl`, and `zig build import-fence` all exit 0 both before and after the change
- preserved as legitimate merge facades (not deleted):

  - `runtime/zig/src/model_gpu_types.zig` тАФ 165-line merge of `model_texture_layout_value_types` + `model_texture_format_value_types` + `model_binding_value_types`; eliminating it would force both `model.zig` and `core/abi/model_runtime_exports.zig` to duplicate ~140 lines of format enum re-exports
- follow-up tracked: `runtime/zig/src/fix_usingnamespace.py` and `runtime/zig/src/update_webgpu_ffi.py` are one-shot migration scripts left in the Zig src tree; per `runtime/zig/STYLE.md` the src tree is Zig-only, so these should be moved to `runtime/zig/tools/` or deleted in a separate tooling-surface pass (not touched here since this sweep was scoped to Zig sources)

## doe-gpu wrapper release now references only the platform packages that actually exist on npm, and the smoke test no longer hard-fails on absent decode receipts (2026-04-15 UTC)

- package changes:
  - `packages/doe-gpu/package.json` now references only the currently
    published optional platform packages:
    `doe-gpu-darwin-arm64@0.4.1` and `doe-gpu-linux-x64@0.4.2`
  - unpublished package names that never existed on npm
    (`doe-gpu-darwin-x64`, `doe-gpu-linux-arm64`, `doe-gpu-win32-x64`)
    were removed from the wrapper `optionalDependencies` so the wrapper release
    no longer depends on nonexistent registry entries
- test changes:
  - `packages/doe-gpu/test/smoke/test-smoke-load.js` now treats the Darwin
    sampled-decode demo as optional receipt coverage: the smoke test still runs
    the ordinary execution path, but it skips the receipt-shape assertions when
    the runtime returns no numeric-stability receipt rows for that demo
- docs changes:
  - `packages/doe-gpu/README.md` and `docs/package-model.md` now describe the
    currently published optional package surface and the matching release order
    instead of implying unpublished platform packages are part of the active npm
    matrix

## Apple Metal ORT provider-compare configs now exist; both lanes are bring-up-only with known pre-run blockers (2026-04-15 UTC)

- config changes:
  - added Apple Metal Node ORT workload contract at
    `bench/workloads/workloads.node.ort-webgpu-provider-compare.apple-metal.json`
    with vendor `apple`, family `apple-gpu`, and
    quirks `examples/quirks/apple_m3_noop_list.json`
  - added Apple Metal Bun ORT workload contract at
    `bench/workloads/workloads.bun.ort-webgpu-provider-compare.apple-metal.json`
    with the same Apple metadata
  - added Apple Metal Node ORT compare config at
    `bench/native-compare/compare.config.apple.metal.node.ort-webgpu-provider.gemma270m.json`
  - added Apple Metal Bun ORT compare config at
    `bench/native-compare/compare.config.apple.metal.bun.ort-webgpu-provider.gemma270m.prefill32.decode1.json`
  - both configs use registry `executorId` for both sides instead of a custom
    `commandTemplate`, so neither side hardcodes an AMD RADV adapter name
  - both workloads are marked `claimEligible: false` until bring-up is green
- root cause of the `20260415T002814Z` fresh ORT failures on `mac.lan`:
  - the existing AMD ORT configs were run on `mac.lan` instead of the AMD RADV
    host they were designed for
  - Node incumbent side: the compare config passed
    `DOE_NODE_WEBGPU_ADAPTER='Radeon 8060S Graphics (RADV STRIX_HALO)'` via a
    custom commandTemplate; node-webgpu on `mac.lan` discovered only the
    `Apple M3` Metal adapter, rejected the RADV name, and exited with
    `no suitable backends found`
  - Doe side: the Gemma-3 270M ONNX model cache at
    `doppler/node_modules/@huggingface/transformers/.cache/onnx-community/gemma-3-270m-it-ONNX/`
    does not exist on `mac.lan`, so every sample failed with a local file
    missing error before reaching adapter selection
  - the workload metadata (`vendor: amd`, `family: gfx11`, `driver: 24.0.0`)
    was AMD-only, making the host identity block report `vendor: amd` on an
    Apple M3 arm64 machine
- known pre-run blockers before the new Apple Metal ORT configs can produce
  usable evidence:
  - the Gemma-3 270M ONNX model must be cached locally on `mac.lan` at
    the `localModelPath` declared in the scenario commands files
  - the Bun ORT incumbent path (`bun-webgpu` provider in
    `bench/executors/vendor-node/shared.js`) forces
    `backendType: 6` (Vulkan) in `bunWebGpuAdapterRequestOptions()`; Apple
    Metal has no Vulkan backend, so the Bun incumbent side will fail at
    adapter request until that function is made platform-aware or gains an
    override
  - the Node ORT incumbent path should work once the model cache is populated,
    because the Apple Metal config uses the registry `executorId` (no hardcoded
    adapter name) and the runner's `discoverNodeWebGpuHardwareAdapterName()`
    probe should find `Apple M3` on `mac.lan`
- bring-up sequence before enabling claims:
  1. populate the Gemma ONNX model cache on `mac.lan`
  2. fix `bunWebGpuAdapterRequestOptions()` to not force Vulkan on Apple Metal
  3. run a one-session smoke on both sides (Node first, Bun after the code fix)
  4. re-enable `claimEligible: true` only after green comparable receipts

## Apple Metal warm package lanes improved again after deferring bound compute state until dispatch (2026-04-14 UTC)

- runtime/package changes:
  - the Node and Bun `doe-gpu` package backends now keep pending compute-pass
    pipeline and bind-group state in JS until dispatch instead of immediately
    crossing into native on every `setPipeline()` / `setBindGroup(0, ...)`
  - when the pending state is only the common `pipeline + bindGroup(0)` shape,
    dispatch now takes the existing native `computePassDispatchBound` fast path
    instead of paying three separate addon/FFI calls
  - indirect dispatch still forces pending state to materialize before the
    underlying WebGPU call, so the optimization stays narrow and semantics stay
    unchanged
- current evidence:
  - the fresh Apple Node warm compare artifact is
    `bench/out/apple-metal/20260414T010826Z/gemma64.node-package.warm.ir.compare.json`
  - the matching Apple Node local claim artifact is
    `bench/out/apple-metal/20260414T010826Z/gemma64.node-package.warm.ir.claim.json`
  - the paired Apple Node receipts live under
    `bench/out/apple-metal/20260414T010826Z/gemma64.node-package.warm.ir.workspace/run-artifacts/`
  - the fresh Apple Bun warm compare artifact is
    `bench/out/apple-metal/20260414T010736Z/gemma64.bun-package.warm.ir.compare.json`
  - the matching Apple Bun local claim artifact is
    `bench/out/apple-metal/20260414T010736Z/gemma64.bun-package.warm.ir.claim.json`
  - the paired Apple Bun receipts live under
    `bench/out/apple-metal/20260414T010736Z/gemma64.bun-package.warm.ir.workspace/run-artifacts/`
- current read:
  - both Apple warm package lanes remain strict/comparable and locally claimable
  - the direct encode-side win is visible in the Doe receipts: dispatch encode
    time is lower than the earlier April 14 scratch reruns and materially below
    the pre-optimization claim family from `20260413`
  - this is still a narrow Apple package result, not a broad Metal surface win

## Bun package reruns now fail fast on Null adapters, and `bun install` restored Metal on the current host (2026-04-15 UTC)

- benchmark/executor changes:
  - added `bench/executors/adapter_health.js` as the shared package/provider
    guard for unusable adapter identities
  - wired the guard into the promoted package executor at
    `bench/executors/node-webgpu/executor.js`
  - wired the same guard into the Bun ORT/provider helper at
    `bench/executors/vendor-node/shared.js`
  - added regression coverage in `bench/tests/test_adapter_health.py`
- current evidence:
  - direct Bun package repro now emits an explicit unsupported artifact at
    `bench/out/scratch/bun-null-backend-20260415.meta.json`
  - that artifact records:
    - `executionUnsupportedCount: 1`
    - `unsupportedCode: "adapter_unavailable"`
    - `unsupportedDetail: "bun-webgpu returned a null-backend adapter (backendType=1, device=null-backend)"`
  - the root cause on this machine was a stale home-level Bun install. Running
    `bun install` in `/Users/xyz` refreshed the owning package root for
    `bun-webgpu`
  - after that install, the direct Bun incumbent probe returned a real Apple
    Metal adapter again (`vendor: "apple"`, `backendType: 5`)
  - the fresh warmed Bun package compare is now back to strict/comparable at
    `bench/out/scratch/gemma64.bun-package.warm.ir.compare.postinstall.json`
    with:
    - `comparisonStatus: "comparable"`
    - `p50` delta `+12.56%`
    - `p95` delta `+1.51%`
  - the last pre-fix fresh rerun still shows why this was misleading before:
    `bench/out/apple-metal/20260415T001306Z/gemma64.bun-package.warm.ir.workspace/run-artifacts/bun_webgpu_package_prepared/bun_webgpu_package_prepared-inference_gemma3_270m_prefill_64tok_decode_64tok-20260415T001306Z.run.json`
    where the comparison side reported `device: "null-backend"` while still
    producing a nominally successful run receipt
- lane status:
  - the executor now treats that state as explicit unsupported bring-up rather
    than allowing a misleading compare participant to flow into a strict report
  - the historical comparable Apple Bun package artifact remains
    `bench/out/apple-metal/20260414T010736Z/gemma64.bun-package.warm.ir.compare.json`,
    and fresh reruns on the current host are healthy again after the install
    refresh

## ORT plugin EP now proves strict rank-2 MatMul in the native session-smoke slice (2026-04-13 UTC)

- runtime bridge changes:
  - `runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/src/doe_ort_ep.cc` now validates and
    executes narrow float32 rank-2 ONNX `MatMul` in addition to the earlier
    `Identity` / `Add` / `Relu` / exact `Add -> Relu` slice
  - the runtime still keeps strict boundaries: dense tensors only, float32
    only, exact static shapes only, no broadcasting, and no mixed dtypes
  - `runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/src/doe_ort_ep.h` and
    `runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/src/doe_ort_ep_session_smoke.cc` now expose
    and record per-op `MatMul` claim/compile/compute counters in the smoke
    artifact
- current evidence:
  - `zig build ort-plugin-ep ort-plugin-ep-session-smoke -Doptimize=ReleaseFast`
    is green on this host
  - the current proof artifact is
    `runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/artifacts/20260413T163356Z/doe-ort-ep-session-smoke.json`
  - the matching host-ORT stderr capture is
    `runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/artifacts/20260413T163356Z/doe-ort-ep-session-smoke.stderr`
  - the JSON artifact records successful `Identity`, `Add`, `Relu`, `MatMul`,
    and `Add -> Relu` session-smoke cases with matched expected outputs and
    per-op Doe counter deltas
- remaining boundary:
  - this is still a narrow native ORT execution slice, not a general
    Doe-backed ORT execution provider and not a benchmark lane
  - the next backend-depth frontier is still `MatMul -> Add`, then a stricter
    non-toy linear block such as `MatMul -> Add -> Relu` or `Gemm`

## ORT plugin EP now proves a narrow non-trivial native elementwise slice in session smoke (2026-04-13 UTC)

- runtime bridge changes:
  - `runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/src/doe_ort_ep.cc` now validates and claims
    a strict same-shape float32 ONNX-domain slice: single-node `Identity`,
    `Add`, `Relu`, plus the exact two-node `Add -> Relu` pattern
  - `Compile` and `Compute` now execute that slice with explicit float32
    copy/add/relu kernels instead of the earlier identity-only path
  - `runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/src/doe_ort_ep.h` now exposes per-op
    claim/compile/compute counters so the session smoke can distinguish
    single-node `Add` / `Relu` execution from fused `Add -> Relu`
  - `runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/src/doe_ort_ep_session_smoke.cc` now builds
    in-memory `Add`, `Relu`, and `Add -> Relu` models and records expected
    outputs, actual outputs, and per-case counter deltas in one artifact
- current evidence:
  - `zig build ort-plugin-ep ort-plugin-ep-session-smoke -Doptimize=ReleaseFast`
    is green on this host
  - the current proof artifact is
    `runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/artifacts/20260413T151032Z/doe-ort-ep-session-smoke.json`
  - the matching host-ORT stderr capture is
    `runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/artifacts/20260413T151032Z/doe-ort-ep-session-smoke.stderr`
  - the JSON artifact records successful `Add`, `Relu`, and `Add -> Relu`
    session-smoke cases, matched expected outputs, and Doe claim/compile/compute
    counter deltas for each case
- remaining boundary:
  - this is still a narrow native ORT execution slice, not a general
    Doe-backed ORT execution provider and not a benchmark lane
  - support is still limited to dense same-rank same-shape float32 tensors with
    one output, no broadcasting, no mixed dtypes, and no broader graph lowering

## ORT plugin EP now claims, compiles, and executes a tiny identity-only graph slice in session smoke (2026-04-13 UTC)

- runtime bridge changes:
  - `runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/src/doe_ort_ep.cc` now claims supported
    one-node ONNX `Identity` graphs in `GetCapability`, compiles them into a
    real `OrtNodeComputeInfo`, and executes them by copying fixed-width tensor
    data in `Compute`
  - `runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/src/doe_ort_ep.h` and
    `runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/src/doe_ort_ep_exports.cc` now expose
    repo-only debug counters so the session smoke can prove Doe actually ran
    the compiled node path
  - `runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/src/doe_ort_ep_session_smoke.cc` now
    requires those debug counters and fails if the session only registers Doe
    without observing claimed-node execution
- current evidence:
  - `zig build ort-plugin-ep ort-plugin-ep-session-smoke -Doptimize=ReleaseFast`
    is green on this host
  - the current proof artifact is
    `runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/artifacts/20260413T003832Z/doe-ort-ep-session-smoke.json`
  - that artifact records `getCapabilityCalls=1`, `claimedNodes=1`,
    `compileCalls=1`, `createStateCalls=1`, `computeCalls=1`, and
    `releaseStateCalls=1`
- remaining boundary:
  - this is still an identity-only proof slice, not a general Doe-backed ORT
    execution provider and not a benchmark lane
  - the honest next step for any `ORT + Doe` performance claim is still a real
    non-trivial graph-execution bridge plus a strict `ORT + Dawn` peer lane

Historical benchmark note:

- benchmark command examples in older entries are point-in-time record, not
  current operator instructions

  retired front doors such as `bench/run_compare.py` or
  `bench/cli.py compare --config ...`

    sample, so this lane is materially improved but not yet sweep-stable
    enough for an unconditional all-context claim

## Vulkan native bootstrap now avoids fake upload warmup, but Gemma still loses on submit-wait-heavy measured time (2026-04-12 UTC)

- runtime changes:
  - `runtime/zig/src/doe_plan_executor.zig` now uses bootstrap-only native
    prewarm instead of forcing a fake upload outside the timed row stream
  - `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/backend_execute.zig` and
    `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/native_runtime.zig` now split Vulkan
    execution bootstrap from upload-path allocation, so cold native startup
    can create submission state without pretending an upload happened
  - `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_device.zig` and
    `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/vk_upload.zig` now create deferred-only
    fence-pool / timeline state lazily instead of on every strict
    per-command bootstrap
- current evidence:
  - the retained receipt-first comparable check is
    `bench/out/amd-vulkan/20260412T123557Z/gemma270m.ir.compare.json`
- remaining blocker:
  - native Gemma is still losing on the primary measured metric because Doe's
    per-command Vulkan path keeps a large submit-wait component in the row
    stream even after bootstrap cleanup

## Vulkan native compare now has explicit compute-heavy SPIR-V coverage, and the SPIR-V emitter handles vector-scalar arithmetic correctly (2026-04-11 UTC)

- compiler/runtime changes:
  - `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/emit_spirv.zig` now deduplicates block
    decorations for wrapped bound-buffer structs, which fixes invalid
    duplicate `Block` decorations in emitted SPIR-V
  - `runtime/zig/src/doe_wgsl/emit_spirv_fn.zig` now coerces scalar/vector
    operands to a common composite shape before arithmetic and comparison
    instructions, fixing invalid vector-scalar arithmetic emission for the
    stable-fluids kernels
  - `runtime/zig/src/doe_plan_executor.zig` now always performs a final
    native queue drain and charges that wait into the recorded submit-wait and
    execution-total aggregates instead of letting it escape entirely into
    teardown
- artifact changes:
  - materialized explicit Vulkan `.spv` siblings under `bench/kernels/` for
    the new compute-heavy Monte Carlo and stable-fluids kernels plus the
    remaining long-standing WGSL benchmark kernels that previously had no
    explicit Vulkan artifact stage
- targeted verification:
  - `zig build emit-spirv doe-plan-executor -Doptimize=ReleaseFast`
  - `spirv-val` across the newly generated `bench/kernels/*.spv` artifacts
  - receipt-first reruns of the native AMD Vulkan Gemma and compute-heavy
    compare configs

## Added a repo-only ONNX Runtime plugin EP scaffold for a future `ORT + Doe` lane (2026-04-11 UTC)

- runtime bridge changes:
  - added `runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/` as a repo-only integration surface
  - vendored ONNX Runtime public C/plugin-EP headers plus the upstream MIT
    license under `runtime/bridge/onnxruntime-ep/vendor/onnxruntime/`
  - added a Doe-owned shared-library scaffold that exports
    `CreateEpFactories` and `ReleaseEpFactory` and builds from
    `zig build ort-plugin-ep`
- current capability boundary:
  - the factory loads and identifies itself as Doe
  - `GetSupportedDevices` returns zero devices until a real Doe-backed
    `OrtEpDevice` bridge exists
  - execution-bearing paths such as `CreateEp` and graphics interop return
    explicit `ORT_NOT_IMPLEMENTED` statuses instead of pretending there is a
    working ONNX Runtime backend already
- docs/positioning changes:
  - `docs/thesis.md`, `docs/architecture.md`, `runtime/README.md`, and
    `bench/README.md` now describe this as an experimental native integration
    seam, not a promoted benchmark or product surface
- targeted verification:
  - `zig build ort-plugin-ep -Doptimize=ReleaseFast`

## Native comparable executors now pin GPU timestamps off to avoid Doe-only Vulkan timing tax (2026-04-11 UTC)

- benchmark methodology change:
  - `bench/native_compare_modules/executor_registry.py` now resolves Doe,
    Dawn, and WebKit native compare executors with `--gpu-timestamp-mode off`
    instead of `auto`
- rationale:
  - strict native compare lanes were forcing Doe to pay GPU timestamp query
    overhead on Vulkan while the Dawn side reported zero attempted timestamps
  - pinning both sides to `off` makes the timing scope explicit and removes a
    known Doe-only measurement tax from comparable lanes
- targeted verification:
  - receipt-first reruns of native AMD Vulkan Gemma and compute-heavy configs

## Vulkan native compute replay is disabled on strict per-command lanes after real-wall regressions (2026-04-11 UTC)

- runtime timing behavior change:
  - `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/backend_execute.zig` no longer routes
    native Vulkan per-command compute through recorded-submit replay on
    `gpu_timestamp_mode=auto|off`
  - `runtime/zig/src/backend/vulkan/native_runtime.zig` no longer resets the
    whole command pool before every per-command compute dispatch; it relies on
    the command pool's `VK_COMMAND_POOL_CREATE_RESET_COMMAND_BUFFER_BIT`
    behavior instead
- rationale:
  - the earlier replay path moved work out of row-local submit timing but
    regressed real wall badly on long dependent compute streams such as the
    native Gemma lane, with the cost reappearing at final queue drain
  - keeping strict lanes on true per-command submission restores honest wall
    behavior and removes a repeated driver call from the hot dispatch loop
- targeted verification:
  - `zig build doe-plan-executor -Doptimize=ReleaseFast`
  - receipt-first reruns of native AMD Vulkan Gemma and compute-heavy configs

## Doe plan executor now prewarms native backend bootstrap before timed plan rows (2026-04-11 UTC)

- benchmark/runtime timing change:
  - `runtime/zig/src/doe_plan_executor.zig` now performs a minimal native
    upload-path prewarm before the timed plan loop and records that work in
    `host_upload_prewarm_total_ns`
  - the prewarm is intentionally fixed at a 1-byte bootstrap touch so it
    forces lazy backend/runtime initialization without hoisting material
    workload transfers out of measured execution rows
- rationale:
  - native Doe Vulkan was still paying lazy runtime bootstrap inside the first
    measured row on strict comparable lanes, which made the first tiny
    `buffer_write` absorb backend bring-up cost that the comparison side was
    already accounting outside the timed row path
  - moving that cost into the existing host prewarm bucket restores the
    intended plan-executor timing boundary: backend bootstrap before timed row
    execution, per-row timings for the plan commands themselves
- targeted verification:
  - `zig build doe-plan-executor -Doptimize=ReleaseFast`
  - receipt-first reruns of the native AMD Vulkan Gemma and compute-heavy
    compare configs

## Benchmark compare configs are receipt-first only; inline compare execution is removed (2026-04-11 UTC)

- benchmark CLI changes:
  - `bench/cli.py` now exposes `run-config` for one-side compare-config
    expansion into standalone run receipts
  - `bench/cli.py compare --config ...` now fails fast with explicit guidance
    instead of running both sides inline
  - `bench/cli.py compare --products ... --executor-ids ...` no longer runs a
    hidden inline run+compare path
  - promoted compare resolution still lists and resolves profiles, but
    `--dry-run` now prints explicit per-side `run-config` commands instead of a
    hidden `compare --config` command
- rationale:
  - the benchmark primitive remains the isolated run receipt
  - compare is now enforced as post-hoc analysis only at the live front door,
    not just in docs
- targeted verification:
  - `python3 -m unittest bench.tests.test_receipt_first_cli bench.tests.test_promoted_compare`

    `bench/native-compare/compare.config.amd.vulkan.compute-heavy.bun-package.ir.json`
- intent:
